b'By Marc Stein'
b'U.S.A. Basketball plans to gauge the interest of the Duke University sensation Zion Williamson in joining the Americans\xe2\x80\x99 12-man squad for the FIBA World Cup in China this summer, according to a person familiar with U.S.A. Basketball\xe2\x80\x99s intentions.'
b'No discussions have taken place with Williamson, whose freshman season at Duke ended Sunday with a 68-67 quarterfinal loss against Michigan State in the N.C.A.A. tournament.'
b'Formal talks with Williams, the presumptive No. 1 overall N.B.A. draft pick, would most likely not take place until Williams had officially declared his intention to turn professional and chosen an agent licensed by the N.B.A. to represent him, said the person, who was not authorized to speak publicly.'
b'But the precedent for such an invitation was set by the current U.S.A. Basketball hierarchy in 2012, when Anthony Davis \xe2\x80\x94 fresh off being drafted No. 1 overall out of Kentucky by the New Orleans Pelicans \xe2\x80\x94 earned a roster spot with Team USA at the London Olympics under Duke Coach Mike Krzyzewski.'
b'The 2019 World Cup, which runs Aug. 31 to Sept. 15 in China, will be the first major competition for the United States since Krzyzewski was succeeded as coach by Gregg Popovich of the San Antonio Spurs. Williamson is widely regarded as the rare sort of talent, like Davis before him, who would not be out of place with the N.B.A. All-Stars expected to fill out Popovich\xe2\x80\x99s roster \xe2\x80\x94 no matter who is coaching.'
b'The Athletic reported Monday that the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 LeBron James, a three-time Olympian, would not make himself available for the World Cup team this summer but that he had not ruled out playing for Team USA at the Tokyo Olympics in 2020.'
b'There was some hope in international basketball circles that James would consider playing in the World Cup since the Lakers had missed the playoffs and James would sit out the N.B.A. postseason for the first time since 2004-05.'
b'Jerry Colangelo, the chairman of U.S.A. Basketball, declined to discuss James or Williamson specifically when he was reached on Monday, saying only that roster invitations \xe2\x80\x9cwill be addressed at the appropriate time.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'The real hoops drama is in Europe.'
b'By Zach Messitte'
b'Mr. Messitte is writing a book about Americans playing basketball in Italy.'
b'MILAN \xe2\x80\x94 As the National Basketball Association plods its way to the 68th annual All-Star Game in Charlotte, N.C., on Sunday, American hoops fans should take note of how the Italians generate hardwood drama in February.'
b'Since Thursday, the eight best teams in Italy\xe2\x80\x99s Lega Basket Serie A from the first half of the season have been competing for the Coppa Italia, a no-holds-barred, single elimination tournament whose outcome actually matters to fans, players, team owners and corporate sponsors. And while a champion will be crowned at the end of the playoffs later this spring, bragging rights for holding the Coppa\xe2\x80\x99s trophy aloft on Sunday provides a midseason shot of adrenaline.'
b'The N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s 82-game regular season, which began in October and will end in April, is a slog. Anyone who has watched a Wednesday night non-marquee matchup in November can attest to that. The action rarely begins before the fourth quarter; coaches rest their superstars.'
b'The first half of the Italian season, by contrast, is an exciting sprint from the opening tipoff. The 16-team league has a 30-game regular season in which each club plays each other twice \xe2\x80\x94 once at each other\xe2\x80\x99s home court. If you play in Venice in week one, Venice\xe2\x80\x99s team comes to your arena in week 16. And there\xe2\x80\x99s drama: Turin, seeded fifth in last year\xe2\x80\x99s Coppa, won the trophy, even though they placed 11th at the end of the season.'
b'There\xe2\x80\x99s an intensity to the Italian regular season that too often is missing from the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s long fall and winter games. Not only are there fewer games, but also they are shorter and quicker (10- as opposed to 12-minute quarters and with fewer play stoppages mandated by television). And even if the quality of play in Italy is inferior, the interest in the February Coppa Italia far outstrips whether Team LeBron will prevail over Team Giannis at the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s All-Star Game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhether it is game six or 26, you are always playing for something,\xe2\x80\x9d said Travis Diener, an American who also holds Italian citizenship and plays on this year\xe2\x80\x99s fourth-seeded team from Cremona. \xe2\x80\x9cThen you get the Coppa and anything can happen.\xe2\x80\x9d Diener, who spent several years in the N.B.A., won the M.V.P. award of the Coppa Italia when he was playing for Sassari in Sardinia in 2014.'
b'The Coppa allows teams from smaller markets (and smaller budgets) like Sassari and Cremona (more famous for Stradivarius violins than hoops) to pull off March Madness-like upsets against more glamorous squads like Milan, which is sponsored by Giorgio Armani and takes full advantage of the lack of a league salary cap.'
b'In last year\xe2\x80\x99s Coppa, Milan was one of three top seeds that lost in the first round, much to the delight of fans from smaller-market teams like Cant\xc3\xb9, which plays in the Milanese suburb of Desio. As one team official told me, it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t hurt that coaches have built-in salary incentives if their team does well at the midseason tournament \xe2\x80\x94 and sponsors, of course, love the positive brand attention of a winning squad.'
b'The quarterfinal round began on Thursday and Friday, featuring a doubleheader each day: Milan-Bologna and Cremona-Varese on day one, and Venice-Sassari and Avellino-Brindisi on day two. American fans should try to imagine a similar midseason weekend tournament: What if the Bucks, Warriors, Raptors, Nuggets, Celtics, Pacers, Thunder and 76ers were playing in Charlotte this weekend for bragging rights to an American Basketball Cup? It would be a fresh take on a tired All-Star Game whose television ratings have declined by more than 50 percent since the Michael Jordan-dominated 1990s.'
b'The Italian basketball league used to have its own all-star game, but there wasn\xe2\x80\x99t enough sustained interest from players or fans, so it ended in 2016. A dunk contest was similarly discontinued. Giorgio Gandolfi, a former basketball journalist who now runs his own international sports agency and who has been to 13 N.B.A. All-Star Games, said that winning the Coppa Italia is second in prestige only to winning the league championship at the end of the season. He doesn\xe2\x80\x99t miss Italy\xe2\x80\x99s all-star games. \xe2\x80\x9cThey were just kind of boring,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'While there is too much money to be made for the N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 and team owners \xe2\x80\x94 to consider shortening the season from the grueling 82-game march to the playoffs, the idea of borrowing from the Italians to make each tipoff count more should be enticing.'
b'Take the case of the New York Knicks, who currently hold the worst record in the N.B.A. There is nothing much left for the Knicks to play for or their fans to watch this season.'
b'By contrast, Italian basketball teams near the bottom of the league run the risk of relegation to the second division, which is a bad result for everyone. That\xe2\x80\x99s why the fight near the end of the season can be just as fierce at the bottom as it is as the top.'
b'If the Knicks had to worry about being consigned to the minor leagues, the folks at Madison Square Garden might think differently about how to handle the final months of the season. If the Knicks were demoted to play against the Maine Red Claws, New York fans would probably have some choice words and creative hand gestures for their team\xe2\x80\x99s poor management. Italian basketball fans would have some advice on how to do that better, too.'
b'Zach Messitte, the president of Ripon College in Wisconsin, is on sabbatical as an associate fellow at the Johns Hopkins School of Advanced International Studies in Bologna. '

b'Follow The New York Times Opinion section on Facebook, Twitter (@NYTopinion) and Instagram.'

b'By Reuters'
b'Although noting "regrets" that LSU men\'s basketball coach Will Wade didn\'t comply with the school several weeks ago when asked about recruiting issues, athletic director Joe Alleva announced in a statement Sunday that Wade\'s month-plus suspension has been lifted.'
b"The university suspended Wade on March 8 because it said he refused to meet with school officials amid scrutiny of a reported FBI wiretap capturing the coach talking about an offer to then-recruit Javonte Smart. Wade missed the Tigers' final regular-season game and all of their SEC and NCAA Tournament games."
b'Assistant coach Tony Benford took over as head coach and led LSU to the SEC regular-season title with a win over Vanderbilt in his first game, then led the Tigers to the Sweet 16, where they lost to Michigan State.'
b'Wade was reinstated after he met with Alleva and NCAA compliance officials on Friday, Alleva said in the statement, adding that he saw no place where Wade violated his contract, allowing for his reinstatement.'
b'"During those meetings, he answered all questions and denied any wrongdoing in connection with recently reported allegations of irregularities in college basketball recruiting," Alleva said.'
b'The statement also said the university "regrets that Coach Wade did not choose to fulfill his obligations to LSU when he was first asked to do so. However, the seriousness of the allegations and Coach Wade\'s prior refusal to refute them could not be ignored without exposing the University and basketball program to great risk. Protecting LSU and preserving our integrity must always be our first priority. Coach Wade\'s explanations and clarifications offered during the meeting, absent actual evidence of misconduct, satisfy his contractual obligation to LSU."'
b"The alleged offer to Smart arose in a conversation Wade was having with Christian Dawkins, described as a middleman in the scandal of paying basketball recruits. Dawkins was convicted on felony charges of wire fraud last year and sentenced last month to six months in prison. The specifics of that case were unrelated to Dawkins' reported interaction with Wade."
b'ESPN and Yahoo Sports reported last month that a wiretap caught Wade upset about not landing Smart at that point despite a "strong-ass offer." CBS Sports described Smart as a top-50 recruit from Baton Rouge. He ultimately signed with the Tigers.'
b'"I was thinking last night on this Smart thing," Wade reportedly said to Dawkins on the wiretap. "I\'ll be honest with you, I\'m (expletive) tired of dealing with the thing. Like I\'m just (expletive) sick of dealing with the (expletive). Like, this should not be that (expletive) complicated."'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'As the crowd filed out of the Barclays Center in May 2015, there was reason for hope. Though the Nets had just been eliminated by the Atlanta Hawks in the first round of the playoffs, they had overachieved and shown some promise for the future. And Phil Jackson had become the Knicks president the year before, bringing his triangle offense and a coaching r\xc3\xa9sum\xc3\xa9 that included 11 N.B.A. titles to Manhattan.'
b'Little did New York fans know that it would be four dreadful years before playoff basketball would return to the city. It finally will on Thursday night, when the Nets host the Philadelphia 76ers in a series tied at one all.'
b'While there has been no playoff basketball in the city in the interim, much has happened in those four years. And for Knicks and Nets fans, not much of it has been good.'
b'May 1, 2015 The eighth-seeded Nets fall to the top-seeded Hawks, 111-87. But they take two games in the series, raising optimism. \xe2\x80\x9cWe were able to secure a playoff spot,\xe2\x80\x9d Coach Lionel Hollins says. \xe2\x80\x9cSome people will say, \xe2\x80\x98Hey, we didn\xe2\x80\x99t deserve it.\xe2\x80\x99 That\xe2\x80\x99s their problem.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'June 25 After putting up a 17-65 record, the worst in franchise history and the league\xe2\x80\x99s second worst in 2015, the Knicks have bad luck in the draft lottery, ending up at the No. 4 spot. Nevertheless, their selection, Kristaps Porzingis of Latvia, will pay off, quickly becoming a star and a fan favorite.'
b'Oct. 3 Knicks Coach Derek Fisher gets into a physical altercation after being confronted by Matt Barnes of the Memphis Grizzlies at the home of Barnes\xe2\x80\x99s estranged wife. Barnes is suspended for two games.'
b'Dec. 30 Cleanthony Early of the Knicks is shot in the knee by masked men and robbed of gold teeth caps after a visit to a strip club.'
b'Jan. 10, 2016 The Nets fire Coach Hollins and demote General Manager Billy King with the team at 10-27. \xe2\x80\x9cFrankly speaking, I deserve a championship now much more than six years ago,\xe2\x80\x9d  owner Mikhail D. Prokhorov says.'
b'Feb. 8 The Knicks, 23-31, fire Fisher. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s not a whole lot to say,\xe2\x80\x9d Jackson says in his first remarks to reporters since the start of training camp.'
b'April 13 The Nets finish the season 21-61, the league\xe2\x80\x99s third worst record. But there will be little help on draft day: They traded their top pick to the Celtics in 2014 for a 37-year-old Kevin Garnett and a 36-year-old Paul Pierce, both of whom are gone at this point.'
b'The Knicks finish 32-50. That\xe2\x80\x99s a 15-game improvement, but Jackson says, \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re disappointed about our season.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'April 17 The Nets hire Kenny Atkinson, a Hawks assistant, as head coach. \xe2\x80\x9cTogether, we can do great things,\xe2\x80\x9d Prokhorov says.'
b'June 2 The Knicks hire Jeff Hornacek as coach, bypassing the interim coach, Kurt Rambis.'
b'June 22 The Knicks trade for Derrick Rose, who proclaims them a \xe2\x80\x9csuperteam.\xe2\x80\x9d After a year he will leave for the Cleveland Cavaliers.'
b'July 7 The Nets sign Jeremy Lin, perhaps hoping to recapture the Linsanity that took over the Knicks in 2012.'
b'July 8 The Knicks sign Joakim Noah for four years and $72 million. This will not work out. Noah will be suspended for 20 games for a drug violation, be sent to the developmental league and get into a shouting match with Hornacek. The Knicks wind up releasing him in 2018 and paying him anyway.'
b'Feb. 8, 2017 The Knicks legend Charles Oakley is ejected from Madison Square Garden during a game. The crowd sides with the former player, chanting \xe2\x80\x9cOakley, Oakley.\xe2\x80\x9d The Knicks say he behaved abusively, and the owner, James L. Dolan, says that Oakley \xe2\x80\x9cmay have a problem with alcohol.\xe2\x80\x9d Oakley sues, claiming defamation and battery.'
b'March 12 Carmelo Anthony gets his 10,000th point as a Knick, becoming the third player to reach that mark with two teams.'
b'April 12 The Nets finish 20-62, the worst record in the league. Once again a potentially high draft pick is gone, as part of the Garnett deal. The Knicks are 31-51.'
b'June 22 The Nets trade their longtime star Brook Lopez to the Los Angeles Lakers for D\xe2\x80\x99Angelo Russell and Timofey Mozgov. Russell will become a key player in the team\xe2\x80\x99s resurgence.'
b'June 28 The Knicks and Phil Jackson agree to part ways after three years. The Knicks never fully embraced his triangle offense, and Jackson remained wary of the 3-point shot as it became increasingly important in the league. He also could never seem to get rid of Anthony, the team\xe2\x80\x99s aging star who refused to waive a no-trade clause. Jackson also feuded with the player expected to be the team\xe2\x80\x99s future, Porzingis.'
b'Sept. 25 A trade is finally worked out for Anthony, who is sent to the Oklahoma City Thunder for Enes Kanter. He gave the Knicks seven seasons of 20-points-a-game play. Jackson was willing \xe2\x80\x9cto trade me for a bag of chips,\xe2\x80\x9d Anthony says. He also notes that under new management, \xe2\x80\x9cThey went from asking for peanuts to asking for steak.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Oct. 18 Lin ruptures a knee tendon  in the Nets\xe2\x80\x99 opening game and misses the entire season.'
b'Feb. 6, 2018 Porzingis tears the anterior cruciate ligament in his left knee and is out for the rest of this season and the next one.'
b'April 11 The Nets finish 28-54. Incredibly, for a third straight year they do not have their top pick because of that Garnett deal. (Garnett is by now 41 and has been out of the league two years.) The lost picks turned into Jaylen Brown, a big part of the contending Celtics; Markelle Fultz, a No. 1 overall choice; and Collin Sexton, who averaged 17 points as a rookie with the Cleveland Cavaliers.'
b'The Knicks wind up 29-53 and fire Hornacek the next day. David Fizdale will be the new coach.'
b'Asked how the Knicks can improve, the superfan Spike Lee can only turn to prayer: \xe2\x80\x9cOn bended knee I pray above to da basketball gods to deliver us back to da glory years of da Orange and Blue. Amen,\xe2\x80\x9d he writes in The New York Times.'
b'June 20 The Nets make a trade to get Dwight Howard from the Hornets, but Howard buys his way out of his contract and never plays for them.'
b'July 13 The Nets trade Lin to the Hawks, curing the city\xe2\x80\x99s second, significantly milder case of Linsanity.'
b'Jan. 31, 2019 The Knicks  send their most popular player, Porzingis, who is still recovering from the torn A.C.L., to the Dallas Mavericks in a blockbuster trade. Two months later it will be revealed that he is under investigation by the New York Police Department after being accused of sexual assault.'
b'The Knicks get Dennis Smith Jr. and some expiring contracts, which should open up salary cap space so they can sign some marquee free agents. Assuming that marquee free agents would want to play for the Knicks.'
b'March 12 Knicks fans hoping for a change in ownership are disappointed when Dolan proclaims that he will not sell the team, even for $6 billion. Two days before that, he was filmed threatening a fan with banishment from the Garden after the fan had urged him to sell the team.'
b'April 10 The Knicks have sunk to the bottom of the league again, finishing 17-65 and tying the franchise-worst mark. The Nets start the season 8-18, but then unexpectedly turn things around behind Russell, Spencer Dinwiddie (picked up from the developmental league in 2016) and Jarrett Allen (a No. 22 pick in 2017). They finish 42-40. Playoff basketball returns to New York. For now.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the Knicks\xe2\x80\x99 record in the 2014-15 season. They were 17-65, not 17-63.'

b'NEW YORK \xe2\x80\x94 Megan Gustafson of Iowa has won the Honda Sports Award as the top woman in college basketball.'
b"Gustafson led Division I women's basketball with an average of 28 points this season. She owns Iowa records for most career points (2,804) and rebounds (1,460)."
b"The 6-foot-3 center from Port Wing, Wisconsin, had 33 double-doubles in her senior season, tying an NCAA record. She led the Hawkeyes to the school's first Elite Eight in 26 years and earned AP Player of the Year honors."
b'The other finalists were Asia Durr (Louisville), Sabrina Ionescu (Oregon) and Teaira McCowan (Mississippi State).'

b'Supported by'
b'On Pro Basketball'
b'By Scott Cacciola'
b'OAKLAND, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 The Golden State Warriors run a practice drill that Coach Steve Kerr did not intend as a tribute, even if he named it after someone who taught him a great deal. He calls it the \xe2\x80\x9cLute Olson drill,\xe2\x80\x9d and it is a blur of activity: a 3-on-2 exercise that Kerr uses to get his players up and down the court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a good way to get a little running and rhythm and shooting,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'The Warriors, who are pretty good at those things, have elevated basketball into modern art in recent seasons. But Kerr, as he helps define basketball\xe2\x80\x99s present, cannot help but dip into his past. He learned that drill in 1983, when he was a freshman guard at the University of Arizona playing for Olson, who was in the early stages of building a college powerhouse. Kerr, ever the student, was already absorbing as much as he could.'
b'Olson, 84, retired as the men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach at Arizona in 2008, but his influence resonates. Not so much, oddly enough, at the college level, where, of late, Arizona has had its well-publicized struggles along with the rest of the Pac-12 Conference. Instead, Olson\xe2\x80\x99s impact exists largely in the N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 and with the Warriors, in particular.'
b'Bruce Fraser, one of Kerr\xe2\x80\x99s longtime assistants, played for Olson in the 1980s before working under him as a graduate assistant. And Andre Iguodala, the veteran Warriors forward, played at Arizona from 2002 to 2004, when he sought to emulate an older teammate named Luke Walton.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll the fundamentals,\xe2\x80\x9d Iguodala said. \xe2\x80\x9cThings like footwork, body positioning and just being a smart player.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Walton, who now has the thankless task of coaching the Los Angeles Lakers, is still considered a member of the Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 extended family after serving as one of Kerr\xe2\x80\x99s assistants for two seasons. Before Walton joined the Warriors in 2014, Kerr did not know him well. But Olson recommended him, and that was more than enough.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you came out of Arizona during that era, you knew how to play the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Fraser said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd that was mostly because of Lute.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Olson, who has had health issues in recent years, emphasized basketball basics. Each practice began with a series of chest passes. Players worked on their weak hands. The Warriors, who warm up by launching half-court heaves, are slightly less regimented.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf Coach Olson walked in and saw some of this, he\xe2\x80\x99d be shaking his head,\xe2\x80\x9d Fraser said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99d think we\xe2\x80\x99re so loose.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Warriors are still mindful of the essentials, though, especially at training camp, where they dribble around traffic cones and throw passes at pitch-back nets configured with targets. If they channel the Harlem Globetrotters, their flamboyance is rooted in bedrock principles.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I think you could tie a lot of that back to Coach Olson and Arizona,\xe2\x80\x9d Fraser said.'
b'Kerr played for several legendary N.B.A. coaches \xe2\x80\x94 Phil Jackson, Gregg Popovich, Lenny Wilkens, Cotton Fitzsimmons \xe2\x80\x94 and he took pieces from each as he developed his own style. Jerry Marvin, his former coach at Palisades High School in Los Angeles, made a big impression, too. But these were coaches with unique approaches.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think the common thread is their force of personality,\xe2\x80\x9d Kerr said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey all saw the game a little differently and ran different stuff, basing a lot of it on their personnel. But it\xe2\x80\x99s not what made them great coaches. It was having great talent, and then developing a great culture and system so that their talent could flourish.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Olson, for example, adapted to the strengths of his roster. He became more guard-oriented over the years, especially after he recruited high-profile players like Damon Stoudamire, Khalid Reeves and Gilbert Arenas. (Kerr noted how he had been one of the \xe2\x80\x9cslow guys in the backcourt\xe2\x80\x9d when Olson was just starting out at Arizona.)'
b'But Olson was not necessarily trying to outwit anyone by being especially innovative. Basketball, Kerr said, is not like football, where a mastermind like Bill Belichick can lean on his tactical genius to mold the New England Patriots into the most dominant N.F.L. team of his era.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFootball is so strategic,\xe2\x80\x9d Kerr said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut in basketball, there aren\xe2\x80\x99t many guys I can think of historically who are the best coaches on earth who were just offensive wizards or defensive wizards. It was more about the culture they built and the way their teams played together \xe2\x80\x94 not a style or a system.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It has become a hackneyed concept in sports, as if teams can just crack the code on demand, but Olson was all about culture, his former players say. Jason Terry, a retired N.B.A. guard who played at Arizona from 1995 to 1999, recalled his recruitment. He was not a shy young man, but Olson, at that point firmly established as one of the game\xe2\x80\x99s top coaches, had the sort of gravitas that intimidated him.'
b'On the second day of Terry\xe2\x80\x99s official visit to Arizona, Olson and his wife, Bobbi, had him over for pancakes.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThese unbelievable pancakes,\xe2\x80\x9d Terry, an analyst for Turner Sports, said in a telephone interview. \xe2\x80\x9cThat was a big part of the recruitment. But I also remember that he kind of came over and put his big paw on my shoulder, and I jumped. He was like, \xe2\x80\x98Nothing to be scared of young fella. It\xe2\x80\x99s great to have you in my home.\xe2\x80\x99 And from that point on, you were just at ease.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Olson, Terry said, was the first coach he had who never used profanity. Olson would glare. His face would go red. And those big paws would shake.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBut he would never yell,\xe2\x80\x9d Terry said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe would just say your name over and over and over.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Above all, Olson imbued his players with the sense that they were a part of something larger than themselves. Before the national championship game in 1997, two prominent alumni \xe2\x80\x94 Kerr and Sean Elliott, both of whom had graduated to the N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 boarded the team bus. Olson had invited them to address his players, and their message was simple: Do it for all of us who have come before you but could never quite get the job done.'
b'Terry saw that Olson had tears in his eyes. Arizona went on to win its first national title by defeating Kentucky in overtime.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe knew that we couldn\xe2\x80\x99t let him down,\xe2\x80\x9d Terry said.'
b'With the Warriors, Kerr definitely swears on occasion. (Ask Draymond Green.) And the N.B.A. is not college basketball. But Kerr still tries to foster an atmosphere that is more about the collective whole than about its supremely talented parts. Kerr loathes isolation sets. He celebrates ball movement. And he stages team dinners on road trips, where family members are welcome.'
b'As for the Pac-12, these are rough days. Arizona, under Coach Sean Miller, has been entwined in a corruption scandal, and the conference could send just one team to the N.C.A.A. tournament. Iguodala described the Pac-12 as garbage (he used a more colorful word), though he expressed hope moving forward. Kerr was more diplomatic.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a dry spell,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I really don\xe2\x80\x99t know the answer.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In fact, the Pac-12 has not won a national championship since Kerr boarded the Arizona team bus back in 1997 and delivered his pregame pep talk. But in his own way, as the Warriors chase another title, he is still carrying the mantle for the conference and his old coach.'

b'Supported by'
b'By Marc Stein and Sopan Deb'
b'It is one of the oldest warnings in sports: Great athletes, they say, don\xe2\x80\x99t often become great coaches.'
b'In the case of Magic Johnson, the legendary former Los Angeles Lakers point guard, that maxim must be amended. For Johnson, neither the front office nor the bench proved to be a winning or even comfortable habitat like the hardwood he used as a launching pad to basketball immortality.'
b'Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s forgettable coaching career with the Lakers lasted just 16 games at the close of the 1993-94 season before he unhappily vowed never to return to that occupation. Then this week, Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s two-year reign as the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 president of basketball operations ended even more ignominiously.'
b'He abruptly announced his resignation before the team\xe2\x80\x99s final game of an enormously disappointing season, then revealed that he had told the news media of the decision before he had informed his boss, Jeanie Buss, in order to deny Buss an opportunity to talk him out of it.'
b'Johnson, of course, has stunned the world before, with his announcement and early retirement in 1991 because he was found to be H.I.V. positive, followed by his brief return to basketball in 1996. He spent the ensuing two decades constructing a business and entertainment empire replete with a highly successful chain of movie theaters and an ownership stake in the storied Los Angeles Dodgers. But Johnson always insisted that he was, first and foremost, a Laker.'
b'Handling his exit in such a haphazard manner has earned Johnson untold amounts of criticism in the days since, given how much the Lakers mean to Southern Californians and how unexpected this news was. Yet he seems prepared to take the hits in exchange for the opportunity to return to his more customary post-playing life \xe2\x80\x9con the other side,\xe2\x80\x9d as he described it \xe2\x80\x94 forever a Laker but officially unattached to any team.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI like to be free,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said.'
b'But his freedom comes at a steep cost \xe2\x80\x94 to Johnson, to the Lakers, to a Hollywood belief in, well, magic.'
b'It turns out Magic Johnson, who piloted some of the greatest teams in N.B.A. history, will not be the savior who helps the Lakers escape their longest run of futility.'
b'After last summer\xe2\x80\x99s blockbuster signing of LeBron James, Johnson proclaimed the Lakers to be \xe2\x80\x9cback\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 with the promise of a return to full \xe2\x80\x9cback back\xe2\x80\x9d status this summer once they acquired at least one superstar sidekick to James. Johnson has instead fled just when the most crucial work was about to commence, with no clear path to bringing that second star to a flailing franchise that last reached the playoffs in 2013 and last won a championship in 2010.'
b'When he convened an impromptu news conference Tuesday night, rather than reveal his updated plan to restore the Lakers to title contention and placate a frustrated fan base, Johnson did just the opposite. Describing himself as \xe2\x80\x9chappier when I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t the president,\xe2\x80\x9d he explained that the conditions and pressures attached to building a championship team around James meant that the real Magic \xe2\x80\x9ccouldn\xe2\x80\x99t come out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In a series of rambling interviews with a number of news outlets while the Lakers were in the process of losing their regular-season finale to the Portland Trail Blazers, Johnson spoke of how he had longed to send a congratulatory tweet to Oklahoma City\xe2\x80\x99s Russell Westbrook or to tutor Ben Simmons, the rising Philadelphia 76ers star, without inciting a storm of tampering allegations.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew if I stayed in the role,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m giving up a lot of me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Such disclosures, of course, only served to validate much of the skepticism that greeted Buss\xe2\x80\x99s decision to install Johnson as the new face of the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 basketball operations in February 2017.'
b'Rival front-office executives questioned Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s lack of experience in the modern game and his willingness to embrace the all-encompassing nature of the job from the moment he was named to replace the much-maligned Jim Buss (Jeanie\xe2\x80\x99s brother) and Mitch Kupchak, the longtime Lakers executive. Those questions only rose in volume when Buss named as Magic\xe2\x80\x99s sidekick another front-office neophyte, Rob Pelinka, Kobe Bryant\xe2\x80\x99s polarizing former agent.'
b'There were red flags from the start. In taking on his first active role with an N.B.A. team since his second retirement as a player in 1996, Johnson admitted that he had much to learn about navigating the ins and outs of the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s complex salary cap and the rhythms of a job that had evolved so much in his time away.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe main part for me is really learning the other part that I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know, and that is to understand the C.B.A., the salary cap, where we are in terms of the salary cap and who\xe2\x80\x99s a free-agent-to-be,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson told USA Today of the challenges he faced in building a roster and understanding the collective bargaining agreement.'
b'Part of the issue might have been that Johnson could never just be a basketball executive. He is a mogul and a cultural force. While other N.B.A. teams primarily lean on decision makers focusing solely on basketball, Johnson seemed to always have his eye on something bigger than the game itself \xe2\x80\x94 reaching with his business tentacles to as many corners as possible.'
b'Johnson acquired a 4.5 percent share of the Lakers in 1994 before selling his stake in 2010. He even once hosted a syndicated late-night talk show, 1998\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cThe Magic Hour.\xe2\x80\x9d And he was never just about one game either, acquiring a minority stake in the Dodgers in 2012 and one in the Los Angeles Football Club of Major League Soccer in 2014.'
b'Business had clearly been on Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s mind when he took the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 front-office job in 2017. He told \xe2\x80\x9cCBS This Morning\xe2\x80\x9d in an interview at the time that he had turned down other offers to run a franchise, including the embattled Knicks, but that he felt it was the right time to rejoin the Lakers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAt this point in my life, you know, I think that I can do it right now because my businesses are running smooth,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said. \xe2\x80\x9cI can turn them over to my executive team that I have.\xe2\x80\x9d In that same interview, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI always wanted to be the male Oprah.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson was one of the first athletes to build an empire for himself outside professional sports. He went from whipping behind-the-back passes and being the engine that made the 1980s Showtime Lakers rev to investing in more than 100 Starbucks and Burger King locations, among many other business investments, all while flashing his famed charismatic grin. According to a Basketball Reference estimate, Johnson made about $23 million from N.B.A. salary alone, not including endorsements. Now his net worth is in the hundreds of millions.'
b'The business of reviving the Lakers, however, proved beyond him. Buss, as a result, is already facing pressure to rebound from her nostalgic faith in Johnson to pursue a more accomplished executive this time \xe2\x80\x94 such as Golden State\xe2\x80\x99s Bob Myers or San Antonio\xe2\x80\x99s R. That\xe2\x80\x99s not fun for me. That\xe2\x80\x99s not who I am.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There had never been a player like Johnson before he was drafted out of Michigan State as the first pick in the 1979 N.B.A. draft. That figure matches the Knicks for the league\xe2\x80\x99s third-longest active drought behind Sacramento (13 seasons) and Phoenix (nine).'

b'The coach, Gary Franklin Sr., started his club from scratch in Los Angeles and ran a program known for its rectitude, according to Sonny Vaccaro, the former Nike and Adidas executive who essentially forged the relationship between the shoe industry and the summer youth basketball circuit. What began as a team for Franklin to coach his then 10-year-old son became a powerhouse club that attracted future N.B.A. stars and major college recruits, and one that steered clear of any scandals.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe was one of the guys who built it up through his own resources, and his program had a reputation as one of the \xe2\x80\x98good guys,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Vaccaro said of Franklin in an interview this week.'
b'Franklin\xe2\x80\x99s club, California Supreme, and others like it are major participants in a system involving youth basketball, shoe companies and colleges that supplies the professional game with a deep reservoir of talent. And Michael Avenatti knew it.'
b'Now Franklin has become a central figure in the case against Avenatti, the lawyer best known for representing Stormy Daniels, the adult film star, in her lawsuit against President Trump. Whether Franklin, who has not been charged, is an accomplice, a co-conspirator or simply collateral damage is not yet clear, but prosecutors\xe2\x80\x99 revelations about his involvement have stunned those who have known him for years.'
b'The question in the club basketball world is, could Franklin have morphed from a stickler who played by the rules into the latest symbol of an amateur basketball world that has spun out of control?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cCal Supreme was always the best team for doing things by the book, because there were a lot of other teams that didn\xe2\x80\x99t do it by the book,\xe2\x80\x9d said Andy Brown, a former forward for Cal Supreme who went on to play at Stanford. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd Cal Supreme did it by the book.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'For Franklin, a soft-spoken coach from Los Angeles, the run was a triumph. His Nike-sponsored team was one of the best in the country in what is now known as grass-roots basketball.'
b'Three years later, Franklin, 51, is in a different spotlight, with federal prosecutors accusing Avenatti of extortion for threatening Nike with the release of information that Avenatti had pledged would damage the company\xe2\x80\x99s stock-market value to the tune of a few billion dollars. Specifically, Avenatti had told Nike lawyers this month that a coach in Nike\xe2\x80\x99s grass-roots basketball league had approached him with information that company employees had paid the families of three players, prosecutors said. Avenatti, prosecutors said, demanded that Nike pay millions to make the whole thing go away.'
b'Paying players and their families would violate N.C.A.A. rules, rendering the players ineligible for college play. Also, if the money was paid in exchange for players to commit to colleges Nike sponsors, it would resemble the behavior that recently led to federal fraud convictions for two former Adidas employees.'
b'Two people familiar with the investigation confirmed that the unidentified coach in the complaint is Franklin. Nike had recently declined to renew its sponsorship deal with Cal Supreme, which was worth more than $70,000 annually. Franklin could not be reached for comment.'
b'Grass-roots basketball is often erroneously called A.A.U. basketball, even in prosecutors\xe2\x80\x99 court filings. That is a misnomer because the elite leagues are not sponsored by the Amateur Athletic Union. Rather, they are supported by sneaker companies that spend hundreds of thousands of dollars every year to organize tournaments from April through July. The teenage players who participate are outfitted, from head to toe, in apparel made by and bearing the logo of the league\xe2\x80\x99s sponsor.'
b'Sneaker companies like Nike and Adidas also pay thousands of dollars each year to sponsor the teams themselves as a sort of long-term investment strategy: They hope to build brand loyalty among young players who could eventually become stars. Get players into your gear early, the thinking goes, and you may be more likely to land them as spokesmen when they turn pro and have even more influence over the world\xe2\x80\x99s fans \xe2\x80\x94 and their wallets.'

Basketball.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s their objective. And if you have a kid who\xe2\x80\x99s good enough to go on to the N.B.A., and he chooses to continue wearing these shoes, you\xe2\x80\x99ve made a long-term investment that could pay off for years.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'A rookie selected in this month\xe2\x80\x99s W.N.B.A. draft will make $41,265 to $53,537 in base salary, and nobody in the league will earn a base salary of as much as $120,000 this coming season.'
b'Because of that, many of the 144 players in the W.N.B.A. maximize their earning window by heading to Europe and Asia, where independent owners, free of salary caps, can offer them lucrative opportunities.'
b'There is a price to pay, however: endless seasons bleeding into one another; a physical, psychological and emotional toll; and, the players say, a heightened risk of injury.'

b'That focus is particularly important right now, after the players\xe2\x80\x99 association opted out of its collective bargaining agreement with the league late last year. So the injury to Stewart, while reflecting a longstanding reality, has also shed new light on the way these players earn a living.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFirst and foremost, our thoughts are with Breanna and we wish her a speedy recovery,\xe2\x80\x9d Mark Tatum, the acting W.N.B.A. president and N.B.A. deputy commissioner, said in an email. \xe2\x80\x9cThe W.N.B.A. and its teams and players share a commitment to growing the league\xe2\x80\x99s business and building on our ongoing work to provide greater professional opportunities for players in the off-season.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The league has good reason to want a pathway to limiting, if not ending, overseas play from players: The teams are consistently affected by the toll it takes on its players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe year-round play for W.N.B.A. players is a detriment to the W.N.B.A. product,\xe2\x80\x9d Minnesota Lynx Coach Cheryl Reeve said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe physical and mental toll it takes on the league\xe2\x80\x99s elite players is reflected in some of the league\xe2\x80\x99s best sitting out the W.N.B.A. season to \xe2\x80\x98rest,\xe2\x80\x99 as well as these players sustaining injuries.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Reeve said the rest, which cuts into the W.N.B.A. season, is critical for elite players who \xe2\x80\x9care asked to perform at their highest levels day in and day out at home and abroad.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt isn\xe2\x80\x99t possible to sustain an elite level without these breaks,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'The new way forward can take many forms, with changes in the base salary merely one of the tools available. Toliver, for instance, is coaching in the N.B.A. this season, but, because of restrictive rules in place from the previous C.B.A., is making just $10,000 to do so. A comprehensive pathway to getting W.N.B.A. players more opportunities on N.B.A. coaching staffs and in front offices during the W.N.B.A. off-season could significantly change the calculation for players by itself.'
b'Jackson spoke optimistically about how that process was going, though even the work to keep her own side informed requires time-zone gymnastics with her leadership scattered all over the world.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe could have a meeting at 10 a.m. or at 10 p.m., Eastern time, just because we have folks in, or we\xe2\x80\x99ve had folks in, Russia and Poland and China, Turkey,\xe2\x80\x9d Jackson said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd so my executive committee just says get it done, so that\xe2\x80\x99s what we do.\xe2\x80\x9d She recalled an executive committee member, Nneka Ogwumike, jumping on a call from China at midnight.'
b'The two sides have until the conclusion of the 2019 season to come to an agreement.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe league has also signaled its willingness, its desire, to have a really collaborative relationship with the players, and to hear and to understand the concerns, and how to make this better,\xe2\x80\x9d Jackson said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is good forward movement. I think that\xe2\x80\x99s where we are.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That comes as welcome news to players like A\xe2\x80\x99ja Wilson, who has followed Stewart\xe2\x80\x99s path in many ways. Stewart was the top overall pick in 2016; Wilson in 2018. Like Stewart, Wilson won an N.C.A.A. championship, then was the W.N.B.A. rookie of the year. And like Stewart, Wilson went straight from college ball to the W.N.B.A. to a stint overseas last year, in China, before an injury ended her season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s definitely not an easy route at all,\xe2\x80\x9d Wilson said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think that\xe2\x80\x99s what makes us just that elite as professional athletes. b'Wilson, too, expressed hope that Stewart\xe2\x80\x99s injury would \xe2\x80\x9cshine a light\xe2\x80\x9d on this scheduling issue. If her team sweeps, she said, she will finish her season on May 2, then fly home to Sweden to see her family on May 3, before reporting to New York for training camp with the Liberty by May 8. On May 9, she will be at Barclays Center for New York\xe2\x80\x99s first preseason game, against the Chinese national team.'
b'She said she was looking forward to playing in the best women\xe2\x80\x99s professional league in the world. But as she attends to her aching ankle, she also echoed her fellow players on just how much better the league, and the professional experience, could be with some rest.'

b"NEW YORK \xe2\x80\x94 After a meandering search, St. John's finally settled on Mike Anderson as its new basketball coach."

b"Once he was let go, it didn't take long for Anderson to land another job. Terms of the contract were not disclosed."
b'"I\'ve been dreaming about this moment for the last nine days," St. John\'s athletic director Mike Cragg said during a news conference at Madison Square Garden. "And I found the right guy. We are going to win championships."'
b'The 59-year-old Anderson takes over for former St. John\'s star Chris Mullin, who resigned on April 9, citing a "recent personal loss." His older brother, Roddy, died last month at 58 after battling cancer for years.'

b'In a radio interview Wednesday on WFAN, wealthy alum Mike Repole was critical of President Conrado "Bobby" Gempesaw, Vice President Joe Oliva, and the school\'s board of trustees.'
b'Ultimately, the Red Storm decided on Anderson, who is 369-200 in 17 seasons as a Division I head coach. He has never had a losing record.'
b"Neither Oliva nor Cragg would comment specifically on Repole's criticism, but both defended the process the school went through before picking Anderson."
b'"I would say nine days is a pretty thorough and efficient search," said Cragg, who came to St. John\'s from Duke last fall.'
b'Anderson, a native of Birmingham, Alabama, spent the first part of his career working for Nolan Richardson. Anderson played for Richardson at Tulsa before becoming an assistant under him with the Golden Hurricane.'
b'When Richardson left for Arkansas, Anderson joined him in Fayetteville. He was an assistant coach at Arkansas for 17 years, helping the Razorbacks win the 1995 national championship.'
b'Known for coaching up-tempo teams that press on defense, Anderson said his goal is to implement an exciting style of basketball that is "really entertaining." He said his teams would be "one of the top assist teams in the country."'

b'"You don\'t know what we\'re going to do," he explained. "Our pressure may come from the half court. It may come full court. It may come from a zone. Now you\'ve got to worry about what we\'re doing. I don\'t worry about what teams do. I worry more about what we\'re doing."'
b"Anderson spoke briefly with St. John's players Mustapha Heron and L.J. Figueroa, who attended the news conference."

b"Anderson, who doesn't have previous New York ties, said his plan is to recruit in the area."
b'"I had somebody ask me, \'Who\'s the guy who\'s going to recruit for you?\' My staff\'s going to recruit. That\'s who\'s going to recruit. Have three guys that are going to be recruiting and you\'re going to see me out there as well," Anderson said.'
b'"I think it comes down to building those relationships," he added. "I know that they\'re going to see me. They\'re going to get a chance to know me."'

b'Ahead of two major shows, the painter Jonas Wood reflects on his early career \xe2\x80\x94 and the most unusual object in his studio.'
b'By Janelle Zara'
b'Jonas Wood\xe2\x80\x99s East Hollywood studio \xe2\x80\x94 a refurbished industrial space hidden behind a razor-wired metal gate \xe2\x80\x94 is populated with the familiar objects that appear in his paintings. There are colonies of potted plants and basketball paraphernalia that ranges in size from plush couch cushions to man-sized orbs. Every room is filled with art, most notably by the ceramist Shio Kusaka, Wood\xe2\x80\x99s studio mate and wife, and Kiki and Momo, their son and daughter. '
b'But the studio is where Wood culls various photographs from the internet or his own archive and uses them as source material for his paintings \xe2\x80\x94 they are printed out and pinned onto walls, then flattened and distilled into blocks of color. Wood then layers these dense graphic patterns, overlapping fields of stipples and stripes, circles, squares, dots and wood grains.'
b'[Coming later this spring: the T List newsletter, a weekly roundup of what T Magazine editors are noticing and coveting. Sign up here.]'
b'Thirteen years into his career, following a year and a half of preparation, Wood is finally wrapping up preparations for the two biggest shows he\xe2\x80\x99s ever done: an exhibition of new work at Gagosian in New York, opening in late April, and a survey at the Dallas Museum of Art, opening this week \xe2\x80\x94 his first major solo museum exhibition. Admittedly, the prospect of facing works \xe2\x80\x94 landscapes, interiors and portraits of family and friends \xe2\x80\x94 from his early career was giving Wood \xe2\x80\x9ca hard time sleeping.\xe2\x80\x9d He wondered, \xe2\x80\x9cAre the old paintings horrible?\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cDid I used to be a better painter and now I\xe2\x80\x99m worse?\xe2\x80\x9d During the installation of the show at the museum last week, he had two big realizations: \xe2\x80\x9cI wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a hack, which is a big relief,\xe2\x80\x9d and that now, after more than a decade of steadily producing gallery shows, he might be ready to slow down.'
b'Nursing a can of tangerine-flavored LaCroix, Wood answered T\xe2\x80\x99s Artist\xe2\x80\x99s Questionnaire, which unearthed memories of the early days of his career, the first painting he ever sold \xe2\x80\x94 and the YouTube videos that nearly brought him to tears.'
b'What is your day like? How much do you sleep, and what\xe2\x80\x99s your work schedule like?'
b'I drop the kids off at school, eat some breakfast, start working a little bit, usually have a meeting, have lunch and work for a couple hours in the afternoon. Maybe I\xe2\x80\x99ll work for a couple hours at night. I\xe2\x80\x99m trying to sleep more. In general, in the last couple of years, I\xe2\x80\x99ve been trying to balance sleeping, eating, working, working out and spending time with the family. I\xe2\x80\x99ve had my head down trying to make it as an artist since 2006, and I\xe2\x80\x99ve had one or two shows a year for 12 years in a row. It\xe2\x80\x99s not that I want to paint less, per se, but I want to take a step back.'
b'I\xe2\x80\x99m talking about taking a step back and looking at what I\xe2\x80\x99ve done, and taking a step back from the pace that I was running and changing gears. After these two exhibitions, I don\xe2\x80\x99t have any booked shows coming up. It\xe2\x80\x99s a big opportunity for me to rearrange the way I spend my time. I love to paint and I want to paint, but I don\xe2\x80\x99t have to paint right now, this second, and I don\xe2\x80\x99t have to paint all next week and miss four school events.'
b'How many hours of creative work do you think you do in a day?'
b'Every day, I\xe2\x80\x99m super into it. I need to paint. If I go away for a couple weeks, I\xe2\x80\x99ll just draw. It\xe2\x80\x99s like a must for my mental health. I would have to say that I\xe2\x80\x99ve been all-in on painting since I was younger, and I realized that it was because of a lot of fear that it would all go away. That\xe2\x80\x99s not how I want to paint in the future. The pressure and psychology of that setup isn\xe2\x80\x99t totally right. I would like to build bodies of work outside the calendar schedule of art fairs and shows for a little while. I love painting, and I think I can paint without having a giant carrot in front of me. I don\xe2\x80\x99t think that I\xe2\x80\x99m the best at painting, and I want to get better at it.'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s the first piece of art you ever made?'
b'The first painting I really cared about was probably when I was a teenager, maybe 13 or 14 years old.'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s the worst studio you ever had?'
b'The freezing-cold basement of my parents\xe2\x80\x99 house on Martha\xe2\x80\x99s Vineyard. Winter of 2002.'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s the first work you ever sold? For how much?'
b'I sold a painting after college for $1,000, before grad school.'
b'When you start a new piece, where do you begin? What\xe2\x80\x99s the first step?'
b'I think there\xe2\x80\x99s a certain amount of avoidance. I like to have things sit around for a while before it\xe2\x80\x99s go time. I find a photograph that I like, and then I usually make drawings. Maybe half the time I paint from the drawings and the other half from photographs. I use the photo for the structure of the painting; I project out different shapes, trace it out, mix the colors and build an image, like a flat map, and then I paint all the details on top. I like to have things just starting and just finishing and everywhere in between. I like to wake up and have choices to gravitate to.'
b'How do you know when you\xe2\x80\x99re done?'
b'You know after a lot of looking.'
b'How many assistants do you have?'
b'Two.'
b'What music do you play when you\xe2\x80\x99re making art?'
b'Mostly basketball podcasts. I listen to Howard Stern three days a week. Reggae, lots of eras of hip-hop, a variety of rock \xe2\x80\x99n\xe2\x80\x99 roll.'
b'When did you first feel comfortable saying you\xe2\x80\x99re a professional artist?'
b'I was a slow learner and a late bloomer in painting. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t really put it all together until 2006. I had a show at Black Dragon Society. I made $29,000, I quit my job, and after 2006, I was a full-time painter. Making a living from being an artist and not having to do anything else usually changes a lot \xe2\x80\x94 something happens, sometimes it\xe2\x80\x99s good, sometimes it\xe2\x80\x99s bad, right? But you spend all your time doing it. You\xe2\x80\x99re dedicated.'
b'Are you bingeing on any shows right now?'
b'Oh yeah. \xe2\x80\x9cCrashing,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cMillion Dollar Listing,\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cVanderpump Rules.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s the weirdest object in your studio?'
b'This giant basketball is a sculpture by Paa Joe, a 72-year-old Ghanaian artist. Look him up. He makes fantasy coffins that are in most major museum collections. This was commissioned; I wanted a giant Spalding basketball, and I told him the colors and everything. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t get a coffin because my wife thought it would be too morbid, so we got a throne. It\xe2\x80\x99s actually called a palanquin, and you carry people around in it.'
b'How do you get your news?'
b'I just started listening to these quick little podcasts that The New York Times does. I read The New York Times. I go to CNN a little bit and check out some weirder news, like serial-killer names and stuff like that.'
b'What do you do when you\xe2\x80\x99re procrastinating?'
b'Play poker with friends. '
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s the last thing that made you cry?'
b'It\xe2\x80\x99s hilarious that this made me cry: The kids wanted to watch N.B.A. players flying into the stands trying to get out-of-bounds balls. I was like, \xe2\x80\x9cThis is so cool that they\xe2\x80\x99re so into basketball.\xe2\x80\x9d Even thinking about it makes me \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s like happy crying. Positive. These kids want to see replays of Shaq, who\xe2\x80\x99s seven feet tall, flying into the stands. You should watch it.'
b'What do you usually wear when you work?'

b'What do you buy in bulk with the most frequency?'
b'LaCroix. I\xe2\x80\x99ve got a variety of favorite flavors.'
b'What do you pay for rent?'
b'We don\xe2\x80\x99t pay rent. We own the building.'
b'Do you exercise?'
b'We have a little gym. I would like to say that I\xe2\x80\x99m fat and I\xe2\x80\x99m also fit at the same time. I have a routine. VersaClimber and a lot of bands to strengthen the buttocks.'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99s your favorite artwork by someone else?'
b'I love that Picasso goat he made out of bronze, where he uses a basket for the goat\xe2\x80\x99s tummy. It\xe2\x80\x99s one of the great bronze sculptures.'

b'On Pro Basketball'
b'By Scott Cacciola'
b'CHARLOTTE, N.C. \xe2\x80\x94 Consider the following scenes from the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s annual bacchanal/business convention known as All-Star weekend:'
b'Spike Lee standing on a street corner waiting for the crosswalk signal. Stan Kroenke, whose family owns the Denver Nuggets, holding court in a hotel lobby. Joel Embiid, the star center of the Philadelphia 76ers, making small talk with the governor of North Carolina. An army of personal stylists waiting to be summoned by their clients for some of the flashiest events of the year.'
b'And then there were the agents and league officials and sneakerheads and reporters, some of whom traveled great distances to make unconventional requests of the weekend\xe2\x80\x99s main attractions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShout out to my fans in Mongolia!\xe2\x80\x9d John Collins of the Atlanta Hawks yelled into a camera the morning before his appearance in the Saturday slam dunk contest.'
b'[Slam Dunk Contest: Hamidou Diallo\xe2\x80\x99s Dunk Is Even Better Viewed Frame by Frame]'
b'All-Star weekend tends to be a blend of basketball and branding, business and pleasure \xe2\x80\x94 a showcase for a powerful league whose global influence continues to expand.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe whole weekend,\xe2\x80\x9d Mike Conley of the Memphis Grizzlies said, \xe2\x80\x9cis just a big party.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The All-Star Game itself, scheduled for Sunday night, felt secondary to just about everything else in the host city, as it has for many years. Daryl Morey, the general manager of the Houston Rockets, recalled waiting in line in 2006 for one of the more popular parties at All-Star weekend in Houston, where he watched Maciej Lampe \xe2\x80\x94 a center from Poland who appeared in 64 career games over parts of three seasons \xe2\x80\x94 bypass the line so that he could immediately be waved inside by security.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I\xe2\x80\x99m like, \xe2\x80\x98Man, I\xe2\x80\x99m behind Maciej Lampe?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d said Morey, who would officially join the front office of the Rockets a little more than six weeks later.'
b'All-Star weekend has only grown in recent years. One spreadsheet making the rounds in Charlotte listed more than 100 parties, and that did not include many of the more exclusive events. (Michael Jordan hosted a big one.) Thanks to a change in the league schedule, there is more partying and less deal-making than there used to be.'
b'Last year, the league moved the trade deadline up so that it preceded All-Star weekend. In the past, the deadline came a few days after the game, a sequence which helped create its share of absurdity. One of the more notorious examples came in 2017, when word leaked during the fourth quarter of the All-Star Game that the New Orleans Pelicans had struck a deal to acquire DeMarcus Cousins from the Sacramento Kings. Cousins learned of the trade during postgame interviews.'
b'The weekend vibe is different now.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s so much more fun,\xe2\x80\x9d one prominent agent said at a party that he hosted.'
b'In the corner, a disc jockey who appeared to be in his 60s spun tunes in a Hawaiian shirt and red-tinted glasses, while women wearing bright red dresses passed out hors d\xe2\x80\x99oeuvres. Agents, clients and marketing honchos milled about the room.'
b'But none of this is meant to suggest that deals do not get done.'
b'On Thursday night, at a downtown hotel bar where patrons sipped $25 cocktails, a crowd of very tall men gathered as a private event wound down at a nearby steakhouse. Among the luminaries who emerged from the event: Adam Silver, the N.B.A. commissioner; Kroenke, who also owns the Los Angeles Rams; Brian Rolapp, the N.F.L.\xe2\x80\x99s chief media and business officer; Bill Simmons, the founder of The Ringer; Connor Schell, ESPN\xe2\x80\x99s executive vice president for content; and Bob Myers, the general manager of the Golden State Warriors.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere are definitely conversations happening,\xe2\x80\x9d Morey said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd there\xe2\x80\x99s serendipity involved. You\xe2\x80\x99re always bumping into people.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Morey was finishing lunch at an upscale restaurant. Warren LeGarie, a longtime agent to many coaches and executives, and Kiki Vandeweghe, the league\xe2\x80\x99s executive vice president for basketball operations, were dining at nearby tables. Morey was about to head into a meeting with Vandeweghe and Monty McCutchen, who supervises the league\xe2\x80\x99s referees.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cObviously, we care deeply about where the league is going,\xe2\x80\x9d Morey said, \xe2\x80\x9cso talking to Adam Silver about strategy or Monty McCutchen about changing how they might call certain things \xe2\x80\x94 all that kind of stuff could impact our franchise moving forward, so I try to be involved.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The atmosphere may seem more relaxed than it was two years ago, when most team executives and agents were focused on the trade deadline, but the shift in the schedule has not pushed aside the league\xe2\x80\x99s most pressing issues.'
b'In Charlotte, a cloud loomed over the festivities, and it came in the shape of a unibrow.'
b'Perhaps you have heard? Anthony Davis, the star center for the Pelicans, requested a trade 10 days before the deadline.'
b'The Pelicans, though, rejected all trade offers for him and instead hope to reap better players and draft picks in a deal this summer. Last week, Pelicans Coach Alvin Gentry called the drama of it all a \xe2\x80\x9cdumpster fire.\xe2\x80\x9d On Friday, the Pelicans fired their general manager. On Saturday, Davis told reporters that his list of preferred destinations included the Knicks and the Los Angeles Lakers. Hours later, Silver said he would like trade demands and discussions to remain behind closed doors.'
b'In any case, the Davis situation only underscored how much the topic of player movement dominates the league \xe2\x80\x94 even in the middle of the season, and even after the trade deadline. Everyone here was fixated on what could happen just over four months from now \xe2\x80\x94 at the start of free agency.'
b'Will Kevin Durant leave the Warriors? Will Kawhi Leonard spurn the Toronto Raptors? Will Kyrie Irving bolt from the Boston Celtics? And, again, what about Davis?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNo one likes to see an instance,\xe2\x80\x9d Silver said, \xe2\x80\x9cwhere a player is demanding that he be traded when he\xe2\x80\x99s still in the middle of a contractual obligation to a team.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Silver made those remarks, and his wish for private trade discussions, at a news conference before Saturday night\xe2\x80\x99s skills, dunk and 3-point competitions.'
b'The media forum, like the carefully coordinated outfits stars wore to events around town, has become part of the event\xe2\x80\x99s routine. So has the roll call of courtside A-listers during the dunk contest; this year\xe2\x80\x99s included the rappers Quavo, 2 Chainz, J. Cole and Gucci Mane.'
b'All-Star weekend was not always so structured \xe2\x80\x94 or extravagant. Paul Westphal recalled making his first trip to an All-Star Game in 1977 as a guard for the Phoenix Suns. The league hosted a modest dinner. Players received commemorative mugs. Anyone associated with the game stayed at the same hotel in downtown Milwaukee.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt wasn\xe2\x80\x99t like it is now where the game takes over the whole city,\xe2\x80\x9d Westphal said.'
b'Kareem Abdul-Jabbar missed practice, Westphal said, then showed up about 20 minutes before the start of the game in a fur coat. Westphal helped seal his team\xe2\x80\x99s win with a late steal against Pete Maravich. It was a moment he said he would never forget.'
b'This weekend, Westphal was in Charlotte, where he was named a finalist for the Basketball Hall of Fame. He said he was not planning to attend any parties.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJust dinner with friends,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'In Charlotte, the streets around the host arena, Spectrum Center, were choked with traffic. Concert fliers hung from every lamppost. And none of the guests, spread among numerous hotels at premium nightly rates, seemed to mind the cold weather as countless lines formed for restaurants, bars and pop-up musical performances.'
b'Given all the extracurriculars, it was easy to forget that basketball was the only reason anyone was here in the first place \xe2\x80\x94 and perhaps that was because the only legitimate basketball was being played in a college gymnasium a few miles from downtown. A group of elite teenage prospects, without much fanfare, had convened for the league\xe2\x80\x99s annual Basketball Without Borders Global Camp.'
b'In all, 63 boys and girls from 31 countries played in front of scouts and executives who hoped to identify the sport\xe2\x80\x99s next batch of stars.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of talent here,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brooks Meek, the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s vice president for international basketball operations.'
b'The spotlight will find them soon enough.'

b'Marc Stein, an N.B.A. reporter for more than 30 years who now covers the league for The New York Times, and Ralph Lawler, longtime broadcaster for the Los Angeles Clippers, were honored on Friday by the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame, which named them as the 2019 Curt Gowdy Media Award recipients for their contributions to basketball.'
b'Stein, 49, and Lawler, 80, will be among those honored at the Hall of Fame\xe2\x80\x99s September enshrinement ceremonies in Springfield, Mass.'
b'Stein started his career covering the Clippers and then the Lakers for The Los Angeles Daily News, before moving to The Dallas Morning News as a Mavericks beat reporter and eventually a national columnist. b'A student at a Catholic school in Kentucky has sued the Northern Kentucky Health Department, claiming it violated his First Amendment rights by barring him from playing basketball because he refused to be vaccinated against chickenpox.'
b'The lawsuit, filed last week in Boone County Circuit Court on behalf of the student, Jerome Kunkel, an 18-year-old senior, argues that the action violates his right to freedom of religion. Being vaccinated, it contends, would go against Mr. Kunkel\xe2\x80\x99s religious beliefs as a practicing Catholic, because the vaccine contains \xe2\x80\x9caborted fetal cells.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The lawsuit came after an outbreak of chickenpox at Assumption Academy in Walton, Ky., prompted officials to send out two warnings in February.'
b'On March 14, the Health Department issued a statement saying that because there had been 32 cases of chickenpox at the school, students who were not vaccinated or already immune could not attend school \xe2\x80\x9cuntil 21 days after the onset of rash for the last ill student or staff member.\xe2\x80\x9d The statement also said all school extracurricular events would be canceled.'
b'Mr. Kunkel\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, Chris Wiest, said in an interview on Monday that the school had told him in February that he could not play in or attend any basketball games because he was not vaccinated.'
b'Mr. Kunkel is also now barred from attending school because of the Health Department\xe2\x80\x99s action.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m pretty devastated,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Kunkel, who was captain of the basketball team, said in an interview on Monday night. After playing for all four years of high school, \xe2\x80\x9cfor it come crashing down at the end, it\xe2\x80\x99s not very fun,\xe2\x80\x9d he added. Mr. Kunkel was not able to play in the last three games of the season.'
b'The lawsuit contends that in Kentucky, students are allowed a vaccination exemption on religious grounds if they provide a sworn statement, which Mr. Kunkel did in early 2018.'
b'The chickenpox vaccine is grown in cells originally derived from fetuses aborted in the early 1960s. Vaccines may contain nanofragments of DNA from the fetal cells, which are used because human viruses do not grow well in animal cells, according to a statement the vaccine\xe2\x80\x99s manufacturer, Merck, gave to ABC News.'
b'It is unclear how many students have been barred from attending the school because they have not been vaccinated or were found to be immune. Mr. Wiest, however, said that the parents of at least 18 children at the school had contacted him since the Health Department\xe2\x80\x99s announcement.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think this is going to be a much bigger fight at the end of the day,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Wiest said.'
b'Officials at the school did not immediately respond to a request for comment on Monday. But the Health Department defended its response to the outbreak.'
b'The action, the department said in its statement, was \xe2\x80\x9cin direct response to a public health threat and was an appropriate and necessary response to prevent further spread of this contagious illness.\xe2\x80\x9d A spokesman for the department declined to comment further.'

b'CHAPEL HILL, N.C. \xe2\x80\x94 Sylvia Hatchell, the University of North Carolina women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach, used to preach about \xe2\x80\x9cthe fishbowl.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re always in the fishbowl,\xe2\x80\x9d Hatchell would tell players like Tonya Sampson, a former player who recalled the admonitions in an interview on Friday. \xe2\x80\x9cYou never know who\xe2\x80\x99s watching. You\xe2\x80\x99ve always got to carry yourself with integrity and the best way you can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Twenty-five years after Hatchell and Sampson won a national title for North Carolina, Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s reputation is in peril and her team is in turmoil. U.N.C. officials, who were told late last month about three episodes that some players thought revealed Hatchell to be racially insensitive and aloof, placed her and her assistants on paid administrative leave and opened a storied program to abrupt scrutiny.'
b'An outside law firm is investigating. Several U.N.C. players are considering transferring. And Hatchell, 67, one of women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball\xe2\x80\x99s most successful and influential coaches and a member of the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame, is not talking beyond a single written statement.'
b'It seems no one, from high-ranking state lawmakers to parents of players, is certain whether she will coach again at U.N.C., a Southern powerhouse of athletics and academics that has spent years grappling with issues of race. Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, Wade M. Smith, could only say, \xe2\x80\x9cI hope she does come back.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The allegations against Hatchell, privately detailed to university officials on March 28 and in news media accounts in the week that followed, represent a grave test to her 33-year tenure at U.N.C., where she is under contract for just one more season. And although the just-concluded season was modestly more successful than other recent campaigns, Hatchell has lately led a program that felt removed from the one that, not long ago, routinely won at least 25 games a year.'
b'This year, in its first appearance in the N.C.A.A. women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball tournament since the 2014-15 season, U.N.C. (18-15) exited in the first round with a 20-point loss to California.'
b'Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s critics have been reluctant to speak publicly, in part, they said, because they fear retaliation. After so many years, Hatchell has become an institution at U.N.C., not quite on par with Dean Smith, the revered former men\xe2\x80\x99s coach, but not far off. Many current and former players did not respond to messages, but some who did expressed support for Hatchell, even as they depicted her as a coach of searing, drawling intensity.'
b'The university said it had hired a Charlotte law firm to \xe2\x80\x9cassess the culture of the women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball program and the experience of our student-athletes.\xe2\x80\x9d Officials have declined to comment beyond that.'
b'The law firm is expected to examine the quality of medical care for players and whether Hatchell had warned her team that \xe2\x80\x9cnooses\xe2\x80\x9d would await them if they turned in a poor performance against Louisville. U.N.C. officials were also told that Hatchell had urged her players to perform a \xe2\x80\x9ctomahawk chop\xe2\x80\x9d war cry to fire them up \xe2\x80\x94 a suggestion the women resisted \xe2\x80\x94 and that she had described players as \xe2\x80\x9cold mules.\xe2\x80\x9d Some people perceived the comment as a reference to female slaves.'
b'Smith, Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, said the coach \xe2\x80\x9cdoesn\xe2\x80\x99t have a racist bone in her body.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He said some players had misconstrued Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s words, but he acknowledged that she had apologized after an internal uproar about the episode in which people recalled that she had referred to nooses.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe said words like, \xe2\x80\x98They\xe2\x80\x99re going to hang us out to dry. They\xe2\x80\x99re going to take a rope and hang us out to dry,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Smith said. He added that Hatchell, who did not believe she had said anything improper, initially apologized by saying something like, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m sorry you took it that way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe team did not see that as an apology,\xe2\x80\x9d Smith said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think she thought she apologized.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But a furor still built, and the university, whose trustees declined to comment or did not respond to messages, will soon have to decide the fate of the coach, who cultivated the modern women\xe2\x80\x99s game and has been known more for her fiery courtside coaching than personal controversy.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI never encountered any kind of racial slurs or racism,\xe2\x80\x9d said Nikki Teasley, a former U.N.C. point guard who went on to a long career in the W.N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x9cMy experience with Coach Hatchell was very heartfelt, very loving, very kind.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Teasley, who is African-American, said she did not recall any racially improper comments but did say Hatchell was fierce and demanding.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAfter playing and then becoming a coach myself and then a mother,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cyou understand that sometimes things do get overheated, and in the heat of the moment you do say some things.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hatchell grew up in Gastonia, N.C., a small city 20 miles west of Charlotte, and graduated from a public high school that had only recently integrated. Judge Jesse B. Caldwell III, who graduated from Hunter Huss High School a few years ahead of Hatchell, recalled little friction over integration in the area. Basketball, he said, helped bring people together. At nearby Ashley High School, an integrated team won a state championship in 1967.'
b'Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s school did not have a women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball team when she was a student. She began coaching as an undergraduate, and she took control of the North Carolina program, already an emerging incubator of basketball players, in 1986.'
b'She became known as a skilled recruiter and drew some of the nation\xe2\x80\x99s top basketball talent to Chapel Hill. Yet to people in and around her program, Hatchell sometimes seemed to be more of a chief executive than a coach. Andrew Calder, a Hatchell deputy since her arrival at U.N.C., was often credited with developing players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI learned the game through Coach Calder,\xe2\x80\x9d Sampson said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou knew who the head coach was, but hands-on, no, she wasn\xe2\x80\x99t hands-on when I was there.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'To a point, the formula worked. Lifted by a 3-point shot as time expired, the Tar Heels won their only women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball title in 1994. Including that season, the Tar Heels have reached the Final Four three times \xe2\x80\x94 far less than programs like Connecticut, Tennessee and Notre Dame.'
b'At their best, Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s teams played with an attractive, fast-paced style that relied on fast breaks and smart point-guard play. This season she continued to tout her up-tempo offense.'
b'Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s stature has grown in a state where college basketball is prized. She missed one season, in 2013-14, for cancer treatment, but the next season North Carolina went 26-9 and finished with a No. 9 ranking.'
b'Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s comeback era came as U.N.C. wrestled with an academic fraud scandal that reached into the women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball program. Although the university was not punished, years of bad headlines, investigations and speculation took a toll. Some players cited the scandal when they chose to transfer elsewhere.'
b'Hatchell, though, remained and, in 2016, received a contract extension. Last year, she signed a deal with Nike: $150,000 for up to four personal appearances a year until 2028. (The contract ends early if Hatchell leaves as head coach.)'
b'Beyond basketball, Hatchell\xe2\x80\x99s Christian faith has long been central to her life and her public persona. More than a decade ago, she started a women\xe2\x80\x99s Bible study in the Chapel Hill area. For the last six years, the teacher has been Rachel-Ruth Wright, a granddaughter of Billy Graham, the North Carolina evangelist.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve never heard her say one negative thing about any of her players,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Wright said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s always positive, always excited. She\xe2\x80\x99s just an encouragement all the time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The university\xe2\x80\x99s investigation might answer if she went too far in doing so. The Charlotte Observer this week published a scathing editorial about the conduct of college coaches.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOther women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball programs, including Georgia Tech, have fired coaches in recent years for mistreating players,\xe2\x80\x9d the paper, among the state\xe2\x80\x99s most widely read, wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cIf U.N.C. finds abuse from any coach \xe2\x80\x94 men\xe2\x80\x99s or women\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x94 it should do the same.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Weeks ago, Hatchell appeared in high spirits at a commemoration of U.N.C.\xe2\x80\x99s only national title.'
b'Hatchell visited a pregame lunch for members of that 1994 championship team, who were later honored on the court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe hugged me. \xe2\x80\x98Glad to see you\xe2\x80\x99 kind of thing,\xe2\x80\x9d Sampson said. \xe2\x80\x9cThen she was off, because she had to get prepared for the game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
