b'By Marc Tracy'
b'A federal judge in Manhattan on Tuesday sentenced three men in a college basketball fraud case to between six and nine months in prison, lenient sentences that the judge said were nonetheless important to deter the funneling of money to the families of college basketball prospects \xe2\x80\x94 an N.C.A.A. violation that a jury found last year also constituted a felony.'
b'The sentences come ahead of a second trial next month at which more may be revealed about how widespread the rot in recruiting has spread.'
b'James Gatto, the former head of global basketball marketing at Adidas, was sentenced to nine months by U.S. District Court Judge Lewis A. Kaplan. Merl Code Jr., another former Adidas employee, and Christian Dawkins, an aspiring agent, were given six months each. Code and Dawkins, who are also defendants in next month\xe2\x80\x99s trial, were ordered to pay restitution of a little more than $28,000 each, with Gatto\xe2\x80\x99s amount of restitution still to be determined.'
b'Kaplan ruled that the punishments would not go into effect until the appeal process is completed. The defendants have two weeks to ask the federal circuit court to re-examine the case.'
b'A jury convicted the three men last fall of defrauding the University of Louisville and, in Gatto\xe2\x80\x99s case, also North Carolina State University and the University of Kansas. The men participated in a scheme in which the families of highly rated men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball recruits were offered money in exchange for pledges to play for one of those teams, which are sponsored by Adidas. Prosecutors argued that by unknowingly making the universities vulnerable to N.C.A.A. sanctions, the defendants had victimized the schools.'
b'Such offers are barred by N.C.A.A. rules, which require that college athletes adhere to the association\xe2\x80\x99s policy of amateurism and not be compensated for their participation in their sport beyond a scholarship and related costs of attendance.'
b'Repercussions from the charges brought by the U.S. Attorney for the Southern District of New York have already included the firing of a Hall of Fame coach \xe2\x80\x94 Rick Pitino, formerly of Louisville, who denies wrongdoing and whom prosecutors did not charge. A Kansas player was ruled ineligible early this year after his connection to the scheme came to light.'
b'The lawyers for Code and Dawkins welcomed the sentence.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHappy might be the wrong word, but the judge granted a lenient sentence,\xe2\x80\x9d said Steve Haney, who represents Dawkins.'
b'Haney also promised that the second trial, which involves alleged bribes to assistant coaches at top men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball programs, would not only exonerate Dawkins but would also show how college basketball business is really done.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re going to pull back the covers,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cThis could transform college basketball and put the players in a situation moving forward so they and their labor are treated fairly.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Haney pledged to put coaches on the stand \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cas many as I can get into the courtroom.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Robert S. Khuzami, the acting U.S. Attorney for the Southern District of New York in this case, said in a statement, \xe2\x80\x9cThe sentences imposed today only begin to reflect the magnitude of the harm these defendants caused through a scheme that not only defrauded multiple public universities but upended the lives of young student-athletes and corrupted a game cherished by so many.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s sentencing hearing in a packed courtroom on a high floor of the federal district building in downtown Manhattan saw all three defendants as well as their lawyers address the court and plead for leniency. They requested no jail time at all. While most of these statements referred to the defendants\xe2\x80\x99 personal characters, some of the attorneys also pointed to the unusual nature of the case, which depended on a theory in which the universities were victimized by the defendants\xe2\x80\x99 attempts to secure them top talent (albeit while putting them at risk of N.C.A.A. penalties).'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf he thought that anyone would conceive what he did here as a crime, he would never have done it,\xe2\x80\x9d Code\xe2\x80\x99s lawyer, Mark Moore, said of his client.'
b'Comparing the situation in the case to a legal principle called the \xe2\x80\x9cdoctrine of unclean hands,\xe2\x80\x9d Moore suggested that widespread illicit activity in college recruiting called into question who was truly responsible for the harm his client had purportedly caused.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAdidas has financial contracts with Louisville through which Louisville profited,\xe2\x80\x9d Moore said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou have not seen Louisville or any of these schools look to get out of their contracts with Adidas\xe2\x80\x9d since the scandal broke in 2017, he added.'
b'Moore noted that although it was not admitted into the record before the jury, Kaplan seemed to recall an earlier scandal at Louisville in which a basketball staffer paid strippers and prostitutes to entertain recruits and players in on-campus housing.'
b'Indeed, Kaplan himself appeared to raise so-called Strippergate, which resulted in N.C.A.A. penalties, during the prosecutor Edward B. Diskant\xe2\x80\x99s statement to the court, in which Diskant insisted that the universities were the victims.'
b'Kaplan said that the defendants had committed \xe2\x80\x9ca serious crime,\xe2\x80\x9d one whose purportedly common nature was not by itself exonerating: \xe2\x80\x9cThe \xe2\x80\x98everybody\xe2\x80\x99s doing it\xe2\x80\x99 argument, in short, is not a Get Out of Jail Free card,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'But the judge also recognized that the alleged behavior of university employees like assistant coaches and, perhaps, the interests of the universities themselves complicated the theory of the case \xe2\x80\x94 on which a jury convicted \xe2\x80\x94 that the universities were victims.'
b'Referring to Brian \xe2\x80\x9cTugs\xe2\x80\x9d Bowen Jr., a prospect whose father testified that he had indirectly taken from Adidas in exchange for Bowen\xe2\x80\x99s commitment to Louisville, Kaplan said, \xe2\x80\x9cTo me, probably the worst, the most seriously injured victim of the Louisville scheme was Tug Bowen.\xe2\x80\x9d (Bowen was declared ineligible and is now playing professionally in Australia.)'
b'On wiretaps, defendants made oblique references to their activity being typical of high-profile men\xe2\x80\x99s college basketball. They also suggested that at least one of Adidas\xe2\x80\x99s rivals were involved in similar schemes, though there have been no further charges.'
b'Last year Yahoo Sports revealed documents that purported to show the families of several former stars who went on to play for many of the top college basketball programs were on the payroll of Dawkins, the aspiring agent.'
b'The second case, scheduled to be tried next month, initially featured as defendants three former assistant coaches at major programs along with Dawkins and a money manager. The money manager, Munish Sood, reached a deal with prosecutors before the last trial and served as their witness. The three former assistants all pleaded guilty in January, after the guilty verdict in the first case.'
b'A third case, whose trial is scheduled for later thus year, features the former Auburn assistant Chuck Person, who has been charged with bribery.'

b'By Marc Tracy and Kevin Draper'
b'When the left sneaker of college basketball\xe2\x80\x99s biggest star split open on national television Wednesday night 30 seconds into the biggest game of the season, what spilled out was not only his foot but also questions about the future of a marquee player and about the huge influence shoe companies hold over big-time college basketball.'
b'The episode occurred in a game between the archrivals Duke and North Carolina. Zion Williamson, a Duke freshman, pivoted with the ball above the foul line, and the sheer force of his 285-pound frame and acrobatic versatility appeared to cut the shoe almost in two, as though severed by a sharp knife.'
b'Former President Barack Obama, sitting on the sidelines at the Duke arena, was seen on video pointing at Williamson and appearing to say, \xe2\x80\x9cHis shoe broke.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As the scene was replayed on countless highlight shows on Thursday, the damaged shoe threatened to become a nightmare for Nike, which pays tens of millions to elite college sports programs to be the exclusive sponsor for teams and supplier of their footwear.'
b'With his shoe split and his knee sprained, Williamson, an unpaid, budding superstar, sat helpless on the arena floor, staring at the shoe he was wearing in part because of a rich deal between Nike and Duke, one of the world\xe2\x80\x99s wealthiest universities.'
b'Here were all the issues of big-time college sports laid bare: Should amateurism be curbed in college sports, allowing athletes a cut of the money they help produce? Should a prodigious talent like Williamson, who is good enough to play professionally right now, have to risk his future competing for free because of an N.B.A. rule prohibiting him from leaping to the league from high school? Do the sneaker companies, which were at the heart of a federal fraud trial near the start of the season, do more harm than good in college sports?'
b'For a quarter of a century, Nike has been paying Duke tens of millions of dollars to sponsor its teams, and to ensure that its athletes wear only footwear bearing the company\xe2\x80\x99s ubiquitous logo. The players receive enough shoes to carry them through the season, allowing them to serve largely as free human billboards.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll this does,\xe2\x80\x9d Gabe Feldman, who directs Tulane\xe2\x80\x99s sports law program, said of Williamson\xe2\x80\x99s injury, \xe2\x80\x9cis put a magnifying glass on an issue that has existed for a long time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williamson has not commented.'
b'Nike stock closed down Thursday by 1.05 percent, as the world wondered how a sneaker could split so badly in the middle of a game.'
b'The answer remains a puzzle even to experts. James Gilbert, an orthopedic surgeon who worked with Duke athletics in the 1990s, said he had seen shoes fall apart similarly on soccer players, but never on the hardwood.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s a product failure,\xe2\x80\x9d Gilbert said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve never seen that. I had no idea that that happens.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In a statement Wednesday night, Nike said: \xe2\x80\x9cWe are obviously concerned and want to wish Zion a speedy recovery. The quality and performance of our products are of utmost importance.\xe2\x80\x9d The statement called the shoe explosion \xe2\x80\x9can isolated occurrence,\xe2\x80\x9d though in 2015, the Kenyan marathoner Eliud Kipchoge won the Berlin Marathon even as the insoles of his Nike shoes slipped out of place.'
b'Williamson, who has a mild knee sprain, will probably be sidelined for one to two weeks, and then continue being the favorite to become the No. 1 overall pick in the N.B.A. draft in June. By then, he will probably already be a millionaire, because of the endorsement deals he can sign when he ends his college career. For now, he is an N.C.A.A. amateur.'
b'Sneaker companies first became deeply involved with college athletics in the late 1970s, when an enterprising Nike executive, Sonny Vaccaro, arranged for several prominent coaches, such as John Thompson of Georgetown and Jerry Tarkanian of Nevada-Las Vegas, to receive money in exchange for outfitting their players in the company\xe2\x80\x99s shoes. Starting in the late 1980s, Nike began to sign deals that covered all of a university\xe2\x80\x99s teams.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow we see the kids wearing the shoes and selling the product all over the world \xe2\x80\x94 and the kids never got anything,\xe2\x80\x9d Vaccaro, who left Nike years ago, said Thursday. \xe2\x80\x9cThe money has served the same people, except for the most important ones.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A decision in a federal class-action lawsuit challenging N.C.A.A. restrictions on compensation is expected any day.'
b'Standout basketball players were squeezed further in 2006, when the N.B.A. barred talented teenagers from following in the footsteps of Kobe Bryant, Kevin Garnett and LeBron James by entering the league straight out of high school.'
b'Then, in September 2017, federal prosecutors in New York\xe2\x80\x99s Southern District revealed more of the chasm between college basketball players, who can receive only scholarships and related costs of being on campus, and the administrators and coaches who reap the benefits of the revenue the athletes generate for their colleges, conferences and the N.C.A.A. itself. The men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball tournament yields about $1 billion a year for the television rights.'
b'In three complaints filed in United States District Court in New York, prosecutors accused roughly a dozen assistant coaches, middlemen and employees of Adidas of plotting to funnel money to players\xe2\x80\x99 families in exchange for pledges that the athletes, among other things, would play for certain universities and sign with Adidas once they began their pro careers. The scandal led to the firing of a Hall of Fame coach, Rick Pitino of the University of Louisville, and has netted three convictions, including of Adidas\xe2\x80\x99s former director of global sports marketing.'
b'The transactions outlined by the complaints are practically the modus operandi at many top basketball programs, documents and testimony in the legal case suggested. Wiretaps revealed suspects describing at least one Adidas rival engaging in similar practices. Documents from the case reported by Yahoo Sports last year indicated that former top players at dozens of prominent programs \xe2\x80\x94 including Duke \xe2\x80\x94 had been on the payroll of an aspiring agent who has since been convicted of fraud.'
b'Duke did not reply to requests for comment Thursday.'
b'The specifics of Duke\xe2\x80\x99s deal with Nike, which the two sides have extended through 2027, are not publicly known. As a private university, Duke is not obligated to reveal the terms.'
b'But a look at Nike deals with similar universities that are public offer some indication of how the contracts work.'
b'Nike\xe2\x80\x99s deal with North Carolina, for instance, will give the university more than $90 million in cash and merchandise over 10 years. Nike also signed personal contracts with a number of North Carolina coaches: Roy Williams, the men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach, will receive an average of $300,000 a year over the life of the 10-year agreement.'
b'Contracts generally state that Nike is not liable for injuries suffered by athletes wearing its products. The contracts also require every player to wear the company\xe2\x80\x99s shoes unless a medical condition makes Nike footwear unsuitable. A player might, as stipulated in Nike\xe2\x80\x99s deal with the University of Michigan, be required to make himself available for examination by Nike or a local podiatrist before using a shoe made by another company.'
b'It is not known why Williamson wore the particular Nike model that tore on Wednesday. It was a Nike \xe2\x80\x9csignature shoe,\xe2\x80\x9d a term for a style endorsed by a specific athlete \xe2\x80\x94 in this case, the N.B.A. star Paul George, who plays for the Oklahoma City Thunder.'
b'What makes Williamson so compelling is the same thing that might make a shoe unable to contain him. He combines size and speed with strength and agility in the manner of James, who during a day off this month went to Charlottesville, Va., to see Williamson and the Blue Devils take on Virginia. Though Williamson weighs 285 pounds, at times he seems like the fastest player on the court.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you\xe2\x80\x99re dealing with some of these athletes who are getting quicker, stronger, faster, you\xe2\x80\x99ve got to consider some of that,\xe2\x80\x9d said Gilbert, the orthopedist.'

b'As you may remember from chemistry class, a litmus test determines a solution\xe2\x80\x99s relative acidity. But the phrase is also used metaphorically to refer to a character-defining political issue, and it has been popping up in coverage of the race for the Democratic presidential nomination.'
b'The chemical test, in use since the Middle Ages, employs a dye derived from lichens to determine whether a solution is more acidic or alkaline.'
b'The political application of the phrase appeared in The Times at least as early as 1950, when it described NATO and the Marshall Plan as \xe2\x80\x9cthe litmus test for distinguishing between Communists and supporters of the United States.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This year, \xe2\x80\x9clitmus test\xe2\x80\x9d has appeared in The Times to refer to marijuana legalization, the proposed border wall and universal health care.'

b'By Chloe Malle'
b'THE FALCONER By Dana Czapnik 278 pp. Atria Books. $25.'
b'Toward the end of \xe2\x80\x9cThe Falconer,\xe2\x80\x9d Dana Czapnik\xe2\x80\x99s electric debut novel, 17-year-old Lucy Adler looks up from Simone de Beauvoir\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cThe Second Sex\xe2\x80\x9d at the Japanese maple on her Upper West Side neighbor\xe2\x80\x99s terrace. It\xe2\x80\x99s difficult to read the passage and not think of beloved Francie Nolan peering out another window in another New York City borough, almost 100 years earlier. Yet whereas in \xe2\x80\x9cA Tree Grows in Brooklyn,\xe2\x80\x9d both Francie and the Tree of Heaven grow up amid an unforgiving, concrete urban setting, Czapnik\xe2\x80\x99s maple has been coaxed and cared for, its leaves treated with a protective coating. Lucy, a middle-class Manhattanite attending an elite private school, has battled none of the Nolan family\xe2\x80\x99s hardships, nor is she plagued by the acerbic ennui that Holden Caulfield gave voice to in \xe2\x80\x9cThe Catcher in the Rye,\xe2\x80\x9d but comparisons to both classic New York bildungsromans nonetheless seem inevitable. That is, until you realize that what binds them \xe2\x80\x94 all tell of a determinedly independent young hero\xe2\x80\x99s quest for selfhood catalyzed by the crucible of New York City \xe2\x80\x94 is also what makes them so resistant to comparison. Like Francie and Holden before her, Lucy, a street-smart, superlative basketballer vulnerable to the perils of approaching womanhood, is too carefully drawn to be equated with anyone else.'
b'Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s fierce first-person point of view is as confident and fearless as she is on the court; she narrates her story with the immediacy and sharpness of a sports commentator, mixed with the pathos and wisdom of a perceptive adolescent charting the perils of her senior year of high school. A self-described \xe2\x80\x9cpizza bagel \xe2\x80\x94 a Jewish and Italian mutt-girl,\xe2\x80\x9d Lucy grapples with the rigid expectations of others, especially her harshly critical high school peers who have rendered her an outcast. \xe2\x80\x9cIsn\xe2\x80\x99t it just so much easier for everybody when a girl fits into a nice little girl category \xe2\x80\x94 good girl slut tomboy girly girl smart girl ditz \xe2\x80\x94 instead of being a fully fleshed-out person who is in constant conversation \xe2\x80\xa6 with all the various fractious parts of herself,\xe2\x80\x9d Lucy wisely observes. We watch that conversation unfold in real time through her adventures with her best friend, Alexis, a tough-talking Dominican sage tethered to Lucy through basketball and their shared outsider status; Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s forays into the navel-gazing Downtown arts scene of her painter cousin, Violet; and, most pulverizing, her unrequited love for her emotionally unavailable scrimmage partner Percy, a self-proclaimed nihilist from a neglected but moneyed family who goes through girlfriends like Kleenex and is referred to by friends as the \xe2\x80\x9cVirgin Surgeon.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But it\xe2\x80\x99s arguably the nonhuman characters that give true shape to Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s evolution: basketball and New York. (The novel\xe2\x80\x99s opening line, \xe2\x80\x9cThe ball is a face,\xe2\x80\x9d confirms the game\xe2\x80\x99s significance and anthropomorphism for her.) Only with ball in hand does Lucy feel invincible and most herself, even as that self changes: \xe2\x80\x9cI ought not to imbue a ball with so much magic, but when I\xe2\x80\x99m holding one I go from Lucy Adler, invisible girl \xe2\x80\xa6 to Lucy Adler, Warrior Goddess.\xe2\x80\x9d Her self-descriptions on the court are as visceral and vivid as any sex scene, and when the actual sex scene does eventually unfold it is against the backdrop of a Rangers game on television, the commentators\xe2\x80\x99 play-by-play mirroring Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s own disembodied narration of her experience.'
b'The basketball grows into a metaphor for the universe: \xe2\x80\x9cI bounce the world hard on the blacktop, and it comes back into my hand covered with a fine layer of New York City diamond dust.\xe2\x80\x9d The entire novel is indeed cloaked in just such a glimmering film, and Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s love-hate relationship with her roiling city reflects her changeable hopes for herself and others. \xe2\x80\x9cI guess New York is like that, in that what you mistake it for matters as much as what it actually is.\xe2\x80\x9d Czapnik, who herself grew up in Manhattan around the same time as Lucy, captures nostalgia \xe2\x80\x94 for both a vanishing New York and Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s evaporating childhood \xe2\x80\x94 with the lucidity of a V.R. headset. The early-90s era seems unremarkable to the characters in the thick of it \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cWe live in \xe2\x80\xa6 insignificant times,\xe2\x80\x9d Lucy says between hits of a joint \xe2\x80\x94 but feels poignantly pre-9/11 to today\xe2\x80\x99s reader.'
b'Lucy\xe2\x80\x99s coming-of-age is tempered by her constant brush-ups against the constrictions society places on her sex. Happening upon \xe2\x80\x9cThe Falconer,\xe2\x80\x9d a bronze of a boy in Elizabethan dress releasing a falcon in Central Park, Lucy is envious that statues of boys depict them in action poses while women are either demure nudes or Alice in Wonderland. \xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you wish they made statues of girls like that?\xe2\x80\x9d Lucy asks Alexis. \xe2\x80\x9cJust some girl having unapologetic fun.\xe2\x80\x9d Alexis replies: \xe2\x80\x9cI never apologize for the fun I have. And neither do you.\xe2\x80\x9d Reader, beware: Spending time with Lucy is unapologetic fun, and heartbreak, and awe as well.'

b'BUIES CREEK, N.C. \xe2\x80\x94 With three seconds left in the first half last Wednesday night, Campbell point guard Chris Clemons was fouled on a layup. He banged the floor in frustration as the ball rimmed out, then rose and hit both free throws. Someone in the sparsely populated stands yelled, \xe2\x80\x9cCongratulations, Chris!\xe2\x80\x9d Given the size of the crowd, it\xe2\x80\x99s almost certain Clemons heard him.'
b'The second free throw was Clemons\xe2\x80\x99s 22nd point of the night, and the 2,952nd of his four-season career at Campbell, a private university about an hour\xe2\x80\x99s drive south of Raleigh, N.C., his hometown. It also meant Clemons, a senior, had entered the top 10 of the men\xe2\x80\x99s Division I college basketball career scoring list, passing the former Kansas star Danny Manning. By the end of the game, when Clemons had finished off a season-high 48-point effort, he had passed Oscar Robertson, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s kind of a gift and a curse that you\xe2\x80\x99re not really able to enjoy the moment \xe2\x80\x94 or that I chose not to, rather,\xe2\x80\x9d Clemons said. \xe2\x80\x9cI do understand the significance of the events.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'History is being made in college basketball this season, but not all of it is being made for teams that are likely bound for the Final Four or by players who are projected to be selected early in the next N.B.A. draft.'
b'With 3,006 career points at Campbell, Clemons is two behind Hersey Hawkins, the former Bradley player, for eighth all time, heading into Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s game with High Point. At South Dakota State, another senior, Mike Daum, is poised to break into the top 10 by season\xe2\x80\x99s end; with 2,943 points, he could pass Manning in the Jackrabbits\xe2\x80\x99 game on Thursday against Fort Wayne.'
b'It is an unignorable fact that most of the players still ahead of Clemons and Daum on the career scoring list are not household names, either. After Hawkins, for instance, Clemons could pass Keydren Clark, who played for St. Peter\xe2\x80\x99s, in Jersey City; Harry Kelly of Texas Southern, in Houston; and perhaps even Alphonso Ford of Mississippi Valley State, who holds fourth place with 3,165 points. (First place, by a country mile, with 3,667 points, is the Louisiana State legend Pete Maravich, even though he played only three seasons.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI recognize that a lot of people on that list, who scored a lot of points in college, didn\xe2\x80\x99t go on to have successful N.B.A. careers,\xe2\x80\x9d said Hawkins, who did have a successful N.B.A. career and now works for the Portland Trail Blazers.'
b'Freeman Williams \xe2\x80\x94 who is second, and the scorer of 3,249 points for Portland State \xe2\x80\x94 acknowledged that his college years had been his glory days. \xe2\x80\x9cI got most of my attention as a basketball player back then,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'Clemons and Daum fit in the same category. Daum is a two-time (and probable three-time) Summit League player of the year. Clemons is leading all Division I players in scoring this season, averaging nearly 30 points a game. Although both are likely to get opportunities to shine during the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s summer league or on its development league rosters, said Fran Fraschilla, the former coach and ESPN draft analyst, the 6-foot 9-inch Daum is at best a late-second-round draft pick. Clemons, who is listed at 5-9, is unlikely to be drafted at all.'
b'The relative anonymity of college basketball\xe2\x80\x99s leading career scorers appears to be a feature, not a bug. If you are scoring so many points for so much time, you most likely are not doing so at college basketball\xe2\x80\x99s heights.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf Mike Daum or Chris Clemons had gone to play in the Big Ten or the A.C.C.,\xe2\x80\x9d Fraschilla said last week, referring to the Atlantic Coast Conference, \xe2\x80\x9cthey wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be on the verge of scoring 3,000 points.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added, \xe2\x80\x9cAs good players as they are, they would be on teams with other really talented players, as opposed to going to a school like S.D.S.U. or Campbell, where virtually from Day 1 their talent was such that they were the dominant player not only on their team but in their league.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And had they dominated as they have in a bigger league, they probably wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be seniors; the best college basketball players are around for only one or two seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s not kid ourselves,\xe2\x80\x9d said Lionel Simmons, who is third with 3,217 career points for La Salle. \xe2\x80\x9cSome of these players, if they didn\xe2\x80\x99t come out early, they could have scored 3,000.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But even when top talents played for three or four college seasons, they did so for top teams whose other talented players lowered the individual demands on them. Superlative college players like U.C.L.A.\xe2\x80\x99s Lew Alcindor (who later changed his name to Kareem Abdul-Jabbar) and Georgetown\xe2\x80\x99s Patrick Ewing had the kinds of supporting casts that come with championship teams.'
b'The most prominent name in the top 20, after Robertson, is Larry Bird, who played most of his college career at Indiana State, a team that he led to the Final Four, but one that needed him to average 30 points a game. But a place on the list can still be a point of pride years later.'
b'Hawkins acknowledged that he kept tabs on developments in the career scoring top 10. In 2014, a Blazers scout was at the Creighton game in which Doug McDermott, now of the Indiana Pacers, passed Hawkins. \xe2\x80\x9cHe was texting me, \xe2\x80\x98Six points away,\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x98Two points away,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Hawkins said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe thought it was funny. I was sitting at dinner getting texted every three minutes.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last week, Clemons deflected postgame questions about passing Manning and Robertson, saying he was focused on this season, in which the Fighting Camels (15-11) are third in the Big South. Asked whether he had kept the game ball, he laughed; of course he had not.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAfter it\xe2\x80\x99s all said and done, I\xe2\x80\x99ll definitely go back and look, reminisce on the years I\xe2\x80\x99ve had here, kind of be amazed at myself, know what I was able to accomplish,\xe2\x80\x9d Clemons said.'
b'Like Clemons, Daum emphasized in a telephone interview that he has been putting his team first. Redick and North Carolina\xe2\x80\x99s Tyler Hansbrough, two stars from the last decade whom Daum had grown up watching.'

b'\xe2\x80\x9cFor me personally,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, \xe2\x80\x9cit\xe2\x80\x99s just getting ready for the next thing.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Marc Tracy'
b'Fans tuning in to Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s marquee matchup between Duke and Virginia waited less than two minutes before getting what they came for. On an early Virginia possession, Duke\xe2\x80\x99s Zion Williamson, the impossible freshman who moves with a guard\xe2\x80\x99s agility while weighing 280 pounds, recovered a loose ball and hammered down a two-handed dunk with Old Testament fury.'
b'Williamson is expected to be the top pick in this year\xe2\x80\x99s N.B.A. draft and has been this season\xe2\x80\x99s signature player \xe2\x80\x94 a quality so inseparable from his ferocious slams that a rare missed dunk last week against Boston College became a highlight in its own right.'
b'The only other player who has come close to capturing the collective imagination as Williamson is Murray State\xe2\x80\x99s Ja Morant, a 6-foot-3 sophomore who has played his way from virtual anonymity to likely top-five draft position on a diet of Jordan-esque leaping, flying slams.'
b'That Williamson and Morant are this season\xe2\x80\x99s college basketball folk heroes is in one sense entirely logical. Dunks are popular, they dunk well, therefore they are popular.'
b'Yet in the context of recent history and current basketball trends, they are outliers as stars because they are relatively poor shooters from long distance.'
b'Neither player can efficiently utilize the 3-pointer, which has cemented itself as the most treasured tool in the modern offensive game. Williamson has made less than 30 percent of the 47 3-pointers he has attempted. Morant is at 32.7 percent, below the Division I average of 34.3 percent.'
b'Williamson\xe2\x80\x99s attitude toward the 3-pointer may be best summarized not by any of his own shots, but by his sensational block of De\xe2\x80\x99Andre Hunter\xe2\x80\x99s ill-fated attempt late in Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s game, an 81-71 Duke victory.'
b'Their proficiency in dunking over long-distance shooting signals how special they are, of course, but also might herald a market correction in which basketball\xe2\x80\x99s most reliable shot is back in.'
b'In recent seasons, the defining players \xe2\x80\x94 the ones who made the biggest impacts and summed up the college basketball zeitgeist \xe2\x80\x94 have overwhelmingly been sharpshooters. Think of Oklahoma\xe2\x80\x99s Trae Young and Buddy Hield, Kansas\xe2\x80\x99 Frank Mason III, Indiana\xe2\x80\x99s Yogi Ferrell, Purdue\xe2\x80\x99s Caleb Swanigan and even Duke\xe2\x80\x99s infamous Grayson Allen. The last 7-footer to be named player of the year, Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x99s Frank Kaminsky, was not a high-volume shooter of 3s, but he made 41.6 percent of his attempts in his Wooden Award-winning season. Villanova won a title at the buzzer when Kris Jenkins hit a 3.'
b'Yet this year\xe2\x80\x99s watch list for the Wooden Award includes Williamson and Morant along with other poor-shooting yet exciting non-big men like Duke\xe2\x80\x99s R.J. Barrett and Tennessee\xe2\x80\x99s Grant Williams. Marquette\xe2\x80\x99s Markus Howard has received comparatively little attention as this year\xe2\x80\x99s exemplary high-volume, high-accuracy distance shooter.'
b'The ESPN analyst Jay Bilas said dunks were emerging as more crucial to offenses because so-called midrange shots \xe2\x80\x94 2-point attempts that are not from close in near the basket \xe2\x80\x94 have been so devalued by analytics. Get to the rim. Get fouled. Or take a 3. Those are the modern basketball credos.'
b'Bilas said it was possible that, after several years in which the 3-pointer has predominated in top offenses, coaches have improved at devising defenses to stymie perimeter shooting \xe2\x80\x94 in that way placing a premium on wing players who excel at close range. But mainly Williamson and Morant stand out because they are standouts.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re seeing more dunks because there are more spectacular athletes out there,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of guys can dunk, but he dunks on the way up,\xe2\x80\x9d he added of Williamson. \xe2\x80\x9cHis head is literally at or over the rim every time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Recent seasons\xe2\x80\x99 emphasis on the 3 was easy to understand if you looked to the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s discovery of the 3-pointer\xe2\x80\x99s efficiency. The Golden State Warriors emerged as a dynasty thanks in part to their high-volume 3-point shooting, and even they have been surpassed by teams like the Houston Rockets who attempt 3s at record numbers while confining their other shots to the restricted area under the basket.'
b'Meanwhile, the trey picked up a cachet that had previously been reserved only for the jam. Players who sank one from deep mimicked bow-and-arrow shots toward their benches, igniting their teammates; Stephen Curry, Hield and Young became the players youngsters aspired to play like.'
b'And to be sure, 3-pointers have not gone away. This season they account for nearly a third of the points scored in Division I, according to KenPom.com, the highest ever and part of a steady upward trajectory. Teams are making 34.3 percent of attempts, which is just a few fractions of a percent off the past couple years\xe2\x80\x99 heights.'
b'What have positively plummeted are, as Bilas suggested, midrange attempts. According to Ken Pomeroy, KenPom.com\xe2\x80\x99s proprietor, midrange shots \xe2\x80\x94 defined essentially as 2-point attempts beyond a couple feet from the basket \xe2\x80\x94 account for barely a quarter of total field goal attempts this season. That figure was 33 percent as recently as the 2012-13 season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe 15- to 20-footers are becoming extinct,\xe2\x80\x9d Pomeroy said in an interview.'
b'With players setting up farther from the basket, the dunk opportunity has opened perhaps more than ever before. And into that breach have stepped an uncommonly talented crop of dunkers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the best dunking college basketball has seen in a while,\xe2\x80\x9d said Chuck Millan, a dunk coach involved not only with high schoolers but with the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s dunk contest, which will be staged Saturday night.'
b'Millan highlighted lesser known players with sensational abilities, including Connecticut\xe2\x80\x99s Kwintin Williams, Florida Gulf Coast\xe2\x80\x99s Troy Baxter and Arkansas-Little Rock\xe2\x80\x99s Rayjon Tucker \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9ca freak of nature,\xe2\x80\x9d as Millan put it.'
b'As for Williamson and Morant, Millan said that, as with chocolate and vanilla, a comparison comes down to personal preference \xe2\x80\x94 although he may ultimately fall on Team Zion.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWith Ja, it\xe2\x80\x99s the dunks in traffic, because he\xe2\x80\x99s little, and the body contact he takes,\xe2\x80\x9d Millan said. \xe2\x80\x9cZion, being 6-8, 280, seeing him be just so agile and almost ballerina-like, being such a huge dude \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s more impressive.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Colleen and Lauren Mullen, who rose through the coaching ranks and married, have a girl and twin boys. For now, Colleen is on the sideline and Lauren is cheering and child-watching.'
b'By Kevin Armstrong'
b'ALBANY \xe2\x80\x94 Lauren Mullen pulled her black hat low over her eyes, paid $10 for a ticket and entered Sefcu Arena just before tip-off recently. She sat in Section 150. There were 18 rows between her and any other fans. She trained her focus on the two head coaches.'
b'On the visiting bench sat the University of Massachusetts, Lowell coach, Tom Garrick, a former N.B.A. player. Last spring, Mullen, then the women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach at New York University, interviewed for the position that Garrick now holds. It was the third time in four years that she had been a finalist for a Division I head-coaching job. Her r\xc3\xa9sum\xc3\xa9 included a 103-58 record and five postseason berths with the Violets.'
b'On the home sideline stood Mullen\xe2\x80\x99s wife, Colleen, the coach of SUNY Albany. Colleen got the job one month after Lauren lost out to Garrick. An associate coach at West Point for six years, Colleen reached the N.C.A.A. Division I tournament twice. When Albany hired Colleen, Lauren resigned from N.Y.U. to stay at home with their children: Maggie, 3, and their 1-year-old twins, Brennan and Callan.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you think about it, if I had gotten the Lowell job, I would\xe2\x80\x99ve been over there,\xe2\x80\x9d Lauren said, pointing to Garrick. And Colleen, she added, would have been with the children. \xe2\x80\x9cCrazy, just crazy,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 she said.'
b'It is, though, the path they are taking as a same-sex coaching couple with three small children and all sorts of demands and challenges. '
b'Indeed, Colleen joined a small sorority when Albany hired her. Although the Supreme Court approved same-sex marriage three years ago and college campuses can be among the more progressive places in the United States, Colleen says she is one of only five women she knows of who are openly gay head coaches in college basketball. She recalled how Sue Johnson, her coach at the University of New Hampshire at the time who is now the athletic director at Concord Academy in Massachusetts, came out 16 years ago, when Colleen was a senior. At the time, Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s longtime partner, Kelly, was pregnant, and Johnson informed the team of their relationship after a practice.'
b'It was the chaos familiar to a lot of dual-income households that led Lauren and Colleen to a crossroads last winter. After four years of matching basketball calendars to Colleen\xe2\x80\x99s biological clock to plan births for the off-season, timing recruiting calls around nap schedules, and wrestling with nanny problems and a merry-go-round of fill-in babysitters, they needed a change. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe were at a breaking point,\xe2\x80\x9d Colleen said. \xe2\x80\x9cA lot of coming and going.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAbsolute insanity,\xe2\x80\x9d Lauren said. \xe2\x80\x9cTo be frank, at the end of last year, it was like, \xe2\x80\x98O.K., what are we going to do?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Both 38, the Mullens knew one of them needed to get a Division I head coaching job so the other could afford to step back into a supporting role. '
b'A pact was made early on. They would not pursue the same jobs, though they had competed for employment once before. '
b'That occurred when they met, in 2007. At the time, Lauren was a graduate assistant at Lehigh. There was an opening for an assistant coaching position, and Lauren applied for the internal promotion. Colleen, then an assistant at Southern New Hampshire University, also applied. They possessed similar credentials. Colleen stood 5 feet 2 inches and had starred at the University of New Hampshire as a pass-first point guard. Lauren was 5-foot-4, and was a facilitator at Hofstra. b'That enduring failure, combined with Dolan\xe2\x80\x99s public mistreatment of some fans, has led to a growing anger and skepticism in a disaffected, if dedicated, fan base.'

b'Yet some people, including commentators on internet sites and men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball fans in real life, contend these women should be happy to have opportunities at all.'
b'This attitude rankles many W.N.B.A. players \xe2\x80\x94 that even Toliver\xe2\x80\x99s shot, let alone chances for other women with considerable experience playing and in many cases coaching, is often thought of as a one-sided benefit for those who are hired.'
b'But in many cases, the N.B.A. came calling after seeing the women excelling on their own. Toliver\xe2\x80\x99s work with the Mystics helped bring her to the attention of Wizards Coach Scott Brooks, just as Hammon got her opportunity in San Antonio because she was employed by the Silver Stars, then owned by the same group as the Spurs, and her W.N.B.A. coach, Dan Hughes, talked her up to Spurs Coach Gregg Popovich.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had a chance to put two parties together that I knew would work,\xe2\x80\x9d Hughes, now the head coach of the Seattle Storm, said. \xe2\x80\x9cI knew Becky, and I also knew Pop, and I knew that Pop, we had a lot of years of conversation about Becky. He had seen her play when I first brought her to San Antonio. So to me it was an opportunity to merge two people that would benefit from each other.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Toliver has opened up that discussion in significant ways, which she said was a large part of her reasoning for taking the job in the first place. In Hughes\xe2\x80\x99s eyes, it is nothing less than the overdue elimination of whatever combination of sexism and inertia has prevented the men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball world from taking advantage of all the talent amassed on the women\xe2\x80\x99s side of the sport, the next step toward N.B.A. teams and W.N.B.A. teams and men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s college basketball programs all hiring from the same pool of candidates.'
b'As Hughes sees it, it\xe2\x80\x99s time, not because these women deserve a chance, but because every basketball team needs more coaches like Hammon, Toliver and those who will follow.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI want a world someday where people judge coaches on how good a coach they truly are,\xe2\x80\x9d Hughes said. \xe2\x80\x9cDoesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter if they\xe2\x80\x99re male or female, doesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter their background. They can say he\xe2\x80\x99s a coach or she\xe2\x80\x99s a coach, and we can use them.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Every W.N.B.A. player who stays home instead of playing overseas in her off-season, the athletes said, is potentially one more person around which to promote the league year-round, and that player gets to rest, too. The grind of playing 12 months a year has led to W.N.B.A. players like Diana Taurasi and Angel McCoughtry taking seasons off.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou always want to protect your product,\xe2\x80\x9d January said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd the majority of our product is being run down and beaten up year-round playing this game. So when they come back around to play in the W.N.B.A., you have half of your players injured, playing through nagging things. We still find a way to have a high talent and high level of basketball, which is crazy to me.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe just have some really strong women, but that needs to be a discussion. What can we do to provide other opportunities for women to make income and prepare for the future on a real-life scale? Something they can live on. Something that makes sense.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Seth Berkman'
b'Seven years ago, Tacko Fall and Christ Koumadje were discovered by basketball scouts in a similar fashion.'
b'They were hard to miss.'
b'On the streets of Dakar, Senegal, the two 7-footers stood out. They were spotted by employees of the Flying Star Academy, a Senegalese training ground for several basketball players who have ended up on college teams in the United States. The employees chased after the teenagers, imploring them to try their enormous hands at the sport.'
b'[Follow our live coverage of the N.C.A.A. tournament here.]'
b'At the time, Koumadje, now a 7-foot-4 senior at Florida State, preferred soccer. Fall, now a 7-foot-6 senior at Central Florida, was more interested in devouring anime and manga series like \xe2\x80\x9cNaruto\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cTokyo Ghoul.\xe2\x80\x9d Both were, at first, indifferent to basketball.'
b'But their potential upside was difficult to ignore. To onlookers, they evoked thoughts of the next Hakeem Olajuwon or Yao Ming.'
b'Today, their size offers less promise. They toiled to become giant forces in the paint, only to watch as basketball evolved from a game that coveted height into a more freewheeling, 3-point-centric game that deems their skill sets nearly as obsolete as a fax machine: nice to have, but no longer entirely necessary.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s interesting about both, their advanced analytics, they play off the charts \xe2\x80\x94 well over 1 point per possession, and that\xe2\x80\x99s really effective in college basketball,\xe2\x80\x9d said Steve Kyler, the editor and publisher of Basketball Insiders, which produces weekly N.B.A. mock drafts. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen you dig deeper, in situational-type things they grade really well, but the truth of the matter is the N.B.A. game isn\xe2\x80\x99t played that way anymore. It\xe2\x80\x99s all about stretch 5s, quickness.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think they may get a look on the fringe based off their size,\xe2\x80\x9d Kyler added. \xe2\x80\x9cBut a guy 7-foot-6 being the first overall pick or top five is pretty rare now.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the college game, where height can still create a tangible advantage, Fall and Koumadje \xe2\x80\x94 who are among the tallest players currently in Division I \xe2\x80\x94 will be crucial cogs in their teams\xe2\x80\x99 N.C.A.A. tournament performance.'
b'Beyond that, whether they can find a place and purpose in the N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 where the only active players who stand 7-foot-3 or taller are Dallas\xe2\x80\x99s Kristaps Porzingis, who has a far more diverse skill set, and Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s Boban Marjanovic \xe2\x80\x94 remains to be seen.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cExtending my range is something I definitely want to work on,\xe2\x80\x9d said Fall, who helped the Knights earn their first N.C.A.A. tournament berth since 2005 by averaging nearly 11 points and 7 rebounds a game. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not going to go out there and shoot 3s like a lot of bigs do now, but pick my spots.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBut I feel like no matter how the game has changed, you still need somebody down low to do some damage.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Basketball academies in Senegal like Flying Star now regularly send players abroad. After playing for a few months at the academy, Fall got a chance to join a high school team in the United States. His mother reluctantly let her son go, hoping he would receive a better education.'
b'Extremely raw when he arrived at Liberty Christian Preparatory School in Tavares, Fla., Fall almost quit basketball. But he refined his game while playing on a travel team alongside Ben Simmons, now with the Philadelphia 76ers. Fall also trained in Houston with Olajuwon, a Hall of Famer who emphasized the importance of footwork for a center his size.'
b'Occasionally, Fall watched Simmons at nearby Montverde Academy, where Koumadje landed after coming to the United States. Fall and Koumadje only briefly overlapped in Dakar \xe2\x80\x94 Koumadje is originally from Chad \xe2\x80\x94 but in high school they talked on the phone or via Facebook. Their discussions rarely veered into basketball. Instead, they commiserated about the difficulties of adjusting to life when you are over 7 feet tall and 4,500 miles from home.'
b'Koumadje, like Fall, grasps the unlikelihood that he will develop into a free-shooting N.B.A. big man. Before his senior year in high school, he played pickup games at the University of Southern California with Andre Drummond of the Detroit Pistons. It was then, Koumadje said, that he realized he was more effective cemented in the post.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe game is evolving and that\xe2\x80\x99s what people want,\xe2\x80\x9d said Koumadje, a two-year starter who led the Seminoles in blocked shots this season. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I play to my strength. That\xe2\x80\x99s what I do.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Fall\xe2\x80\x99s turning point came after his sophomore season at Central Florida, when he contemplated entering the 2017 N.B.A. draft. Five teams told him he needed vast improvement adapting to the speed of the pros, particularly in guarding pick-and-rolls.'
b'Central Florida Coach Johnny Dawkins \xe2\x80\x94 a former Duke guard who played with the towering centers Shawn Bradley and Manute Bol in the N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 was hired before Fall\xe2\x80\x99s sophomore year, and created a three-year plan for him. Increasing mobility and stamina came first, followed by catching the ball down low and learning to work out of double and triple teams. This season, Dawkins has moved Fall farther out on the perimeter defensively.'
b'Wherever he stands, Fall often forces opposing players to elevate more when they shoot, to get the ball over his arms.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOur floaters have to be a little bit higher, and it probably screwed a couple of guys up,\xe2\x80\x9d Fran Dunphy, Temple\xe2\x80\x99s coach at the time, said after a game against Central Florida on March 9.'
b'Teams have tried less inventive strategies to bypass Fall\xe2\x80\x99s 8-foot-4 wingspan. Fall, who is bulkier than Bol or Bradley, said that he had heard opposing coaches tell players to go after his knees.'
b'Though he is all but assured of breaking the Division I record for career field-goal percentage \xe2\x80\x94 he currently shoots over 74 percent; the record is 67.8 \xe2\x80\x94 Fall converts only 36 percent of his free throws. Fall \xe2\x80\x94 whose hands are 10\xc2\xbd inches long \xe2\x80\x94 said that when he shoots free throws it feels as if he is holding a volleyball.'
b"His shooting form, which involves using only his right hand while flinging his left arm in the air and then slouching, has drawn derisive comments on social media, where he is sometimes treated as a sideshow. After Fall had 13 points and 10 rebounds in a win over Houston that ended the Cougars' 33-game home winning streak, Fall got more attention for a GIF that showed him holding the ball over an opponent\xe2\x80\x99s head like an older brother playing keep-away."
b'Fall and Koumadje are accustomed to stares in airports and snide remarks from opposing fans. b'Koumadje said he would eventually like to work for the United Nations, helping refugees in Chad. Fall wants to become an engineer.'

b'SACRAMENTO \xe2\x80\x94 The Boston Celtics were not in a good place when they boarded a plane bound for California on Sunday. b'But after some reflection and conversation, the Celtics regained a bit of their swagger with back-to-back wins this week against the Golden State Warriors and the Sacramento Kings. b'Such uncertainty does not make Irving unique in the modern N.B.A. \xe2\x80\x94 Kevin Durant of the Warriors and Kawhi Leonard of the Toronto Raptors are among the other stars who will weigh big decisions in free agency this summer \xe2\x80\x94 but the Celtics have let the noise affect them.'

b'Yet Connelly pointed out that as fluky as skeptics might find the Nuggets\xe2\x80\x99 No. 2 seed, team officials set three fairly lofty goals before the season started. Then they watched this group, largely assembled through Denver\xe2\x80\x99s own shrewd drafting and trading, reach them all.'
b'End the playoff drought? Check.'
b'Win the Northwest Division? Check.'
b'Secure a top-four seed and home-court advantage in the first round of the postseason?'
b'Check.'
b'The next step was making sure they didn\xe2\x80\x99t spoil all that by falling into an 0-2 hole to San Antonio with two home defeats, which is the sort of deficit only four teams in league history have managed to erase. b'The Nuggets have only three players (Millsap, Barton and Mason Plumlee) who appeared in a playoff game before Game 1 of this series, and they acknowledge it\xe2\x80\x99s an obstacle, especially against a team that can carry out a game plan like the Spurs.'

b'By Richard Goldstein'
b'Cal Ramsey, a presence on the New York basketball scene for more than a half-century, who starred at New York University in the 1950s, played briefly for the Knicks and remained with them as a longtime broadcaster and community relations representative, died on Monday in Manhattan. He was 81.'
b'The Knicks announced his death, at a rehabilitation center. He had been in poor health in recent years.'
b'Ramsey, who had lived in Harlem since he was young, began honing his skills on the playground courts of the Rucker League, which has attracted some of the game\xe2\x80\x99s greatest players over the years.'
b'He first appeared at Madison Square Garden while playing for Commerce High School of Manhattan. He played at the Garden for three seasons as a forward at N.Y.U., where he was a teammate of the future Boston Celtic forward Tom Sanders. He is 11th on the leading scorers list for N.Y.U. with 1,275 points.'
b'Ramsey was selected in the second round of the 1959 N.B.A. draft by the St. Louis Hawks. At 6 feet 4 inches, he was an outstanding rebounder with a good shooting touch, but he came to be considered too small as a forward and not good enough as a dribbler to excel at guard.'
b'He played in only four games with the Hawks and seven with the Knicks in the 1959-60 season, then in two games with the Syracuse Nationals, the forerunners of the Philadelphia 76ers, in 1960-61.'
b'Ramsey may have faced another obstacle in the N.B.A. that had little to do with his skills. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve been told at the time there was a quota system in the league,\xe2\x80\x9d in which teams \xe2\x80\x9cmay have wanted only two or three blacks,\xe2\x80\x9d Ramsey told Charles Salzberg for the oral history \xe2\x80\x9cFrom Set Shot to Slam Dunk\xe2\x80\x9d (1987).'
b'After Ramsey\xe2\x80\x99s stint with Syracuse, he went to the semipro Eastern League but incurred a severe knee injury in his third season with the circuit. It ended his playing career.'
b'Ramsey was born on July 13, 1937, in Selma, Ala. He was a teacher in New York after his playing days, having received a bachelor\xe2\x80\x99s degree from N.Y.U.'
b'He was a color analyst for Knicks broadcasts from 1972 to 1982, then rejoined the team as a community representative in 1991. He was also an assistant basketball coach at N.Y.U., which had become a Division III team, from 1983 until the past season. He served N.Y.U. as assistant director of community relations for 20 years and received the N.Y.U. President\xe2\x80\x99s Alumni Achievement Award in 2004.'
b'Information on his survivors was not immediately available.'
b'James L. Dolan, the Knicks\xe2\x80\x99 owner, said in a statement that Ramsey \xe2\x80\x9cwill be remembered for the thousands of young lives he influenced as a community leader.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A case in point involved Al Barden, who, after starring for Boys High School in Brooklyn (now Boys and Girls), was recruited to N.Y.U. by Ramsey while he was playing there.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAl was a tough kid with a habit of getting into some trouble,\xe2\x80\x9d Ramsey told Harvey Araton of The New York Times in 2009. \xe2\x80\x9cSo I stayed on him, made sure he was going to class, doing the things he needed to stay eligible.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Barden\xe2\x80\x99s basketball career was over, Ramsey, mindful of the problems athletes have in transitioning to a new phase of life, hired Barden as his replacement to direct a high school program for at-risk students. They remained friends through the years.'
b'One day, Barden, living in California, phoned Ramsey to tell him of the birth of his son, whom he had named Ramses, ostensibly for the pharaohs of ancient Egypt as a symbol of everlasting strength.'
b'But there was more to it than that.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cReplace the \xe2\x80\x98s\xe2\x80\x99 with a \xe2\x80\x98y\xe2\x80\x99 and what does it spell?\xe2\x80\x9d Barden asked Ramsey. \xe2\x80\x9cI really named him for you.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In June 2009, the Giants selected Ramses Barden, a receiver from Cal Poly, in the third round of the N.F.L. draft, and he spent four seasons with them.'
b'When Ramses was drafted, Al Barden, speaking to The Times, said of Cal Ramsey, \xe2\x80\x9cHe could get you to do anything just because of who he was: someone you just had to respect.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'An earlier version of a picture caption with this obituary misidentified when Ramsey played for the Knicks. As the obituary correctly states, it was the 1959-60 season, not 1960-61.'

b'By Peter S. Goodman'
b'LONDON \xe2\x80\x94 In theory at least, we understand the words on the sports radio we hear incessantly \xe2\x80\x94 in taxis, at the fish and chips place, at the corner newsstand. But we are foreigners here and the stories are inscrutable, full of happenings from cricket ovals and rugby pitches.'
b'Our sports focus is confined to our darkened living room, where my 7-year-old son, Leo, and I have lately been absorbing improbable happenings from the other side of the Atlantic \xe2\x80\x94 one exhilarating victory after another for our suddenly mighty Brooklyn Nets.'
b'This has become our early-morning ritual. Wife and daughter still asleep, the boys watch the action from the night before, the scores carefully hidden from our N.B.A. League Pass app lest we ruin the ending.'
b'We are basketball expatriates, two steps removed from the initial source of my N.B.A. obsession by a change of team loyalties and a move to London.'
b'In our North London surroundings, we may as well be rooting for a badminton team from Bhutan. While the odd LeBron James jersey can be spotted, our Brooklyn Nets gear seemingly fades into the sea of Yankees caps brought home by tourists returning from New York (oblivious to the hate they are inspiring from this Mets fan) and the endless Brooklyn-related mumbo jumbo that now adorns T-shirts worldwide.'
b'[Nets\xe2\x80\x99 Run to the Playoffs Hits a Snag With Spencer Dinwiddie Injury]'
b'While N.F.L. gear is a common sighting, owing to the constant staging of American football games here, N.B.A. basketball is largely invisible. One imagines this was unaltered by the recent showdown of two of the league\xe2\x80\x99s most dreadful teams, the Knicks and the Washington Wizards, inside London\xe2\x80\x99s unlovable O2 arena. (We did not attend, just as we do not take leisure trips to see the dentist.)'
b'Our sports-related conversations with Britons tend to revolve around the astronomical ticket prices required to see Arsenal, the English Premier League soccer team Leo has decided that we love forever. Our Nets fandom is like membership in a secret society, whose disclosure would mark us as eccentric and produce puzzlement.'
b'Even my Knick fan friends back in New York do not want to hear about the Nets via email. My only real communion comes via obscure Nets-related podcasts I listen to while washing the dishes. When Bill Simmons and Zach Lowe devoted perhaps 3 minutes of a recent pod to the Nets surge, I confess to feelings of pride and validation I can only liken to a U.F.O. conspiracy theorist hearing that the government is probing the sighting of a flying saucer.'
b'My embrace of the Nets began seven years ago when the Knicks \xe2\x80\x94 the only team I had ever rooted for \xe2\x80\x94 shunned a gift from the basketball gods by letting Jeremy Lin leave town. It was the final indignity after years of atrocious basketball. I dumped my Knicks season tickets and adopted the fledgling club whose arena had just risen over my Brooklyn neighborhood.'
b'I did not do so lightly. As a born-and-bred New Yorker, I saw abandoning a team as a serious breach of the tribal code. I disdained fans from other cities who rooted for two teams in the same sport. I was unremittingly harsh to the worst transgressor of all: the bandwagon fan. (If that Steph Curry jersey you own was the first Warriors gear in your closet, yes, I\xe2\x80\x99m talking about you.)'
b'But I was hopping on no bandwagon. With the exception of a pair of distant trips to the N.B.A. finals, the New Jersey-turned-Brooklyn Nets were a pathetic franchise. I was living in Brooklyn. My father had grown up in Queens and traveled on a streetcar to watch the Dodgers at Ebbets Field. I was not abandoning my tribe. I was returning to it.'
b'This is what I told myself as I began reading about the odd collection of players I was now rooting for, trying to divine the narrative that would make it real. I fought through a sense of exile in the slick, new Barclays Center, which was full of fans for whom the game itself appeared peripheral to the cool Brooklyn food, the dancing during timeouts, and whatever fascinating things were happening on their phones.'
b'Yes, it was a gorgeous arena with excellent sightlines and welcoming staff. The season tickets I bought the day the Knicks said goodbye to J-Lin put me in seats that were a 10-minute walk from my house in Prospect Heights. Madison Square Garden was a cramped dump reached via a creaking subway and a walk through the bowels of Penn Station.'
b'Yet there was something about the Garden, even as the Dolan era yielded a lost decade of basketball. The crowd understood. Hustle plays drew appreciation in an arena that had revered Charles Oakley. The energy was electric.'
b'In Brooklyn, the mostly mercenary fans got what we deserved: a team of past-their-prime castoffs imported by the bombastic Russian magnate, Mikhail Prokhorov, who had brought the franchise to Brooklyn. Vowing to spend whatever it took to eclipse the Knicks \xe2\x80\x94 a low bar \xe2\x80\x94 he built a bonfire of money at the corner of Flatbush and Atlantic.'
b'In came the wildly overpaid Joe Johnson, a seven-time All-Star. In came the mediocre Gerald Wallace in exchange for a first-round pick that Portland turned into Damian Lillard. The centerpiece was the sullen, out-of-shape Deron Williams who, in another lifetime, looked like the best point guard on earth, and whose passions no longer appeared to include basketball.'
b'They fit uneasily around the likable 7-footer, Brook Lopez, whose sweet shooting came along with rebounding and defensive skills that seemed better suited for other pursuits, like calligraphy.'
b'My history as a Knicks fan made the plan feel familiar. Win now, baby! The future was for losers. The oligarch was buying his way to competitiveness pronto. Leaving no doubt, the Nets soon traded every first-round pick until the sun dies for the remains of Paul Pierce and Kevin Garnett.'
b'When it all unraveled and the Nets descended into an unwatchable state, I hung in. You can not renounce the team of your life and then walk away from your new one because they are terrible. Real fandom is forged in suffering. Even when my family traded Brooklyn for London in 2016, we remained Nets fans.'
b'This happily coincided with another development: The Nets bucked the conventional wisdom that New York fans will not accept rebuilding and embraced patience.'
b'Sean Marks, the general manager, somehow turned a collection of mostly indifferent veterans into a raffish crew of young, hungry players led by a first-time head coach, Kenny Atkinson. They run at a ferocious pace, share the ball with grace, and play with joy.'
b'Since an excruciating eight-game losing streak, the Nets have won 18 of 23. Even from afar, we can tell that the intensity has changed at the Barclays, the Brooook-Lyyyyn chants filling our London living room.'
b'And still, an intense New York team deserves better. Back for the holidays, I took Leo to see New Orleans and their marquee star, Anthony Davis, at Barclays. The place was packed with tourists who seemed intent on taking selfies and buying Brooklyn gear at the swag shop.'
b'Whatever.'
b'On Saturday morning, we will sit on the couch in our pajamas, Leo and me, and see what happened against the now-hated, if pitiful, Knicks the night before.'
b'Please don\xe2\x80\x99t tell us who won.'

b'By Alex Wong'
b'Nathaniel Butler has been an N.B.A. senior photographer since 1984. Those were the days of shooting on film and developing photos in hotel rooms after games. Today, players text Butler as they arrive at the arena so he can be in position to capture a perfect arena entrance shot for them to post on Instagram.'
b'The job isn\xe2\x80\x99t what it used to be.'
b'When Andrew D. Bernstein became an official N.B.A. photographer in 1986, he was continually thwarted in his attempts to get his camera into in-game huddles to capture the interactions between players and coaches. Pat Riley, who was the coach of the Los Angeles Lakers, made sure to obscure all viewpoints.'
b'Halfway through the season, Riley asked Bernstein why he wanted to be in the huddle. People want to see what\xe2\x80\x99s happening on the inside, Bernstein told Riley, who agreed to give Bernstein a chance. If you screw up, Riley said, you are never coming back.'
b'More than three decades later, Bernstein is still photographing N.B.A. players, huddles and pretty much whatever he pleases as the league\xe2\x80\x99s longest tenured senior photographer.'
b'Photographers have long played a critical role in shaping narratives in a league defined by faces and moments. The most iconic posters are the finished works of the photographers who position themselves along the baseline each game, often contorting their bodies and forgetting about personal comfort to get closer and take countless snaps, in hopes of capturing a masterpiece.'
b'In today\xe2\x80\x99s N.B.A., they allow players to use those photographs as building blocks for their social media profiles. They have adapted to an ever-changing digital world that has presented new opportunities and a whole new set of challenges.'
b'On game day, Butler uses a combination of tethered remotes and custom phone apps to operate any number of cameras in an arena.'
b'He sends photographs to a team of editors in Secaucus, N.J., with the press of a button. In seconds, they can be published on the league\xe2\x80\x99s official social media feeds and reach millions of people around the world.'
b'Despite the technological advances, shooting an N.B.A. game can be more difficult than one would think. \xe2\x80\x9cA basketball game is a complex situation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Bruce Ely, the lead photographer of the Portland Trail Blazers. \xe2\x80\x9cThere are a lot of moving parts.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Like a fan\xe2\x80\x99s arms waving across the frame just as Damian Lillard makes a 3-pointer. Or the leg of another player sneaking into the edge of the image, ruining a portrait. Another time, it might be a referee walking into a perfect shot.'
b'Despite the challenges, some N.B.A. photographers do not consider it their most difficult assignment. Nelson Campana, who photographs the Raptors as an employee of Maple Leaf Sports and Entertainment, which owns the team, regularly shoots weddings as well. The pressure of game night is nothing compared with the responsibility of chronicling a couple\xe2\x80\x99s special day.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou have one night to make it right,\xe2\x80\x9d Campana said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a list of things you need to get, and you don\xe2\x80\x99t get another chance. At a basketball game, you\xe2\x80\x99re just hoping things happen.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Some nights, there is too much happening at the same time. As the Oklahoma City Thunder eliminated the San Antonio Spurs in the 2016 playoffs, Butler had to make a split-second decision about what to photograph at the buzzer. He focused on Kevin Durant and Russell Westbrook embracing, and then got a shot of Durant with Tim Duncan. He stayed with Durant afterward, but that meant missing a chance to capture Duncan walking off an N.B.A. court for the final time.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIdeally,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said, \xe2\x80\x9cI would like to be in two places at one time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'While some players enjoy being on the other side of these photographers\xe2\x80\x99 lenses, others say it is an adjustment. Aaron Gordon of the Orlando Magic first remembers being in front of a camera as a high schooler being interviewed after winning a basketball tournament.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou have to live in a way where you\xe2\x80\x99re O.K. with being seen,\xe2\x80\x9d Gordon said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re always being watched these days.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'To take more control over their visual narratives on social media, players are working with photographers to shoot them outside basketball arenas.'

b'The trouble began harmlessly enough over the summer, when Davenport represented the United States at the FIBA Under-18 Women\xe2\x80\x99s Americas Championship in Mexico City. She led the team in rebounding and blocks as it won gold.'
b'U.S.A. Basketball compensates players who compete on national teams to make up for wages they could have earned working summer jobs rather than practicing or competing. The N.C.A.A. allows college athletes to accept those payments. It calls them broken-time payments.'
b'For players with high school eligibility remaining, U.S.A. Basketball typically inquires with individual state high school athletics associations to see if the payments can be accepted. Policies can vary by state.'
b'In this case, because of what Craig Miller, a spokesman for U.S.A. Basketball, termed a clerical error, nobody checked with the state high school athletic associations for the three players on the under-18 team with high school eligibility remaining. U.S.A. Basketball sent checks for $857.20 to Davenport and every other player on the team. On Aug. 27, Mario Davenport, Maori\xe2\x80\x99s father, received it. Two days later, she cashed it.'
b'Two months later, U.S.A. Basketball realized the error. In November, an employee called the Alabama athletics association, which told the U.S.A. Basketball employee that under Alabama rules, athletes could accept broken-time payments only if the value was less than $200. On Nov. 26, a U.S.A. Basketball official called Davenport\xe2\x80\x99s mother, Tara Davenport, and informed her that Maori was not allowed to accept the stipend. The next day, Tara Davenport reported the violation to the state association and informed Charles Henderson High School officials, and on Nov. 28 she repaid U.S.A. Basketball.'
b'Two days later, the state ruled Davenport ineligible for the rest of the season. Two appeals boards have upheld the ruling.'
b'On Wednesday afternoon, Tara Davenport said she hoped attention from the news media, as well as pressure from Alabama politicians, would convince the association to change the ruling. The Alabama House Republican Caucus unanimously approved a resolution supporting Maori Davenport, and its members were among the many local politicians supporting her. If the association\xe2\x80\x99s officials were unwilling to change their ruling, Tara Davenport was prepared to take the next step.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf they don\xe2\x80\x99t, we are definitely going to take some legal action to try to help get her on the court,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. The next day, she and Mario Davenport filed a lawsuit in Pike County Circuit Court seeking their daughter\xe2\x80\x99s reinstatement.'
b'Since Maori Davenport\xe2\x80\x99s final appeal was denied in December, attention and pressure had been building.'
b'The story gained national attention recently after Jay Bilas, an ESPN college basketball analyst who was once called \xe2\x80\x9cthe N.C.A.A.\xe2\x80\x99s most dangerous critic,\xe2\x80\x9d wrote a column blistering Steve Savarese, the executive director for the state athletic association. Bilas accused Savarese of \xe2\x80\x9cblindly asserting authority without regard for whom it may hurt, or the reasonable likelihood of a similar issue recurring in the future.\xe2\x80\x9d On Thursday, the tennis legend Billie Jean King joined the N.B.A. star DeMarcus Cousins and a chorus of others in voicing their support for the player.'
b'The association did not immediately respond to a request for comment on the judge\xe2\x80\x99s ruling, and earlier in the week it declined to make Savarese available for an interview. On Tuesday, Johnny Hardin, the president of the association\xe2\x80\x99s Central Board of Control \xe2\x80\x94 which heard and denied Davenport\xe2\x80\x99s final appeal \xe2\x80\x94 released a statement asserting that \xe2\x80\x9cfacts involved in the ruling have either been misstated or ignored.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'According to Brock Kelley, the Charles Henderson High School principal, it is the association\xe2\x80\x99s facts that are misleading.'
b'Hardin\xe2\x80\x99s statement says that Tara Davenport is a certified basketball coach and therefore should know the eligibility rules. Kelley wrote in an email that Tara Davenport, who is a fifth-grade teacher, coaches middle school basketball, for which there is no rules test. Hardin\xe2\x80\x99s statement says Kelley has not attended an association rules conference for the past three years. Kelley wrote that his school\xe2\x80\x99s athletic director had attended each one and that the amateurism rule had not been covered at the last meeting.'
b'Tara Davenport emphasized that neither she nor her daughter had hidden the check. They simply thought that U.S.A. Basketball had done its due diligence and that they could accept it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI reported it as soon as I knew that Maori wasn\xe2\x80\x99t supposed to have it,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Kelley, the high school principal, and Miller, the U.S.A. Basketball spokesman, focused on how institutionalized the payments are. After U.S.A. Basketball sent the check but before Tara Davenport received it, Kelley wrote, she received a call from Jeff Walz. Walz is the women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach at the University of Louisville and was also the coach of the United States under-18 team. Walz asked Tara Davenport if she had received the check yet. She said she had not and asked whether Maori could accept it. Walz told her that she was allowed to and that it was permitted by the N.C.A.A.'
b'Louisville officials did not respond to a request to comment.'
b'In Maori Davenport\xe2\x80\x99s absence, the Charles Henderson girls basketball team has won all but two games and is the top-ranked 5A team in the state. Davenport is attending school, going to practices and working on her game with an outside trainer. She said she was focusing on ball-handling skills and other drills that would allow her to play more as a wing.'
b'On Friday night, she will get her first opportunity to show off those newly developed skills in a competitive game.'
