b'Sometime in the third quarter, as the Philadelphia 76ers rained down 3-pointers like mortar shots and Ben Simmons, a giant point guard possessed of preternatural passing ability and a bricklayer\xe2\x80\x99s touch, carved through the Nets, a thought occurred:'
b'This was not the playoff homecoming of the Nets\xe2\x80\x99 dreams.'
b'The Nets tried but never really contended Thursday night. The men from Philadelphia simply had too much talent and too many big bodies on their way to a 2-1 first-round series lead, and that was a shame. Saddled with the worst attendance in the N.B.A. this season, Barclays Center in Brooklyn was packed to the gills with fans waving towels and hooting and yelling. The joint was packed and joyfully rocking.'
b'The Nets are a pretty good pro hoops team in a city where terrible often rules the roost. Their coach, Kenny Atkinson, a likable and intelligent basketball lifer, took over a team that was expected to dwell in the cellar and won more games, 42, than it lost, 40, this season.'
b'That was in contrast to the disaster masquerading as a basketball team at Madison Square Garden, where the Knicks\xe2\x80\x99 management team crafted a grotesquely bad team that finished 17-65. (Losing no longer impresses because the Knicks have posted losing records in 15 of the last 18 years.) In a sign that God may have a strange sense of humor, those same Knicks are widely rumored to be a favorite to gain the services of the brilliant forward Kevin Durant, who can become a free agent this summer.'
b'But enough about that other New York team.'
b'After falling into a deep ditch under previous management, the Brooklyn Nets have executed a slow, steady rebuild, instilling discipline and a sense of Nets basketball, which is to say a fluid, slashing style that relies on small forwards and guards bolstered by lean, swift centers who block shots and rebound and run. Their general manager, Sean Marks, a former San Antonio Spurs assistant and executive, has picked up talented role players much as a fishmonger sorts through a barrel and plucks out tasty sea bass.'
b'The Nets have a fine quartet of guards and small forwards, D\xe2\x80\x99Angelo Russell and Spencer Dinwiddie, Joe Harris and Caris LeVert, creative players all, who can probe and find seams in defenses and stroke jump shots.'
b'So this game on Thursday offered a chance to draw the measure of a Nets team rising more quickly than expected and of a Sixers team that hopes to compete for a championship. On that last point I walked away nursing doubts.'
b'The Sixers for six years were an experimental laboratory, their former general manager Sam Hinkie occupying a reputational land between supposed genius and madman. They lost intentionally and insistently, and accumulated top draft picks, not the least the 6-foot-10 point guard Simmons and the splendidly talented big man Joel Embiid. Sixers ownership eventually discarded Hinkie. But that team now is expected to contend, and the current general manager made a series of trades toward that end this season.'
b'Yet a week into playoff season, the engine of that 76ers machine is coughing. Embiid has come up with a chronically sore knee. That is a problem for any athlete, much less a 7-foot, 270-pound center. The assumption Thursday night was that he would play, an impression reinforced when Embiid took the court an hour before the game and shot around. He shot fadeaways and spun like a dervish and put up graceful hook shots.'
b'Then minutes before tipoff, the 76ers\xe2\x80\x99 coaches shook their heads. Nope, his knee was too sore. Embiid was sitting. That left the big man in a bad mood. Moments before the tip, as teammates walked over to dap him up and slap his back, Embiid could barely look at them or the court.'
b'Simmons is no less talented, and perhaps more baffling. He is a brilliant athlete with stunning vision and dribbling ability. When he breaks swiftly into the open court, his passing takes on a sleight-of-hand quality, so quick that you notice the ball only as it lands in the hands of a teammate.'
b'Alas, his shooting edges toward disastrous, and his confidence in it is sodden. Rather than put his hand under the ball, he puts it off to the side, his left elbow sticking out like a chicken wing. He practices his shooting before games with often unsightly results. On Thursday evening, he stood in the corner and took pass after pass from an assistant coach and shot and shot. He made, by my count, five baskets in 15 attempts. Then he took 3-point shots from the shoulder of the key, going 1 for 6.'
b'You wanted to cover your eyes and suggest that maybe he should stick to layups. Yet by shooting layups and hook shots and dunks, he finished the game with 31 points and 9 assists.'
b'He is the best fundamentally unsound player in the N.B.A. And you wonder how this still unformed 22-year-old star and a gimpy-knee center can stumble into the N.B.A. finals.'
b'In a strange way, on this night, Embiid\xe2\x80\x99s absence liberated his teammates. They shot 40 percent from 3-point range to the Nets\xe2\x80\x99 20 percent, and they outrebounded them, too.'
b'If the 76ers have a playoff advantage, it may reside with their veteran talent, in particular Tobias Harris, Jimmy Butler and J.J. Redick. During a Nets run late in the third quarter, Philadelphia Coach Brett Brown called a timeout and drew up a play. Then you saw Redick stand up and start talking and pointing. Then Butler leaned in and interjected. Brown fell silent, then nodded in agreement. Fine, he said, we\xe2\x80\x99ll run it differently.'
b'As they walked out onto the court after the timeout, Butler and Redick kept talking, resembling two professors discussing a knotty physics problem. \xe2\x80\x9cThat was pros talking to pros,\xe2\x80\x9d Brown said later.'
b'The Nets are a young crew, not unduly burdened by egos and attitude. But they are not yet at a pros-talking-to-pros level. They are a promising troupe still in search of a leading man.'

b'He had become \xe2\x80\x98that guy,\xe2\x80\x99 the player left wide open during pickup basketball. So he enlisted the help of his 10-year-old son\xe2\x80\x99s coach.'

b'Supported by'
b'By Nik Mittal'
b'Photographs and Video by Jonah Markowitz'
b'I was 8 years old when my parents \xe2\x80\x94 both graduate students from India \xe2\x80\x94 moved from married student housing to a little home in Raleigh, N.C., with a basketball hoop in the backyard. Even as an immigrant from South Asia, I knew what that hoop meant.'
b'Basketball is a religion in North Carolina, and I quickly became a disciple. When I was 11, the N.C. State Wolfpack won the N.C.A.A. championship in heart-stopping fashion. I still remember my dad taking me to the center of campus for the midnight celebration and being transfixed by the sheer size and emotion of it.'
b'My love for the game soon became an obsession. I taught myself to shoot in the backyard and played against the neighborhood kids. I learned to make up for my disadvantages on the court \xe2\x80\x94 both real (I\xe2\x80\x99m definitely undersized) and perceived (no one expected a short Indian kid to be any good) \xe2\x80\x94 through hustle and perfecting a low left-handed heave that I used whenever I could beat my man into the lane.'
b'My crowning achievement came in the final seconds of a Little League championship game, when I went to the free-throw line with my team down a point. Both shots clanked around the rim but went in.'
b'In college, watching the sport became equally addictive \xe2\x80\x94 especially now that I was at UNC-Chapel Hill. My senior year, the Tar Heels won their fourth N.C.A.A. Championship.'
b'Now, at age 47, I am a New York City dad who watches Carolina basketball obsessively with his three sons and who, after a 15 year hiatus (thanks to a couple of knee surgeries) decided to play pickup again. But on the court recently, I came to a shocking realization.'
b'My ugly but effective left-handed heave was no longer effective. I had become the player in the pickup game who everyone leaves open from a distance.'
b'Call it ego, but I really didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to be that guy. So I turned to the only expert I knew \xe2\x80\x94 my 10-year-old son\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach.'
b'Macky Bergman, 35, runs Steady Buckets, a nonprofit that teaches more than 1,000 boys and girls from around the city. Coach Macky, as everyone calls him, is a product of New York City basketball \xe2\x80\x94 he was a star player at Bronx Science and played four years at the University of Rochester. He assured me that anyone could learn to shoot if they put the time in.'
b'But could a middle-aged, undersized father of three really remake his jump shot and become a solid pickup basketball player again?'
b'Coach Macky and I met in early October on a typical outdoor court \xe2\x80\x94 fenced-in blacktop, metal backboards, rims with no nets \xe2\x80\x94 on Second Avenue and 19th Street. It was 8 a.m. on a weekday, so the place was vacant, except for a grousing tenant who lived near the court and asked us to practice as far away from his home as possible. This somewhat safe space meant I could relax a little, although the pressure was still on, as both Macky and the Times photographer, sent to track my progress, were both former college players.'
b'We began with a shooting test: a series of midrange and 3-point jumpers while moving between five spots on the court. I did this 10 times, shooting 10 free throws after each round. By the end I was drenched in sweat.'
b'The results weren\xe2\x80\x99t great \xe2\x80\x94 62 percent from the free-throw line, 49 percent on 2-point jumpers and an abysmal 30 percent from the 3-point line. As for my self-taught shooting technique, which even my son, Kavi, had described as \xe2\x80\x9cpretty ugly,\xe2\x80\x9d Coach Macky decided we would have to start over from scratch.'
b'In our first few sessions, we set about erasing the muscle memory of 1983 to develop proper form. We started as close to the basket as possible \xe2\x80\x94 almost directly under the rim.'
b'The ball was to be perched just above my eyes, on the fingertips of my left hand, directly underneath the right angle at the bend of my elbow. My guide hand would hold the right side of the ball.'
b'For my lower body: knees bent, feet shoulder-width apart, weight on the balls of my feet. Then I was to push the ball up \xe2\x80\x94 not out \xe2\x80\x94 release and follow through, fingers pointed down.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOn the follow-through, Kobe sometimes joins his thumb and index finger, and his guide hand points at the basket,\xe2\x80\x9d Macky would say. \xe2\x80\x9cSteph Curry\xe2\x80\x99s guide hand flips out and his arms come together.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The more shots I took \xe2\x80\x94 the goal was 100 baskets in a row \xe2\x80\x94 the more I could feel myself adapting. Set, shoot, follow-through. Take one step forward and catch the ball as it comes through the net. Repeat. It was surprisingly meditative. Before I knew it, I had made it all the way to 88 shots in a row.'
b'But Macky had identified some weaknesses.'
b'For one, I was landing with one leg practically a foot in front of the other. Macky had me stick a soccer ball between my legs and practice a series of jump shots while squeezing it between my knees.'
b'This was surprisingly hard \xe2\x80\x94 either I\xe2\x80\x99d brick the shot, or the soccer ball would pop out \xe2\x80\x94 until I focused on taking really small jumps, landing like I was on train tracks. Kavi even sort of complimented me, calling this an \xe2\x80\x9cadvanced drill\xe2\x80\x9d that only the teenagers do.'
b'Coach Macky encouraged me to attend his weekly shooting clinic at a high school on the Lower East Side with about two dozen of his other students. They were all between 8 and 14 years old, including my son.'
b'I tried to blend in by standing with the coaches. That didn\xe2\x80\x99t last long. When Macky assigned me to work with one of them, Torrence Ested, the first thing Coach Torrence said to me was, \xe2\x80\x9cI got you old man.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When I asked Kavi who he thought was more embarrassed by the whole venture \xe2\x80\x94 me or him \xe2\x80\x94 his vague reply spoke volumes. \xe2\x80\x9cTough to say,\xe2\x80\x9d he responded.'
b'For the final lessons, Coach Macky moved me out to the 3-point line. I\xe2\x80\x99d never been comfortable shooting the three. Because my old jump shot was a heave that began at the chest, it was all arms and no legs.'
b'As it turned out, I\xe2\x80\x99d been learning how to be a better 3-point shooter all along. Proper technique and good arc make for a more accurate shot, regardless of distance.'
b'The difference was clear in my final set of drills. I shot above 70 percent from the free throw line, 65 percent on my two pointers, and a remarkably improved 55 percent from 3-point range.'
b'But improving my stats was never really the point. I\xe2\x80\x99ve started hooping again at the McBurney YMCA on West 14th Street and reconnecting with the sport I\xe2\x80\x99ve loved since I was a kid practicing in the backyard. My jumper is still a work in progress, but I\xe2\x80\x99m not being left wide open on it anymore.'
b'At a recent pickup session \xe2\x80\x94 with adults, this time \xe2\x80\x94 I was shooting for the last spot in the next game and was matched against the best shooter in our group. We both made our first two free throws, but on the third shot his bounced out. Mine found the bottom of the net.'
b'Not quite the Little League championship game, but I\xe2\x80\x99ll take it.'

b'In February 2017, four seasons into the team\xe2\x80\x99s longest-ever playoff drought, the Lakers reshuffled their front office by firing the general manager, Mitch Kupchak, and installing Johnson as its president. Less than a month later, Rob Pelinka, a longtime agent, was hired as the general manager, reporting to Johnson.'
b'Officially and unofficially, Johnson had remained tied to the team since he retired in 1996. b'The first major test of the new regime had decidedly mixed results.'

In addition to Kuzma, the Lakers struck gold with Josh Hart, who was selected 30th and has become a core piece.'
b'Johnson made no secret of his intent to draw the game\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stars to Los Angeles, with an eye toward what was expected to be a major 2018 off-season. The team largely punted on the 2017 off-season to preserve its salary cap space in 2018, signing Kentavious Caldwell-Pope to a one-year deal.'
b'At the 2018 trade deadline, the Lakers shed the contracts of Jordan Clarkson and Larry Nance Jr., opening more cap space. Johnson said the trade indicated the Lakers would have the cap space and the ability to land two star players, either by trade or free agency.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have made the move if I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t confident,\xe2\x80\x9d he said at the time.'

b'An optimist would have called them playoff-tested veterans. Others saw it differently: A cast of nonshooters and big personalities who would have a questionable fit next to James and the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 young talent.'
b'The hodgepodge crew was assembled partly because the team struck out on its bigger targets. b'Once the season arrived, the Lakers blew it in dramatic fashion, extending their record playoff drought. But they preserved cap space for the 2019 off-season, giving them another chance to add a star.'

b'John MacLeod, the coach who led the Phoenix Suns on an improbable run to the 1976 National Basketball Association finals against the Boston Celtics \xe2\x80\x94 a series that included one of the most memorable playoff games in N.B.A. history \xe2\x80\x94 died on Sunday. He was 81.'
b'MacLeod\xe2\x80\x99s son, Matt, confirmed the death to The Associated Press but did not say where he died. The elder MacLeod had Alzheimer\xe2\x80\x99s disease for more than a decade.'
b'MacLeod joined the Suns in 1973 after they had ended a 38-44 season. At the time the Suns, who joined the league in the 1968-69 season, had never won an N.B.A. playoff series.'
b'His first two seasons in Phoenix were rocky, but in time he became the most successful coach in Suns history, going 579-543 in the regular seasons over 14 years.'
b'MacLeod\xe2\x80\x99s first winning season with the Suns ended with a 42-40 record, just enough to edge them into the 1976 playoffs. Phoenix then went on a dramatic run that culminated in their defeating the top-ranked Golden State Warriors for the Western Conference championship in seven games.'
b'The finals against the Celtics featured a tense fifth game, with the teams tied at two games apiece, that went into triple overtime at Boston Garden and into the basketball history books.'
b'Coming back from far behind, Phoenix tied the game at the end of regulation play and again at the end of the first overtime. Many fans swarmed the court after the Celtics star John Havlicek sunk a shot at the end of the second overtime to put Boston ahead, 111-110. But the referees ruled that a second remained on the clock and cleared the court.'
b'The game, with an unruly capacity crowd in the stands, went into a third overtime because of a canny decision. With that one second remaining, the Suns Hall of Fame guard Paul Westphal called a timeout, even though Phoenix had none left. That cost the Suns a technical foul and gave Boston another point on a successful free throw, but it also gave the Suns the ball at center court for a final play. The Suns forward Gar Heard took the inbounds pass, shot and tied the score, 112-112.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cCredit that move to Paul Westphal,\xe2\x80\x9d MacLeod told The New York Times. \xe2\x80\x9cHe thought of it while we were trying to map out a play. But with all those fans surrounding him, taunting our players and causing more fights, how could a coach coach? It was the most dangerous situation I\xe2\x80\x99ve ever been in.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the end, the Celtics triumphed, 128-126, and won the series, four games to two. The Suns, nicknamed the Sunderella Suns for their unlikely run, went on to appear in eight more playoffs and two more Western Conference finals under MacLeod.'
b'He had a franchise-record 37 playoff victories with the Suns and was placed in the Phoenix Suns Ring of Honor in 2012.'
b'The Suns dismissed him in 1987, after the team started the season 22-34. He also coached the Dallas Mavericks from 1987 to 1989, taking them to the playoffs in one season, and the Knicks, in 1990-91, achieving a 32-35 record. He finished his 18-year head coaching career with a 707-657 mark.'
b'John Matthew MacLeod was born on Oct. 3, 1937, in New Albany, Ind. He played basketball at Providence High School in Clarksville, Ind., and at Bellarmine University in Louisville, Ky.'
b'He was a successful head coach at the University of Oklahoma before he joined the Suns. He was later the head coach at the University of Notre Dame from 1991 until 1999. MacLeod\xe2\x80\x99s son Matt played on the team for his last two seasons as coach.'
b'After leaving Notre Dame, MacLeod returned to the Suns as an assistant coach. He was also an assistant with the Denver Nuggets and the Warriors, ending his career in 2006.'
b'In addition to his son, his survivors include his wife, Carol, and a daughter, Kathleen.'
b'The New York Times contributed reporting.'

b'Lou Williams, who has the unusual role of leading the Clippers in scoring while coming off the bench, does not run around the court so much as flutter across it. At 6 feet 1 inch and 175 pounds, he has embraced his identity as a butterfly among a herd of cattle.'
b'But at this stage of his career, Williams wants to feel as light and nimble as possible \xe2\x80\x94 so he essentially starves himself on game days. After a big breakfast, he refuses to eat again until well after the game itself, often going nearly 12 hours between meals.'
b'It is one of several habits that Williams, 32, has developed over the years, and one that clearly works for him. It is also the opposite of how most elite athletes prepare for games. But Williams is different: He wants to take the court with an appetite.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s crazy,\xe2\x80\x9d Landry Shamet, the first-year Clippers guard, said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99d weigh about 115 pounds if I did that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Clippers, as they often have this season, turned to Williams on Monday night for an extraordinary performance \xe2\x80\x94 this time against the Golden State Warriors in Game 2 of their first-round playoff series. In the Clippers\xe2\x80\x99 135-131 win, Williams collected 36 points and 11 assists to help erase a 31-point deficit.'
b'Shamet sealed the biggest comeback in N.B.A. playoff history with a go-ahead 3-pointer with 16.5 seconds left, and the Clippers evened the best-of-seven series at one game apiece.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m one of those guys who can get hot,\xe2\x80\x9d said Williams, who shot 13 of 22 from the field, \xe2\x80\x9cand I just got lost in the moment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Clippers, who have thrived behind Williams in the wake of a midseason deal that sent Tobias Harris to the Philadelphia 76ers, will need all of him again \xe2\x80\x94 all his scoring, all his savvy, all his unusual rituals \xe2\x80\x94 when the Warriors come to Los Angeles for Game 3 on Thursday.'
b'Make no mistake, the Clippers have their share of scrappy, no-nonsense guys. Patrick Beverley, who has spent the series covering the Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 Kevin Durant like aluminum foil, would trash talk a telephone pole.'
b'Williams, on the other hand, carries himself with a brand of quiet composure that has a power all its own.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe goes about his business,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sam Cassell, an assistant coach for the Clippers. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s not overwhelmingly faster than people. He\xe2\x80\x99s not bigger than people. But he understands what he can do on the basketball court, and he does it well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 Klay Thompson recently came across a package of highlight clips from Williams\xe2\x80\x99s days as a star guard at South Gwinnett High School outside of Atlanta. What stood out to Thompson was how little Williams had changed.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe played the exact same way,\xe2\x80\x9d Thompson said in an interview before the start of the series. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was incredible: same step-back jumper, same hesitations, same floaters.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams has stuck with the same general blueprint while refining his skills \xe2\x80\x94 slicker, craftier, jazzier. He has also become more resilient. There was a time, he said, when he thought his career might be finished. In 2013, he tore the anterior cruciate ligament in his right knee while playing for the Atlanta Hawks. In his comeback, he turned to Kenny Atkinson, who was then one of the team\xe2\x80\x99s assistants, to help reassemble his game.'
b'Atkinson, now the head coach of the Nets, imbued Williams with the importance of routine.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cKenny is one of my all-time favorite people in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said. \xe2\x80\x9cI give him a lot of credit for getting me back on my feet when I was down and out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'By 2015, Williams was the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s sixth man of the year with the Toronto Raptors. But he has never been better, more efficient or more dynamic than he has been in his last two seasons with the Clippers, all at an age \xe2\x80\x94 early 30s \xe2\x80\x94 when most players see their production begin to erode.'
b'Instead, Williams, who has scored more points off the bench than any other player in league history, has only improved. This season, he averaged 20 points and 5.4 assists in just 26.6 minutes a game. Williams also had the ball in his hands more than ever, with the Clippers running 32.4 percent of their plays through him whenever he was on the court, according to usage-rate statistics compiled by Basketball Reference.'
b'Coming off the bench was never something that he necessarily wanted to do, but Williams has no doubt that the role has helped preserve his career because it has kept his minutes down. He has averaged 24.6 minutes a game over his 14-year career. (LeBron James, by comparison, has averaged 38.6 minutes.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s given me an opportunity to stretch my career out, and I think I\xe2\x80\x99m in my prime right now, man,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m just rolling.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'At the same time, Williams has his quirky customs, which help give him a sense of stability, starting with his game-day breakfast: hash browns, egg whites, French toast and chicken sausage along with a fruit smoothie that he sweetens with honey. He loads up because he knows he won\xe2\x80\x99t eat again for a while.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI guess my body\xe2\x80\x99s gotten used to it,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said, who will just do the smoothie if the Clippers have an early tipoff.'
b'He also has the peculiar habit of arriving at the arena on the late side, about 90 minutes before the start of the game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t like idle time,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'Once there, though, Williams has an active schedule: 15 minutes in the training room getting stretched out, 10 minutes in the weight room doing exercises with a stretch band and a medicine ball, then about 17 minutes on the court making 150 field goals as Cassell feeds him passes.'
b'Before a recent home game ahead of the playoffs, Williams made nearly 80 percent of his attempts, including two skyscraping moonshots from the baseline, which is a shot that he has developed in case a 7-footer lunges at him with his arms extended. Williams says he only practices shots that he will attempt in games, however improbable or acrobatic.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI catch myself at least two or three times a game just putting my hands up, like, \xe2\x80\x98How did that even happen?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Shamet said.'
b'Williams wraps up his on-court work with 20 free throws and 10 court-width sprints, then retreats to the locker room to put on his ankle braces and check his phone. \xe2\x80\x9cJust to make sure there\xe2\x80\x99s no family emergencies or anything like that,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'With 20 minutes on the clock, the Clippers have their team meeting. Before they head to the court, Williams gathers his teammates around him for one final huddle \xe2\x80\x94 or rather, they gather around him, as if he has some sort of gravitational pull.'
b'Once the game begins, Williams takes a seat on the bench \xe2\x80\x94 which is the only time he stops moving. But he is watching his potential defenders and studying the flow, readying himself for the moment when he sheds his warm-ups late in the first quarter.'
b'If Cassell can pinpoint one flaw, it might be that Williams commits too many turnovers. He is an excellent passer, especially coming off ball screens \xe2\x80\x94 Shamet considers him one of the most underrated passers in the league \xe2\x80\x94 but he sometimes tries to do too much, Cassell said. So Cassell will remind Williams to do what he does best: Shoot the ball. '
b'It is what everyone wants to see from Williams, who is regarded around the league as a player whom other players love to watch.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt means a lot coming from my peers,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think as competitors, that\xe2\x80\x99s why we get into this, to gain respect from the guys who have played the game, and you walk away and they say, \xe2\x80\x98He was a tough cover \xe2\x80\x94 that dude was nice.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'All while being fueled with a hunger of his own creation.'

b'Sports of The Times'
b'By Michael Powell'
b'HOLBROOK, Ariz. \xe2\x80\x94 A wind that would not stop tugged at flags and sent sand devils spinning into this desert town as I walked past Mr. Maestas Restaurant and the Arizona Pawnman and the Empty Pockets Saloon and came to a rise and looked across an emptiness of plain that stretched the limits of vision.'
b'I recalled my talk a few days ago with Mike Budenholzer at the Ritz-Carlton in New York City. He coaches the Milwaukee Bucks, who finished the regular season with 60 wins and the best record in the N.B.A. His team features a brilliant Greek forward-guard-center named Giannis Antetokounmpo, Montenegrin and Turkish forwards, a Spanish center, and black and white players from corners rural and urban.'
b'He is known for his deft handling of diverse pro players. Where, I asked, did you pick up that skill?'
b'Let me tell you about my hometown, Holbrook, he said.'
b'Budenholzer, blue-eyed and middle-age, was once was a skinny, blond, teenage shooting guard in this old cattle and railway town. He starred on the Roadrunners basketball team at Holbrook High School alongside his boyhood friend B. J. Little, an African-American; a few Anglos; and a half-dozen Navajo boys who could run and pass all day and all night.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s no doubt in mind that my background there has helped me navigate life in the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x9d Budenholzer said. \xe2\x80\x9cGrowing up, you knew Navajo culture and black culture from Louisiana and Mexicans. I learned to foster the same sort of culture.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Holbrook comprises its own world, an isolated high desert city of 5,053 that sits on the southern lip of the Navajo Nation, which is the size of the Republic of Ireland. To the south lies the small Mormon town of Snowflake, and beyond that the forests and canyons of the White Mountain Apache Reservation, which is bigger than Delaware.'
b'Holbrook\xe2\x80\x99s population is roughly 50 percent white and 50 percent Navajo, Hopi, Mexican and black. The city has long kept a dormitory for Navajo children whose parents want them to attend the well-regarded Holbrook High School. Founded in the 1880s, Holbrook was an outlaw-friendly habitat, and a sign on the South Side tends to underline this point: Bucket of Blood Street. Terrill\xe2\x80\x99s Cottage Saloon once stood on this street, and more than a few cowpokes breathed their last there.'
b'Quite a few youngsters leave in search of better prospects. The city is tattered at the edges, a few buildings lie gape-toothed and abandoned, a motel stands vacant, and a single movie theater shows a single movie. But it\xe2\x80\x99s a hospitable place, and the main drag, Navajo Boulevard, has Mexican restaurants and motels and Native American jewelry stores and a herd of giant plastic dinosaurs that signal proximity to Petrified Forest National Park.'
b'Budenholzer\xe2\x80\x99s father, Vince, coached the basketball team and won a state championship in 1971 and was inducted into the state coaching hall of fame. At the time, Mike was an assistant to Gregg Popovich of the San Antonio Spurs. During a team visit to Phoenix, he told Popovich of his father\xe2\x80\x99s ascent. When Vince showed up later that day, Popovich got down on a knee in the hotel and said, \xe2\x80\x9cHere is a real coach.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Father and son were two hoops tramps who traveled in school buses hundreds of miles across the empty quarter of Northern Arizona in search of games and wins.'
b'Vince\xe2\x80\x99s Holbrook teams played a variation on the Native American hoops style known as Rez Ball: A quicksilver, sneaker-squeaking, run-pass-pass-shoot style, perfect for the Navajo and the Apache, for whom distance running is a millenniums-old tradition.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe pressed from the minute we stepped off the bus,\xe2\x80\x9d Vince said. \xe2\x80\x9dI had one Navajo who was taller than 6 foot, and so what?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Vince is 89 and still lean in that way of an old athlete, and he and his wife, Libby, moved nine years ago to Queen Valley, in the cactus foothills of the Superstition Mountains, east of Phoenix. They miss Holbrook; it remains the home of their hearts, but the winters on that mile-high plateau ran them off. \xe2\x80\x9cThe winds never stop blowing,\xe2\x80\x9d Libby said.'
b'The couple raised seven children, five boys and two girls, in a small house across Florida Street from Hunt Park. Libby became a councilwoman and served a term as mayor, and Vince moonlighted as Holbrook\xe2\x80\x99s parks and recreation director during the summer. He built a hoop in his backyard and put up a floodlight so the teenagers could play into the evening.'
b'Little, Mike\xe2\x80\x99s old teammate who is now a judge in nearby Winslow, drove me by that house, which was sold years back. The hoop still stood.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOh man, we\xe2\x80\x99d play there the whole night, and Vince would never stop coaching,\xe2\x80\x9d Little said. \xe2\x80\x9cMy grandparents said I had to get home before the streetlights came on. But if I was playing ball with Mikey at the Budenholzers, that was my pass.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Father and son Budenholzer flashed hauntingly similar smiles when they recalled those days. Mike was the leading scorer on the Roadrunners, a kid who could shoot from near and far and almost as well with his left hand as his right. Little, whose grandparents came from Louisiana to work in the McNary Saw Mill, ripped rebounds, and the Navajo kids dribbled and ran and pressed.'
b'The day before the tournament, two of the best players got drunk. They were suspended, and that left the Roadrunners with one star: Mike Budenholzer. That was not enough horsepower, and the team lost. \xe2\x80\x9cIt boggled my mind that they would get caught,\xe2\x80\x9d Mike said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think I would give up an N.B.A. championship to get that one back,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'I looked at him: You\xe2\x80\x99re kidding, right? He shrugged. \xe2\x80\x9cI mean, winning a state championship in Arizona, that\xe2\x80\x99s a big deal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Navajo and Mexican and Anglo kids still play baseball, basketball and football and live more or less shoulder to shoulder. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was a town where you played everything and with everyone else,\xe2\x80\x9d Mike said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe only social rule you recognized in high school was that Mormon girls don\xe2\x80\x99t date non-Mormons.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He shrugged. \xe2\x80\x9cSo you adjust.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Budenholzer was a good student and got into Pomona College, a fine liberal arts institution in California. He was not yet sold. He was a jock and he wanted to play basketball and he already had a scholarship offer in hand.'
b'He visited Pomona and sat around with other students and listened as they talked of their choices. There was the kid who was weighing Williams College or Pomona, and another who was wait-listed at Stanford University. They looked at Budenholzer and asked, What about you?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI tell them I\xe2\x80\x99m trying to choose between Pomona and Yavapai Community College, where I could get a free ride,\xe2\x80\x9d Budenholzer said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd they were, like, \xe2\x80\x98whaaaat?\xe2\x80\x99 And I\xe2\x80\x99m thinking, \xe2\x80\x98What am I doing here, I\xe2\x80\x99m in the wrong place.\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x9d'
b'His brothers and sisters decided Mikey, the youngest, was going to Pomona. They pooled money as best they could so he could afford it. He graduated with a degree in philosophy and economics.'
b'Before he left Holbrook and set out on his life journey, Budenholzer did what he did every summer, which is to say he rounded up B. J. Little and other buddies and piled into a car and headed north to play in the informal spring tournaments that are a staple of life on the Navajo reservation. They drove across washes and around canyons and past red-ribbed buttes that reared like primeval monsters. They pulled into Navajo towns: Dilkon and Window Rock, Tuba City and Ganado, anywhere there was a tournament.'
b'They got caught up in endless Rez Ball games, running and shooting and banging one another from morning till late at night. As hoops is civic religion on the rez, crowds of hundreds watched and cheered, not least for the bilagaanas (Navajo for whites).'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThose spring tournaments got rough, the referees were terrible and man, it was just the best,\xe2\x80\x9d Budenholzer said.'
b'During the season when reservation teams arrived to play Holbrook, a long line of cars would follow. The rule was straightforward for Holbrook\xe2\x80\x99s fans, Vince said. Make it to the gym by 4 p.m. for a 7 p.m. game, or you could forget about finding a seat.'
b'It is not so different when Mike\xe2\x80\x99s teams pull into Phoenix. After working as an assistant with the Spurs, he coached the Atlanta Hawks before coming to Milwaukee. Whenever his team plays the Phoenix Suns, Little\xe2\x80\x99s sister sets to work organizing a Holbrook caravan. Dozens of cars wend their way down through ponderosa forests and jagged mountains to the game \xe2\x80\x94 whites, Mexicans, blacks and Navajos, sometimes 100 strong. After the game, Budenholzer talks with them.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt always moves me,\xe2\x80\x9d Mike says.'
b'It\xe2\x80\x99s been a long time since he left home. This summer, after the N.B.A. playoffs and before the pro summer leagues begin, he and Vince and Libby plan to drive up through the Tonto National Forest and across the Salt River Canyon to Holbrook. And when they reach their old high school gym, they will find teammates and students and teachers and townspeople gathered to listen as Superintendent Robert Koerperich dedicates the Vince Budenholzer gym floor.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo let our kids know that you can come out of Holbrook and coach a pro team, how amazing is that?\xe2\x80\x9d Koeperich says.'
b'Mike Budenholzer looks forward to walking Navajo Boulevard and maybe seeing the family house again. Then he wants to stand behind Vince and Libby and clap so hard.'

b'During warm-ups for Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s game, Curry mimicked a game of volleyball with Philadelphia 76ers center Joel Embiid, posted up a ball boy so that he could take an entry pass from Oklahoma City Thunder point guard Russell Westbrook, made chitchat with bigwigs who were courtside and jacked his share of 30-footers. Most of them went in. All-Star weekend is a circus, but it is still basketball, after all, and Curry has unique skills.'
b'He is assembling another spectacular season, even if his work has been overshadowed by fellow All-Stars like James Harden of the Houston Rockets, Paul George of the Thunder and Milwaukee\xe2\x80\x99s Giannis Antetokounmpo. Curry has been so consistently good for so long now \xe2\x80\x94 and his team so dominant \xe2\x80\x94 that perhaps some of the novelty has worn off. It is unfair, of course.'
b'If his feats feel too familiar, consider his production this season: 28.6 points, 5.2 assists and 5.1 rebounds per game while shooting 48.8 percent from the field and 44.4 percent from 3-point range. He missed 11 games with a groin injury but spent part of that time gluing the Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 locker room back together after Kevin Durant and Draymond Green had a big dust-up.'
b'The friction stemmed from Durant\xe2\x80\x99s looming free agency, which has been a steady hum of distraction for the Warriors. But Curry has been a stabilizing force for his team \xe2\x80\x94 and even for the league.'
b'With a contract that runs through the 2021-22 season, Curry has not had to face pressing questions about his future. He is committed to the Warriors, and the Warriors appear committed to him. He is a throwback in an era dominated by player movement, the current face of which is Anthony Davis, the All-Star center who recently requested a trade from the New Orleans Pelicans. So many other stars face uncertain summers, too: Durant, Kyrie Irving and Kawhi Leonard among them.'
b'But Curry has his niche in Northern California, even if his roots are in North Carolina. After Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s game, he described trying to persuade his father to move to the Bay Area, where Curry has settled in with his wife, Ayesha, and their three children.'
b'Dell Curry, who is a color commentator for the Hornets, always says no.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is where home is for him,\xe2\x80\x9d Stephen Curry said.'
b'And for Stephen Curry, the whereabouts of his father seem to be the only player movements on his mind. Curry said he was unconcerned with free agency this summer and the potential departures of his teammates.'

b'By Jason Bailey'
b'Steven Soderbergh\xe2\x80\x99s electrifying new film \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird,\xe2\x80\x9d which debuted Friday on Netflix, tells the story of a fictional N.B.A. lockout set in the Instagram Age, in which longstanding concerns about money, race and social justice are galvanized by disputes over players\xe2\x80\x99 personal images, and who has the right to control them. (Appropriately, the entire film was shot on an iPhone.)'
b'The film\xe2\x80\x99s dense but fast-moving script, written by the playwright Tarell Alvin McCraney (\xe2\x80\x9cMoonlight\xe2\x80\x9d), is also replete with references to the game\xe2\x80\x99s history \xe2\x80\x94 not least to the currents of protest and politics that have coursed through pro basketball since it was segregated. There\xe2\x80\x99s a rich subtext here, much of it only hinted at. Below is a spoiler-filled guide.'
b'As in baseball, football and most areas of American life, segregation kept black players out of the white pro basketball leagues, confined to amateur and semipro all-black teams, which formed in schools, churches, community centers and the like. Games were frequently paired with ragtime dances to make for a full evening of entertainment.'
b'The best known of these barnstorming teams, often called \xe2\x80\x9cBlack Fives\xe2\x80\x9d by historians, were the New York Renaissance and the Harlem Globetrotters. The Renaissance \xe2\x80\x94 or, as they were better known, the Rens \xe2\x80\x94 were so impressive that in 1947, Coach Joe Lapchick of the New York Knicks lobbied the Basketball Association of America to admit the team into the young league, a precursor of the National Basketball Association. The owners voted him down. The next year, a competing league, the National Basketball League, brought the team in instead.'
b'[Read the Times review of \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird\xe2\x80\x9d by A.O. Scott.]'
b'Indirectly. The Rens and the Globetrotters, in particular, were internationally known for their dazzling play, often besting white teams when matched up for exhibition games. The Rens, for example, beat the all-white Oshkosh All-Stars in the first integrated tournament championship in 1939; the Globetrotters beat the Minnesota Lakers in a celebrated 1948 exhibition game that The Chicago Tribune pinpointed as key to the integration of the game.'
b'As Spencer (Bill Duke) explains in \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird\xe2\x80\x9d: \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a reason why the N.B.A. started integrating as the Harlem Globetrotters exhibitions started going international. Control. They wanted the control of a game that we played, and we played better.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Lapchick, however, did not give up. In 1950, the year after the Basketball Association of America absorbed the smaller National Basketball League and became the N.B.A., he signed Nat (Sweetwater) Clifton, who had played for the Rens and the Globetrotters (as well as in baseball\xe2\x80\x99s Negro leagues), to join the Knicks. That same season, West Virginia State\xe2\x80\x99s Earl Lloyd joined the Washington Capitals and Chuck Cooper was drafted out of Duquesne by the Boston Celtics. (Another black player, Hank DeZonie, played five games with the Tri-Cities Blackhawks in December of that season.)'
b'Talking to The Times in 2008, Lloyd told stories of being heckled and spat upon by fans, although the abuse he encountered was \xe2\x80\x9cno comparison,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, to what Jackie Robinson withstood three years earlier in professional baseball.'
b'Yes \xe2\x80\x94 in fact, there were four. (One lasted only a few hours.) In the first dialogue scene of \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird,\xe2\x80\x9d the sports agent Ray Burke (Andr\xc3\xa9 Holland) tells a client, \xe2\x80\x9cLast time this happened, folks was broke left and right!\xe2\x80\x9d That \xe2\x80\x9clast time\xe2\x80\x9d was the 2011 lockout, which lasted  five months and resulted in the loss of 16 regular-season games, the entire preseason and an estimated $400 million in revenue for team owners and players.'
b'A 10-year deal was announced late that November, which heavily favored owners. It reduced player salaries by nearly $300 million and shifted an estimated $3 billion to the owners over the course of the contract. The truncated 66-game season finally got underway on Christmas Day.'
b'Much screen time in \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird\xe2\x80\x9d is spent contemplating the legality of public appearances and exhibition games by league-signed players during the lockout. The 2011 lockout was threaded with similar concerns. The film\xe2\x80\x99s fictional team owners grouse over the attention attracted by a \xe2\x80\x9clockout street ball event in Las Vegas,\xe2\x80\x9d presumably inspired by the \xe2\x80\x9clockout league\xe2\x80\x9d in Vegas, which comprised two weeks of pickup games with more than 70 N.B.A. players in September 2011, according to The Las Vegas Sun. (Profits from ticket sales were donated to charity).'
b'Dozens of players filled the pay gap by picking up spots on teams in Europe and Japan. As The Times\xe2\x80\x99s Howard Beck noted at the time, however, \xe2\x80\x9ca vast majority of them are rookies, middling veterans and fringe players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As New York magazine and others have noted, the character Myra (Sonja Sohn) strongly resembles Michele Roberts, who became the executive director of the National Basketball Players Association in 2014. The first woman in history to head a major sports union, Roberts made waves from the beginning. A Times profile a few months into her tenure noted that she had already \xe2\x80\x9cforcefully questioned the league\xe2\x80\x99s pay model and labeled its entire cadre of owners as replaceable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Like the character she inspired, Roberts is a tough-as-nails negotiator who is undaunted by working in a male-dominated world. \xe2\x80\x9cMy past,\xe2\x80\x9d she told players while making her case for the job, \xe2\x80\x9cis littered with the bones of men who were foolish enough to think I was someone they could sleep on.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the film\xe2\x80\x99s first scene, Ray gives a client a mysterious package, calling it \xe2\x80\x9cthe Bible.\xe2\x80\x9d It contains the book \xe2\x80\x9cThe Revolt of the Black Athlete\xe2\x80\x9d by the sports sociologist and civil rights advocate Dr. Harry Edwards, who also appears briefly in Ray\xe2\x80\x99s office near the end of the film. Edwards first came to national prominence for organizing the Olympic Project for Human Rights, whose members Tommie Smith and John Carlos made headlines for raising their gloved fists while receiving medals at the 1968 Olympics.'
b'Edwards has spent the ensuing years teaching, writing, consulting and leading protests. \xe2\x80\x9cRevolt,\xe2\x80\x9d published in 1969, argued that racism is as prevalent in sports as in any other section of society. \xe2\x80\x9cThe sports world is not a rose flourishing in the middle of a wasteland,\xe2\x80\x9d he writes. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is part and parcel of that wasteland, reeking of the same racism that corrupts other areas of our society.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHigh Flying Bird\xe2\x80\x9d is bookended by recordings of two folk-rock classics, both performed by Richie Havens as part of his opening set at Woodstock. The title track, Havens\xe2\x80\x99s recording of a folk song written by Billy Edd Wheeler, was praised by the musicologist Richie Unterberger for its \xe2\x80\x9carresting minor-keyed melody and brooding lyrics, contrasting the freedom of a bird to the singer\xe2\x80\x99s earthbound misery.\xe2\x80\x9d It isn\xe2\x80\x99t hard to connect those lyrics to Ray\xe2\x80\x99s notion that his clients should free themselves from the earthbound constraints of the sports industry and bring the game back to its roots.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHandsome Johnny,\xe2\x80\x9d which Havens wrote with the Oscar-winning actor Louis Gossett Jr., closes the film, telling the story of a young man who marches off to a series of wars. Given the movie\xe2\x80\x99s themes, the song\xe2\x80\x99s refrain is appropriate: \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a long hard road, hey, before we\xe2\x80\x99ll be free.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Billy Witz'
b'GREENSBORO, N.C. \xe2\x80\x94 As advanced statistical analysis and its attendant new technology continue to reshape how sports are understood, watched and even played \xe2\x80\x94 when to punt on fourth down in football, where to position a baseball team\xe2\x80\x99s infielders and how to build a winning basketball team \xe2\x80\x94 these new numbers also create a vexing problem:'
b'How to account for what complex algorithms cannot explain.'
b'The thirst for information is such that one essential set of college basketball data that will help determine the field for this month\xe2\x80\x99s N.C.A.A. tournament, Ken Pomeroy\xe2\x80\x99s eponymous KenPom ratings, includes a metric to shed light on when things do not actually go by the numbers.'
b'Pomeroy has a rather analog term for it: luck.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLuck is basically performance in close games,\xe2\x80\x9d Pomeroy said. \xe2\x80\x9cPeople generally don\xe2\x80\x99t like the term \xe2\x80\x98luck\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x94 that\xe2\x80\x99s the feedback I get. Technically, I\xe2\x80\x99d call it \xe2\x80\x98randomness\xe2\x80\x99 or something a lot more wordy, but that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t fit well above a column.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In short, KenPom\xe2\x80\x99s luck factor considers the difference between a team\xe2\x80\x99s record and what the data would expect it to be. If a team\xe2\x80\x99s record is better than its predictive numbers, it is lucky. If it is worse, then it is unlucky.'
b'This season, according to the KenPom ratings, no team among the 353 Division I college men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball programs has been luckier than the University of North Carolina at Greensboro.'
b'The Spartans resemble a team one might expect from a coach, Wes Miller, who transferred to North Carolina as a walk-on, then earned a letter on a national championship team and eventually a spot in the starting lineup. They are resourceful and determined, and have the ethos (and the recruiting budget) of an underdog.'
b'Greensboro has a 28-6 record \xe2\x80\x94 the best in program history \xe2\x80\x94 and finished second in the Southern Conference, behind Wofford, which was ranked 20th in this week\xe2\x80\x99s Associated Press poll.'
b'Did luck have something to do with it?'
b'Miller, pulling up a folding chair before a recent practice, reacted as one might expect. He praised Pomeroy as \xe2\x80\x9ca genius,\xe2\x80\x9d expressed fascination with analytics and said there were others on his staff who delve deeper into the data to provide the most salient information about the Spartans and their opponents.'
b'Then he assumed a defensive stance.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not a mathematician,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m a basketball coach who\xe2\x80\x99s always trying to figure out an edge to help me coach better. But there\xe2\x80\x99s never been anybody that could put a number on will and togetherness of group.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s something that\xe2\x80\x99s happening in our games that\xe2\x80\x99s indescribable to his data that\xe2\x80\x99s getting us over the hump,\xe2\x80\x9d Miller added. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s toughness. That\xe2\x80\x99s the ability to win close games. The proudest I ever am as a coach is when we have an awful shooting game or we have an awful offensive game and things don\xe2\x80\x99t go our way and we still find a way because our team was able to dig down and figure out a way to get over the hump.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Francis Alonso, a senior guard from Malaga, Spain, who is the heartbeat of his team, put it another way: \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s this saying \xe2\x80\x94 it\xe2\x80\x99s champions\xe2\x80\x99 luck.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alan Castel, a psychology professor at U.C.L.A. who studies memory and metacognition \xe2\x80\x94 how we think about our thinking \xe2\x80\x94 said that while confidence (or the lack of it) is a fundamental element of athletic competition, it is often misplaced.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe human mind doesn\xe2\x80\x99t rely on big data,\xe2\x80\x9d said Castel, whose research has debunked the hot-hand theory \xe2\x80\x94 the belief that a team should get the ball to a shooter who is on a hot streak. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re prone to rely on illusions and small sample sizes and what we want to think.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'If Greensboro\xe2\x80\x99s Spartans are the luckiest team in the country, he said, they deserve some of the credit for it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo be lucky, you need to put yourself in a situation,\xe2\x80\x9d Castel said. \xe2\x80\x9cTo win the lottery, you need to buy a ticket.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Or, he added, to win the N.C.A.A. tournament, you need to get in. And to do that, the Spartans almost certainly will require a little more luck.'
b'Some years ago, a r\xc3\xa9sum\xc3\xa9 like the Spartans\xe2\x80\x99 might have looked glossier. They have a sparkling record, are 7-0 in games decided by 5 points or fewer and have been competitive in defeats at 10th-ranked Louisiana State (97-91) and sixth-ranked Kentucky (78-61), a game that they led with less than nine minutes left. But they lost to Wofford twice in the regular season \xe2\x80\x94 by 29 and 30 points \xe2\x80\x94 and for a third time on Monday night, 70-58, in the Southern Conference tournament championship game.'
b'Yet it is this profile \xe2\x80\x94 a team that has squeaked past bad teams, competed against good ones and been pounded only twice, by the best team in its conference \xe2\x80\x94 that explains why Greensboro\xe2\x80\x99s luck factor is +.175, which, if it holds until the season is over, would be the highest of any team since 2013.'
b'What that figure means, Pomeroy said, is that in a luck-free environment, the Spartans\xe2\x80\x99 winning percentage would be 0.175 lower than it is. As a result, they would have six fewer victories \xe2\x80\x94 and a 22-12 record \xe2\x80\x94 without any luck.'
b'There are real-world consequences: Through Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s games, Greensboro ranked 81st in KenPom\xe2\x80\x99s overall ratings, lagging behind East Tennessee State (71st) and Furman (55th), against whom they combined to win four of five games this season. b'Once the N.C.A.A. tournament begins next week, with a broad spectrum of schools from around the country, a clearer picture will emerge of whether teams that have been deemed to have enjoyed metric good fortune have punched above their weight all season.'
b'The Spartans, at this point, would consider themselves lucky to have the chance.'

b'By Marc Tracy'
b'Vertical leap is measured using a simple contraption: a tall pole with a series of long, metal fingers that project horizontally from it on top of one another \xe2\x80\x94 narrow wings stacked up, up, up, at consistent increments. It may seem lo-fi, but it is also foolproof: Your vertical reach while jumping is the highest metal flange you are able to bat away from its set position. Subtract standing vertical reach from that number, and you have a player\xe2\x80\x99s vertical leap. '
b'When Duke put its players through the test one day last summer, Zion Williamson\xe2\x80\x99s vertical leap was measured at 46 inches. But to the teammates and Duke staff members who were present, mere numbers do not do the moment justice.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe were all in shock,\xe2\x80\x9d the sophomore guard Alex O\xe2\x80\x99Connell said. '
b'Williamson, who went last, was off the charts. On his first attempt, he casually swatted aside the highest measurement. A staff member adjusted the pole to its highest setting and reset the tabs, and Williamson repeated the feat. They put weights under the contraption to lift it a few more inches into the air. Williamson batted the highest measurements aside again. '
b"\xe2\x80\x9cIt was something you don't see a lot, especially with a guy who is built like him flying through the air,\xe2\x80\x9d forward Javin DeLaurier said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt's a sight to behold.\xe2\x80\x9d"

b'LOS ANGELES \xe2\x80\x94 Steve Kerr, the coach of the Golden State Warriors, was asked about the concept of inevitability before his team faced the Los Angeles Clippers on Thursday night, which is something that happens during the N.B.A. playoffs. Some questions are more philosophical than others.'
b'In this case, the question had to do with the perception shared by many that the Warriors are invincible, that another championship is theirs to lose: What is it like for Kerr to live inside that bubble, knowing full well that his players are capable of making mistakes and even (gasp) failing?'
b'Kerr took the opportunity to recall a moment from his childhood in Southern California. When he was 9 years old, he watched his beloved U.C.L.A. Bruins defeat the Kentucky Wildcats for another N.C.A.A. championship, their 10th in 12 years. Coach John Wooden retired after the game. In the nearly half-century since, U.C.L.A. has won one championship \xe2\x80\x94 in 1995, when Bob Myers, now the general manager of the Warriors, was a reserve forward.'
b'Kerr made sure to note that coincidence. But his larger point was about how sports are unpredictable, which is one of the reasons they are so appealing. Just as no one knew, for example, that the Warriors would make the wrong kind of history by blowing a 31-point lead on Monday, no one knew that they would bounce back on Thursday by obliterating the Clippers, 132-105, in Game 3 of their first-round series.'
b'At the same time, no one knows whether the Warriors will go on to win a third straight championship \xe2\x80\x94 or how long this team will remain intact. Nothing is inevitable. Everything is uncertain. All dynasties end.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSo you don\xe2\x80\x99t worry about expectations,\xe2\x80\x9d Kerr said. \xe2\x80\x9cJust go out there and play and do your best and see if you can sustain it for a long time. But everything comes to an end, and we\xe2\x80\x99re just trying to keep this going for as long as we can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The central (if unmentioned) figure in all of this, of course, is Kevin Durant, who has taken on all comers this season in the form of a 7-foot, long-limbed question mark. But if he cannot live up to the hype he created in last year\xe2\x80\x99s playoffs \xe2\x80\x94 that is, if he becomes just another guard \xe2\x80\x94 the Pelicans may be more likely to accept a package from the Los Angeles Lakers or another team besides Boston. At the same time, if Celtics point guard Kyrie Irving opts for free agency this summer, the future of the franchise may rest on Tatum\xe2\x80\x99s shoulders. At barely 21, he\xe2\x80\x99d be the alpha.'
b'Tatum\xe2\x80\x99s future is more uncertain than many other players who have received significant early acclaim. But one way or another, the Celtics need Tatum to be great. Not just for this year\xe2\x80\x99s playoffs, but for the future.'
b'In short, they need him to boom.'
b'In a conversation at the Celtics\xe2\x80\x99 practice facility about his future and the atypical stakes, Tatum had talking points at the ready, ones that he had delivered multiple times before. He stared straight ahead, not making eye contact, as if he were running through the script in his head.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTrade rumors don\xe2\x80\x99t bother me,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in his deep monotone. \xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re talking about trading me for guys like Anthony Davis. So, I mean, I must be doing something pretty well.\xe2\x80\x9d When pressed on whether this bothered him, he didn\xe2\x80\x99t budge: \xe2\x80\x9cI love the game of basketball. Being traded is part of the game. I\xe2\x80\x99ll play for whomever. It\xe2\x80\x99s something I can\xe2\x80\x99t control.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He didn\xe2\x80\x99t have much more to say than that. But that is Tatum\xe2\x80\x99s personality, Brad Stevens, the Celtics\xe2\x80\x99 head coach, said. No distractions. That, Stevens said, is his best quality.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cCircumstances don\xe2\x80\x99t affect him,\xe2\x80\x9d Stevens said. \xe2\x80\x9cFirst game of the season, he\xe2\x80\x99s unaffected by the jitters that everybody has. Seventh game of a playoff series? Unaffected. At least, he shows himself to be unaffected, and he can thrive in that environment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Stevens said Tatum\xe2\x80\x99s quality of play had improved as he got deeper into the season. He became a better passer, averaging 2.8 assists after the All-Star break, compared with 1.9 before. But his shooting dipped, from 38 percent from deep before the break to 35 percent afterward.'
b'Last season, Tatum benefited from the low expectations for the Celtics after injuries to Irving, forward Gordon Hayward and the reserve center Daniel Theis. But he also helped carry Boston to within one win of an unlikely N.B.A. finals appearance. This year, \xe2\x80\x9cunlikely\xe2\x80\x9d is not in the playoff vocabulary. The Celtics are supposed to get there. And Boston\xe2\x80\x99s fans, never the most positive bunch, can turn on a player in a second. b'Tatum said he was not as nervous about the playoffs this time around. Taking a daily pregame nap with his 16-month-old son has helped. b'By Marc Tracy'
b'The N.C.A.A. said on Saturday that it was appealing a Federal District Court\xe2\x80\x99s decision this month that barring athletes from being paid beyond a scholarship and related costs violated antitrust law.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe believe, and the Supreme Court has recognized, that N.C.A.A. member schools and conferences are best positioned to strengthen and revise their rules to better support student-athletes, rather than forcing these issues into continuous litigation,\xe2\x80\x9d Donald Remy, the N.C.A.A.\xe2\x80\x99s chief legal officer, said in a statement.'
b'Remy said the decision to appeal, by the N.C.A.A. and the major college conferences named as defendants in the suit, was unanimous.'
b'The ruling this month by Judge Claudia Wilken in the United States District Court for the Northern District of California was actually far more favorable to the N.C.A.A. than the plaintiffs, a class of Division I men\xe2\x80\x99s and women\xe2\x80\x99s basketball players and football players, had hoped.'
b'The suit, known as Alston after a lead plaintiff, argued that the N.C.A.A.\xe2\x80\x99s rules barring payments to players \xe2\x80\x94 the center of what the association terms the collegiate model, and what is broadly known as amateurism \xe2\x80\x94 was illegal collusion. It asked the court to declare as much, and to eliminate all such rules, leaving it up to individual conferences to set caps independently if they so chose.'
b'Instead, while Judge Wilken agreed that the rules were illegal, she found that an alternative, in which the N.C.A.A. continued to restrict payments unless they were tied to education, was acceptable. Under her ruling, colleges could give athletes items like computers, but the N.C.A.A. could continue to bar them from receiving cash in express exchange for their athletic contributions.'
b'Judge Wilken cited a 2015 ruling from the United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit in a similar case, in which a three-judge panel partially insisted that payment to athletes be \xe2\x80\x9ctethered to education.\xe2\x80\x9d The same appellate court \xe2\x80\x94 albeit probably three different judges \xe2\x80\x94 would hear this appeal.'
b'While the N.C.A.A. largely welcomed Judge Wilken\xe2\x80\x99s finding when it was handed down, it said on Saturday that it sought more: to get the courts out of regulating college athletics as much as possible.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhile the district court upheld the distinction between full-time students who play college sports and professional athletes, it erred by giving itself authority to micromanage decisions about education-related support,\xe2\x80\x9d Remy said.'
b'Jeffrey Kessler, a lead lawyer for the plaintiffs, said of the appeal in a text message on Saturday morning: \xe2\x80\x9cWe are not surprised. It was a major defeat for the N.C.A.A.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'The rapper was not pleased that the Minnesota Timberwolves mocked his performance in Milwaukee. He put a curse on the team.'
b'By Benjamin Hoffman'
b'Sports curses come in all shapes and sizes. They can involve livestock, soup commercials, magazine covers and, frequently, the selling of star players.'
b'In recent years, the rapper Lil B has made a name for himself in the sports realm with his curses \xe2\x80\x94 most notably on James Harden of the Houston Rockets \xe2\x80\x94 but it appears he has some new competition: the rapper Ja Rule.'
b'It all started on Saturday, when Ja Rule was performing at halftime of a game between the Minnesota Timberwolves and the host Milwaukee Bucks.'
b'The performance came on the 17th anniversary of Ja Rule\xe2\x80\x99s collaboration with Ashanti, \xe2\x80\x9cAlways Be On Time,\xe2\x80\x9d hitting No. 1 on Billboard\xe2\x80\x99s Hot 100. But the show came under criticism immediately because of a somewhat misleading video of the crowd reaction and another one showing an unexpected guest: Giannis Antetokounmpo, the Bucks\xe2\x80\x99 star forward, who came out to begin warming up for the second half while Ja Rule was still performing on the court along with a group of dancers.'
b'The rapper initially shrugged off the criticism, but his tone changed when the Timberwolves decided to mock the performance on social media. In a post to Twitter, the team said \xe2\x80\x9cWe too were hustled, scammed, bamboozled, hood winked, lead astray!!!\xe2\x80\x9d The post was a reference to an earlier post by Ja Rule about his role in the ill-fated Fyre Festival, a luxury music event in the Bahamas that failed spectacularly in 2017. '
b'The rapper was not amused.'
b'The potential effects of this particular curse are unclear, though. The Timberwolves have existed as a franchise for 30 seasons and not only have not won a championship, but they have only made it out of the first round of the playoffs once \xe2\x80\x94 in 2004. They are 28-31, putting them just outside legitimate playoff contention, and the notion that Karl-Anthony Towns is departing anytime soon \xe2\x80\x94 as Ja Rule suggested with \xe2\x80\x9cAND KAT IS LEAVING!!!\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 seems unlikely, as he has signed a five-year contract extension that kicks in next year and guarantees him nearly $160 million.'
b'Of course, logic does not have to play a role in sports curses. The Chicago Cubs endured the so-called Curse of the Billy Goat for more than 70 years after the team asked the owner of the Billy Goat Tavern, William Sianis, to leave a game because his goat was bothering fans. That the team had not won a World Series in more than 30 years before the episode was treated as mostly irrelevant. '
b'Other popular curses have included one in which the athletes endorsing Campbell\xe2\x80\x99s Chunky Soup seemed to become injured at an extraordinary rate. Another claimed that athletes had their performance fall off after appearing on the cover of Sports Illustrated.'
b'The most famous, of course, is the Curse of the Bambino, which doomed the Boston Red Sox to lose after selling Babe Ruth to the Yankees in December 1919. The jinx is credited by some with keeping the Red Sox from winning a World Series for 86 years, despite the first year of that stretch coming before the team sold Ruth, and the fact that the curse was barely mentioned in popular culture before George Vecsey wrote a column about it for The New York Times in 1986. Dan Shaughnessy of the Boston Globe also wrote a book in 1990 that popularized the phrase.'
b'At the very least, the talk of Ja Rule\xe2\x80\x99s curse was good news for Lil B, who spent part of the weekend trending on Twitter. He celebrated by retweeting various people saying Ja Rule was simply stealing a tactic that Lil B had already perfected.'
b'Benjamin Hoffman is a senior staff editor and regular contributor to the Keeping Score column in sports. He joined The Times in 2005.  @BenHoffmanNYT \xe2\x80\xa2 Facebook '

b'Having been traded five times in eight seasons, Harris would like to be able to drop off his dry cleaning, then wake up in the same city to pick it up. At 26, after an All-Star-caliber season, he is looking for a home. That might even be Philadelphia.'
b'He averaged 20 points and 7.9 rebounds this season in a total of 82 games with the Clippers and Sixers. In 27 regular-season games for Philadelphia, Harris averaged 18.2 points, tying him with Butler for second on the 76ers\xe2\x80\x99 scoring list, behind Embiid, who averaged 27.5.'
b'For Game 4, the 76ers may still be without Embiid, which means that they will again need balanced scoring from the rest of their talented cast. On Thursday, Philadelphia had three scorers with 26 or more points (Simmons, Harris, Redick). The last time the franchise accomplished that in a playoff game was Game 3 of the 1978 conference semifinals against the Knicks. That night, it was Julius Erving, George McGinnis and World B. Free.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI felt good,\xe2\x80\x9d Harris said. \xe2\x80\x9cI just came in knowing with Joel down, it was a big scoring loss we had out there. I had to be aggressive from the start. I got some good looks throughout the game. I was able to let it fly, and it felt good for it to go in.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was a big game personally for myself and for the team, too,\xe2\x80\x9d he added.'
b'Beyond basketball, Harris co-stars in the best buddy movie in the N.B.A., known as the Bobi + Tobi Show. In 2016, Harris and Boban Marjanovic, a 7-foot-3 Serbian center, developed a close bond while playing for the Detroit Pistons. They were then traded to the Clippers for Blake Griffin in January 2018. About a year later, they became a package deal headed to Philadelphia.'
b'The Clippers produced three web episodes of the \xe2\x80\x9cBobi + Tobi Show\xe2\x80\x9d focused on the pair\xe2\x80\x99s friendship and foibles. They took a SoulCycle class together. They attempted a dance lesson. The fun continued in Philadelphia, where a TV station did a quiz show segment with them, focusing on trivia about their new city. Neither could pronounce \xe2\x80\x9cSchuylkill.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In Game 3, Marjanovic played the sidekick during Harris\xe2\x80\x99s star turn. He came off the bench and split time with Greg Monroe, who had replaced Embiid in the starting lineup.'
b'Monroe and Marjanovic combined for 43 minutes and 21 of the Sixers\xe2\x80\x99 54 rebounds. With Harris defending on the perimeter, the load was lighter on the big men in the paint, though Marjanovic fouled out with about seven minutes left in the game.'
b'No matter. His buddy had his back. The game was in control, and Harris looked right at home.'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'It was a humble TV listing, informing readers that the Knicks would be playing the Washington Bullets on MSG that night. The short item noted that \xe2\x80\x9cThe Knicks tried double-teaming Jeff Ruland in the second of those games, but the tactic didn\xe2\x80\x99t work: He responded with a triple double-digit effort \xe2\x80\x94 22 points, 12 rebounds and 10 assists.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was Dec. 29, 1984. And for the very first time, The New York Times had cited the triple-double.'
b'On Monday night, Russell Westbrook completed an unprecedented 10th consecutive triple-double, with 21 points, 14 rebounds and 11 assists as the Oklahoma City Thunder defeated the Portland Trail Blazers. Westbrook broke the record of nine, set by Wilt Chamberlain in 1968.'
b'The moment Russ passed Wilt for the longest triple-double streak \xf0\x9f\x94\xa5 pic.twitter.com/xTytZdyzDd'
b'But while triple-doubles are no longer uncommon \xe2\x80\x94 Westbrook\xe2\x80\x99s teammate Paul George turned in an even more immpressive line (47 points, 10 rebounds, 12 assists) on Monday \xe2\x80\x94 the term is relatively new. Like Chamberlain, some of the greatest practitioners made every one of their triple-doubles when triple-doubles were not even a thing.'
b'The Times quickly embraced the triple-double. Two days after its debut, the label made it into an ordinary sports article, this time without the clunky words \xe2\x80\x9cdigit\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9ceffort.\xe2\x80\x9d Precedent had been set.'
b'In those early days, some of the references to triple-double in The Times were in quotes, as if editors were afraid that the new term would pollute the newspaper\xe2\x80\x99s august pages. Eventually the arbiters of style settled on no quotes, and a hyphen in between the two words.'
b'The first triple-double in Basketball-Reference\xe2\x80\x99s database is from 1950, when Andy Phillip of the Philadelphia Warriors tallied 17 points, 10 rebounds and 10 assists, although there were almost certainly others before that when stat keeping was less precise and complete.'
b'Harvey Pollack, the longtime 76ers stats guru, is generally credited with inventing the term in the early 1980s, inspired by Magic Johnson, who made a habit of triple-doubling. (Ruland, though he was the Times\xe2\x80\x99s triple-double pioneer, claimed only five in his career.)'
b'There are also double-doubles \xe2\x80\x94 the career record is held by Chamberlain \xe2\x80\x94 and quadruple doubles, for those who can also manage 10 blocks or steals. That has only happened a handful of times in the N.B.A., and not since David Robinson in 1994.'
b'There are even quintuple doubles, a stupefying exploit \xe2\x80\x94 25 points, 18 rebounds, 11 assists, 10 steals and 10 blocks \xe2\x80\x94 performed by the women\xe2\x80\x99s star Tamika Catchings when she was in high school in 1997.'
b'Westbrook has taken the triple-double to new heights, though, actually averaging a triple-double for the last two seasons. He is on pace to do so again this season. And unlike his early predecessors, he is keenly aware of the stat, often looking to add that one more assist or rebound that he needs late in a game.'
b'Westbrook now has 127 total triple-doubles, closing in on Johnson, the inspiration for the term, who has 138.'
b'But above all of them is Oscar Robertson, the only other man to average a triple-double; he had 181 in his Hall of Fame career.'
b'His last one came in 1974, when the feat was still unnamed, at least in The Times.'

b'James\xe2\x80\x99s absence \xe2\x80\x94 however long it lasts \xe2\x80\x94 may not wind up being the worst thing for the Lakers. Assuming he returns at full strength, without complications, James could probably benefit from a midseason break.'
b'More important, perhaps, has been the opportunity for the team\xe2\x80\x99s lesser lights to operate on their own. The training wheels are off. For a while, it looked bleak. b'On Monday, with the rust from his injury still apparent, Kuzma shot 4 of 20 from the field in a win against the Dallas Mavericks. b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you would have told me two years ago, when I was in college, that I would score 40 for the Lakers, I probably wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have believed you,\xe2\x80\x9d Kuzma said. \xe2\x80\x9cKind of crazy.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'But really, Walton said, there are probably more unknowns than knowns with this group. On only a handful of occasions has he had close to a full roster at his disposal. The rest of the league will be interested to see what the Lakers look like when he finally does.'

b'But his type of injury has ended careers, particularly among big men, and every team in the league balked at offering him a long-term deal. b'\xe2\x80\x9cWell,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI won\xe2\x80\x99t be taking as many shots as I have in the past.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He also has a reputation for being emotional, and something of an antagonist. Some of the Warriors have firsthand experience. But before he left the court, Kerr caught Cousins taunting him by waving goodbye.'
b'Then there was an episode last season, when Cousins was playing for the Pelicans, and he got into an altercation with Kevin Durant. After both players were ejected, Cousins tried to track down Durant outside the Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 locker room \xe2\x80\x94 and not to exchange pleasantries.'

b'Malone said he expected that Cousins would give the Warriors \xe2\x80\x9ca big lift,\xe2\x80\x9d and Malone made those remarks before the Nuggets\xe2\x80\x99 142-111 loss to the Warriors.'
b'The Warriors have had their struggles this season, although these things tend to be relative. Green beefed with Durant. Stephen Curry missed 11 games with a strained groin. b'The Warriors have been rolling of late, though, winning seven of their last eight before their game against the Pelicans on Wednesday night. They appear to be playing their best basketball of the season, as evidenced by their demolition of the Nuggets, a rout so thorough that Malone said it would be impossible for his team to just \xe2\x80\x9cflush\xe2\x80\x9d the loss and forget it.'

b'As the Warriors continue to try to assimilate the former All-Star center DeMarcus Cousins into their rotation, Bogut said he had \xe2\x80\x9cno illusions\xe2\x80\x9d about the fact that \xe2\x80\x9csome games I\xe2\x80\x99ll play and some games I won\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d But Bogut insisted he was \xe2\x80\x9chappy to be a positive influence on that bench\xe2\x80\x9d no matter how much he plays.'

b'Warriors Coach Steve Kerr referred to Bogut as \xe2\x80\x9can insurance policy in the frontcourt.\xe2\x80\x9d But Bogut\xe2\x80\x99s defensive know-how and his familiarity with the Warriors\xe2\x80\x99 star trio of Stephen Curry, Klay Thompson and Draymond Green certainly can\xe2\x80\x99t hurt the league\xe2\x80\x99s prohibitive championship favorites in the quest to improve on their woeful standing of 16th in defensive efficiency (109.5 points allowed per 100 possessions.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t foresee this happening but I\xe2\x80\x99m excited as hell about it,\xe2\x80\x9d Green told Bay Area reporters. He and Bogut quickly meshed as co-anchors of a vaunted Golden State defense in 2014-15, when the Warriors began their five-season run of dominance.'
b'After the Warriors won a league-record 73 games in 2015-16 but blew a 3-1 lead to the LeBron James-led Cavaliers in the N.B.A. finals, Bogut and the veteran forward Harrison Barnes were quickly jettisoned to Dallas to create the requisite salary-cap space for Golden State to sign Kevin Durant.'
b'Bogut, though, said that returning to the Warriors nearly three years later to play alongside Durant would not \xe2\x80\x9cbe weird\xe2\x80\x9d despite the contentious nature of his departure.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe Golden State Warriors are a very special organization in my heart,\xe2\x80\x9d Bogut said. \xe2\x80\x9cI had a lot of great years there and won a championship. Even though they moved me, it was understandable to get a guy like Kevin Durant. I probably would have traded myself if I had the same opportunity.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was Bogut\xe2\x80\x99s longtime agent, David Bauman of Independent Sports and Entertainment, who first pointed out to him that Wednesday\xe2\x80\x99s signing with the Warriors coincided with the two-year anniversary of the fractured tibia in his left leg that Bogut sustained 56 seconds into his Cleveland Cavaliers debut in March 2017.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just funny how the world works sometimes,\xe2\x80\x9d Bogut said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is an unbelievable opportunity that I\xe2\x80\x99m really thankful for.\xe2\x80\x9d'
