b'Times Insider'
b'For basketball reporters, April means it\xe2\x80\x99s time to kiss the family goodbye and set off on the year\xe2\x80\x99s most thrilling \xe2\x80\x94 and exhausting \xe2\x80\x94 reporting trail.'
b'By Harvey Araton'
b'Times Insider explains who we are and what we do, and delivers behind-the-scenes insights into how our journalism comes together.'
b'The N.B.A. playoffs begin this weekend, which for those who report regularly on the world\xe2\x80\x99s premier professional basketball league means one thing: the temporary suspension of life as they know it.'
b'If it\xe2\x80\x99s April, it\xe2\x80\x99s time to tie up loose ends at home, kiss the significant other or beloved cat goodbye and wish the kids well on the soccer pitch. Someone please remember to send Mother\xe2\x80\x99s Day flowers. Father\xe2\x80\x99s Day will be celebrated pending the length of the finals.'
b'The reporting grind of the 82-game regular season is disruptively hectic enough. But during the postseason, the sport sheds its least watchable teams, as well as a few that are competitively marginal, and gets down to the games that conclusively matter.'
b'Breakout performances will become instant classics. Acknowledged stars could transition into legends with championship rings. Nothing may be missed in the postseason business of media-driven mythmaking.'
b'Will Stephen Curry of the Golden State Warriors win a fourth ring in June, bringing him within two of Michael Jordan\xe2\x80\x99s and Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\xe2\x80\x99s half-dozen each (though still far behind Bill Russell\xe2\x80\x99s 11)? Or will destiny call upon a first-timer like the so-called Greek Freak, Giannis Antetokounmpo of the rising Milwaukee Bucks?'
b'As a sports reporter and columnist for four decades, the last 25 years of which were with The Times, the playoffs habitually meant two months of missing the springtime sun and \xe2\x80\x94 by the early 1990s \xe2\x80\x94 my two young sons, while chasing the extended N.B.A. family of one-name luminaries. (You know who I mean: Magic, Larry, Michael, LeBron.)'
b'Throughout the playoffs, reporters must confront the crush of late-night deadlines while nattily dressed superstars complicate filing by taking their sweet time getting to the interview podium. Hours later, it\xe2\x80\x99s on to the next city, the next round, often dealing with the logistical conundrum of never being sure when one series will end and the next will begin.'
b'For a portion of my years on the basketball beat, that meant attaching myself to the Knicks, who children of a certain age might have a hard time believing consistently qualified for the playoffs. That was way back in the 1990s, otherwise known around New York as the Patrick Ewing Era.'
b'When Ewing\xe2\x80\x99s Knicks were ousted, it was on to chronicle Michael Jordan and his Chicago Bulls as they accumulated six titles in eight years, disbanding in 1998 and ceding short-term control of the sport to the Los Angeles Lakers of Shaquille O\xe2\x80\x99Neal and Kobe Bryant. And so it went, into a new century that spawned even greater global exposure and scrutiny of a virtual one-man industry, LeBron James Inc.'
b'For those having slept through the last six months, James will not be appearing in the 2019 playoffs after a gargantuan run of reaching the league championship series for eight straight years. His migration to Hollywood from Cleveland produced a critically assailed version of Lakers Showtime that, had he not signed a four-year contract last summer, would have already been canceled. (The Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 hope of attracting a worthy co-star is as yet unrealized.)'
b'Hence, the fortunes of the soon-to-be free agents Kevin Durant, Kawhi Leonard and others will be fascinating spring subplots. No reporters worth their credentials will risk blinking through a telltale expression or a body-language betrayal of otherwise guarded intentions.'
b'The playoffs, while typically impassioned and illuminating, are also logistically exhausting, but I confidently speak for my N.B.A. media brethren when I say that covering them is far more privilege than punishment.'
b'The game looks much different now \xe2\x80\x94 so much of it focused on 3-point shooting \xe2\x80\x94 than it did during my earliest years on the N.B.A. beat. Back then, I routinely insisted there was no place in the world I would rather be than the old, ventilation-challenged Boston Garden for a showdown between the Celtics and Lakers. The modern and far more international N.B.A. media no doubt is equally passionate.'
b'But lives do change. Issues arise. We in the ever-more-distant press-row seats do not attend games with traditional partisan interests, but over the long playoff haul, personal circumstances and needs do create some dilemmas.'
b'Consider my plight in the final seconds of Game 6 of the 1993 finals between Jordan\xe2\x80\x99s Bulls and Charles Barkley\xe2\x80\x99s Phoenix Suns. The Bulls were leading in the series three games to two, but were trailing by 2 points while trying to avoid playing a seventh game in a hostile road arena.'
b'Back home in Brooklyn, my wife was seven months pregnant with our second child while simultaneously preparing to sell our co-op and buy a house in New Jersey. Had the Bulls lost Game 6, I would not have made it home until the night before both closings and the move.'
b'Fortunately for me, if not the Suns, all five Bulls touched the ball on a play that produced a historically clutch 3-point shot by John Paxson. The Bulls\xe2\x80\x99 bid for a third straight title survived, along with my marriage.'
b'Harvey Araton is the editor and annotator of \xe2\x80\x9cElevated: The Global Rise of the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x9d (Triumph), an archival book of selected works by the staff of The New York Times. Follow the @ReaderCenter on Twitter for more coverage highlighting your perspectives and experiences and for insight into how we work.'

b'By Marc Stein'
b'With all of the trade drama surrounding Anthony Davis and Kristaps Porzingis, the N.B.A. intruded on the N.F.L.\xe2\x80\x99s run-up to the Super Bowl as we have not seen since Kobe Bryant scored 81 points on football\xe2\x80\x99s so-called Championship Sunday in 2006.'
b'Now that the Super Bowl is over and even more of North America\xe2\x80\x99s sporting consciousness is there to be seized by professional basketball\xe2\x80\x99s tireless headline-makers, here is our best advice: Buckle up.'
b'What follows is a by-the-numbers look at what the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s 73rd season has served up so far \xe2\x80\x94 and what the next five months hold.'
b'Through Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s games, only the Milwaukee Bucks were on a 60-win pace. The Bucks\xe2\x80\x99 Eastern Conference-leading record of 38-13 projects to a 61-win campaign \xe2\x80\x94 which could keep this season from being the league\xe2\x80\x99s first since 2000-1 without a 60-win club.'
b'There are realistically 11 teams battling for the Western Conference\xe2\x80\x99s eight playoff spots, after the new calendar year began with 14 teams in the conference \xe2\x80\x94 all but Phoenix \xe2\x80\x94 in the race. Dallas, New Orleans and Memphis have dropped off in January, prompting all three teams to focus more on trades than the standings.'
b'The consensus top three in the Most Valuable Player Award race coming out of Super Bowl weekend are Milwaukee\xe2\x80\x99s Giannis Antetokounmpo, Houston\xe2\x80\x99s James Harden and Denver\xe2\x80\x99s Nikola Jokic. According to the Basketball-Reference.com M.V.P. Award Tracker, Antetokounmpo awoke Sunday with a 37.8 percent chance of winning \xe2\x80\x94 far ahead of Harden\xe2\x80\x99s 21.1 percent.'
b'Harden has scored at least 30 points in 26 consecutive games, good for the third-longest such streak in N.B.A. annals behind Wilt Chamberlain\xe2\x80\x99s streaks of 65 and 31.'
b'The league\xe2\x80\x99s trade deadline (Thursday at 3 p.m. Eastern) is three days away. This is the second season since 1978-79 (as far back as reliable N.B.A. record-keeping goes) that the deadline falls before the All-Star Game.'
b'The New Orleans Pelicans have made two trips to the playoffs \xe2\x80\x94 winning only one series \xe2\x80\x94 in Davis\xe2\x80\x99s first six seasons with the team. Davis requested a trade on Jan. 28.'
b'It took 54 days for the Minnesota Timberwolves to find a trade they liked for Jimmy Butler after Butler\xe2\x80\x99s request to be dealt became public Sept. 18. Butler was snubbed by East coaches in All-Star voting, but the potential ceiling for Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s rugged new star threesome was evident Thursday night at Golden State, when Joel Embiid, Ben Simmons, Butler and Company brought a halt to the longest winning streak of the season \xe2\x80\x94 after the Warriors had won 11 in a row.'
b'Minnesota is 21-18 since the trade that sent Butler and Justin Patton to Philadelphia on Nov. 12 \xe2\x80\x94 and 6-6 since firing Tom Thibodeau, the coach/team president who made it, on Jan. 6. Ryan Saunders, Thibodeau\xe2\x80\x99s 32-year-old replacement, has many admirers around the league, but the Wolves are a long way from convincing skeptics that the deal (to bring in Robert Covington, Dario Saric, Jerryd Bayless and a 2022 second-round pick) was sufficient for a player of Butler\xe2\x80\x99s caliber.'
b'Thibodeau is one of three coaches to be fired this season \xe2\x80\x94 after nine coaching changes in the off-season. The other coaches to lose their jobs since opening night: Cleveland\xe2\x80\x99s Tyronn Lue and Chicago\xe2\x80\x99s Fred Hoiberg.'
b'There were 20 teams, entering Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s play, attempting at least 30 3-pointers a game. This is poised to become the first season in N.B.A. history that the leaguewide average per game (31.4) will finish in the 30s.'
b'With coaches calling for more 3-pointers than ever before and greenlighting shots earlier and earlier in the 24-second shot clock \xe2\x80\x94 along with a new rule that resets the shot clock at 14 seconds on offensive rebounds \xe2\x80\x94 teams are averaging 100.0 possessions per 48 minutes leaguewide. The last N.B.A. season in which that figure finished in triple digits was 1988-89 (100.6).'
b'Milwaukee\xe2\x80\x99s Khris Middleton, Orlando\xe2\x80\x99s Nikola Vucevic, Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s Simmons and Denver\xe2\x80\x99s Jokic will make their All-Star Game debuts Feb. 17 in Charlotte, N.C. The All-Star player draft, in which the captains LeBron James and Antetokounmpo will fill out 13-man rosters by picking players playground-style, is Thursday at 7 p.m. \xe2\x80\x94 just four hours after the trade deadline passes. (D\xe2\x80\x99Angelo Russell of the Nets, who was named later as a replacement for Indiana\xe2\x80\x99s Victor Oladipo, who is injured, will also be making his All-Star debut this year.)'
b'Four teams are in contention for the league\xe2\x80\x99s worst record: Phoenix (11-43), Cleveland (11-42), Chicago (12-41) and, of course, the Knicks (10-42). The teams that finish in the bottom three will share a 14 percent chance of landing the No. 1 overall pick in the draft in June in the first year of the league\xe2\x80\x99s revised lottery system.'
b'San Antonio sits a surprising fifth in the West, at 32-22, in its first season since trading Kawhi Leonard to Toronto in July. The Spurs are bidding for a record 22nd consecutive playoff berth, a streak that began in Gregg Popovich\xe2\x80\x99s first full season as Spurs coach in 1997-98.'
b'At 27-25, Sacramento is on course to post its first winning record since the 2005-6 season. But the Kings will have to leapfrog at least two teams to stop the league\xe2\x80\x99s longest playoff drought (12 seasons). The Suns (nine seasons) and the Orlando Magic (seven) are on course to extend their own playoff droughts.'
b'The Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 playoff drought will hit a hard-to-believe six seasons in a row if James cannot save Los Angeles over its final 29 games. James just missed 17 consecutive games with a strained groin \xe2\x80\x94 the longest injury absence of his pro career \xe2\x80\x94 and is at risk for missing the postseason for the first time since his second N.B.A. season, in 2004-5.'
b'Carmelo Anthony finally became an unrestricted free agent on Sunday after clearing waivers nearly three months after the Houston Rockets sent him away in November after just 10 games together. The Rockets traded Anthony to Chicago on Jan. 21; the Bulls, who needed a roster spot, waived him Friday without him spending a single second with the team.'
b'In the seven games Golden State has deployed a lineup of DeMarcus Cousins, Stephen Curry, Kevin Durant, Klay Thompson and Draymond Green, that group is averaging 127.1 points per 100 possessions in 54 minutes. Call it a small but ominous sample size.'
b'Oddsmakers in Las Vegas have the Warriors as overwhelming favorites to win their third consecutive championship and fourth in five seasons. According to ActionNetwork.com, Golden State is -225 to win it all, meaning that you would have to bet $225 to win $100. Boston, Milwaukee and Toronto are next in line at +1,000, meaning that a $100 bet would win $1,000 if any of those teams won the title.'

b'The Mavericks rookie is drawing LeBron James comparisons and has \xe2\x80\x9cfast-forwarded\xe2\x80\x9d his team\xe2\x80\x99s decision-making.'
b'By Marc Stein'
b'DALLAS \xe2\x80\x94 Dirk Nowitzki has seen many things in his 21 seasons with the Dallas Mavericks. What he had never seen, until last month, was a fellow Maverick who could attract nearly two dozen autograph seekers in subzero temperatures to greet the team bus on a Thursday morning in Detroit.'
b'Luka Doncic did just that in the 2 a.m. hour of Jan. 31, as the Mavericks pulled into a hotel adjacent to the world headquarters of General Motors, on the unglamorous end of a back-to-back set that began in New York.'
b'It is likewise safe to presume that none of Nowitzki\xe2\x80\x99s other 197 teammates over two decades in Dallas could have inspired what happened mere hours later. In a swift-moving blockbuster trade, Dallas acquired Kristaps Porzingis from the Knicks to serve as Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s sidekick, with Mavericks General Manager Donnie Nelson openly admitting that he pushed for the deal because Doncic has \xe2\x80\x9cfast-forwarded a lot of our decision-making.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'These are the tales from just one day, albeit maybe the wildest day, of what Nowitzki frequently refers to as Lukamania.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen we get to cities now, even late at night, there are so many people waiting with things for him to sign that it\xe2\x80\x99s almost like we\xe2\x80\x99re the Warriors,\xe2\x80\x9d Nowitzki said. \xe2\x80\x9cLukamania is real. We\xe2\x80\x99re living it every day.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'[Another Rookie: The Perimeter Can\xe2\x80\x99t Protect You From Mitchell Robinson]'
b'This week brings another milestone for Doncic, who celebrates his 20th birthday on Thursday. He is averaging 20.9 points, 7.2 rebounds and 5.7 assists through 56 games and is responsible for four of the five triple-doubles in N.B.A. history recorded by teenagers. It is a start that has quickly validated Nelson\xe2\x80\x99s long-held belief that Doncic possessed superstar potential.'
b'The only other rookie in league history to hit those levels over a full season was Oscar Robertson in 1960-61.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI love, love, love guys that can pass the ball,\xe2\x80\x9d Nelson said, prioritizing Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s ability to run a team at 6 feet 7 inches over the fact he is already known for having the league\xe2\x80\x99s second-most-feared step-back jump shot, behind only James Harden\xe2\x80\x99s.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew I could play over here,\xe2\x80\x9d Doncic said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut it\xe2\x80\x99s better than I expected, for sure.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The gaudy numbers and worldwide interest in his exploits enabled Doncic to amass more than four million votes in N.B.A. All-Star balloting, trailing only LeBron James and Giannis Antetokounmpo. Doncic, in other words, finished higher in leaguewide balloting than Michael Jordan (fifth) did as a rookie. Higher, too, than James (13th) and even Yao Ming, who could manage only the fourth-highest total in 2003 despite the considerable voting might of Yao\xe2\x80\x99s native China.'
b'Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s instant production has also validated every pundit who insisted, amid no shortage of skepticism, that concerns about Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s athleticism and corresponding ability to deal with the length of N.B.A. defenders were folly given the rampant success he achieved both at the club (Real Madrid) and national team (Slovenia) levels as an 18-year-old. In the process, Doncic has unleashed a torrent of second-guessing upon the teams (Phoenix, Sacramento and Atlanta) that let him slip to the Mavericks. '
b'Yet Doncic insists his maiden N.B.A. season, which appears destined to be christened with the league\xe2\x80\x99s rookie of the year trophy, has not been as easy it looks.'
b'The Mavericks, you see, were 26-34 entering Wednesday night\xe2\x80\x99s home date with Indiana and likely to miss the playoffs for a third consecutive season. They have traded away all four of Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s projected fellow starters (Dennis Smith Jr., DeAndre Jordan, Wes Matthews and Harrison Barnes) in deals that netted Porzingis and roughly $30 million in salary-cap space, neither of which can help the team this season.'
b'It is the first time in Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s life, since he took up basketball at age 7, that he has experienced losing. One hint of how well he\xe2\x80\x99s coping with it: Doncic has pulled his jersey apart in frustration after a play gone awry \xe2\x80\x94 twice.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s harder than people think,\xe2\x80\x9d Doncic said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a winner \xe2\x80\x94 he won everything in Europe,\xe2\x80\x9d Juancho Hernangomez of the Denver Nuggets said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo every time he loses, he gets so mad.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hernangomez has been observing Doncic from close range for years, both on the floor \xe2\x80\x94 since Doncic played alongside Hernangomez\xe2\x80\x99s brother, Charlotte\xe2\x80\x99s Willy Hernangomez, at Real Madrid \xe2\x80\x94 and through their shared WhatsApp chat room, which houses various European players fond of the popular video game Fortnite. But Mavericks officials are not worried about a scouting report from a friend that paints Doncic as a sore loser.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe doesn\xe2\x80\x99t handle losing well \xe2\x80\x94 I know that for a fact,\xe2\x80\x9d Dallas Coach Rick Carlisle said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I don\xe2\x80\x99t handle losing well, either.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As recently as May 15, Mavericks executives were worried about Doncic \xe2\x80\x94 big time. Having known for more than a year that they wanted to draft him if they had the chance, team officials were crestfallen in Chicago when Dallas slipped from a projected No. 3 in that night\xe2\x80\x99s draft lottery to No. 5. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was devastating for us,\xe2\x80\x9d Nelson said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe thought our chance to get him was gone because it\xe2\x80\x99s really hard to trade up in the lottery.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Nowitzki betrayed a public hint of the organization\xe2\x80\x99s disappointment when he tweeted this reaction: \xe2\x80\x9cOf course.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'To move up high enough, Dallas ultimately had to persuade the Atlanta Hawks to surrender the No. 3 overall pick. It cost Dallas both the No. 5 pick, which Atlanta used to take Trae Young, as well as the Mavericks\xe2\x80\x99 top pick in the 2019 draft. '
b'But the Dallas owner, Mark Cuban, blessed the deal, even at that price, because Nelson lobbied so hard for it. Five years earlier, during the 2013 draft, Nelson and his longtime international scout, Tony Ronzone, pushed for the Mavericks to use the No. 13 pick on a little-known Greek teenager named Giannis Antetokounmpo. Cuban wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t allow it, given that Antetokounmpo, unlike Doncic, was mostly a mystery \xe2\x80\x94 and promptly regretted it as Antetokounmpo blossomed into a star in Milwaukee.'
b'So this time, after the disappointment of the lottery, Cuban blessed Nelson to do whatever it took to land Doncic. What the team got was the son of a former Slovene pro \xe2\x80\x94 Sasa Doncic \xe2\x80\x94 and a veteran of three full seasons in the EuroLeague and Spain\xe2\x80\x99s La Liga with Real Madrid after Luka Doncic made his pro debut at 16.'
b'To the Mavericks\xe2\x80\x99 delight, Doncic was more N.B.A.-ready than they ever dreamed \xe2\x80\x94 as his 16-for-29 shooting in the final three minutes of one-possession games this season would suggest. As Carlisle put it: \xe2\x80\x9cUnique background, unique skill set, unique body type.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI hesitate to throw out names like LeBron James and Magic Johnson, who have been do-everything kind of stars, but it\xe2\x80\x99s pretty clear now that Luka has many of those same traits and has proven that he can do a lot of those things,\xe2\x80\x9d Carlisle said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe has deceptive size, strength and quickness \xe2\x80\x94 and an understanding beyond his years on how to use his body to make plays and draw fouls.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Carlisle is hardly alone in making such lofty comparisons. Miami\xe2\x80\x99s Dwyane Wade, one of the league\xe2\x80\x99s foremost James experts after their four seasons together with the Heat, has called Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s passing \xe2\x80\x9cLeBron-like.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'Los Angeles Clippers Coach Doc Rivers said of Doncic: \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s my favorite player to watch almost, and not talking just rookies. First of all, he plays with a great joy \xe2\x80\x94 I love that. And he\xe2\x80\x99s just so advanced in the way he plays. The sky\xe2\x80\x99s the limit for him. Wait until he gets in shape.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Rivers was laughing when he tacked on that last line, but he did hit on a prime area of Year 1 concern with Doncic \xe2\x80\x94 conditioning.'
b'The Mavericks and Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s representatives, headed by the longtime N.B.A. agent Bill Duffy, agreed shortly after the draft to impose as much rest on Doncic as possible from July through September after a nonstop run at the highest levels of international basketball for nearly a year. Doncic thus began the season heavier than his listed weight of 218 and has absorbed jibes about his diet ever since.'
b'But Mavericks officials are pleased with the gradual changes in Doncic\xe2\x80\x99s dietary habits. At the team\xe2\x80\x99s behest, Doncic hired a chef in December to prepare a number of meals for pregame and off-night consumption. Doncic has also begun working fresh juices into his routine.'
b'In Madrid, Doncic lived for the past two and a half years with his mother, Mirjam Poterbin, who raised Doncic while running two beauty salons in Ljubljana. (Doncic has long declined to discuss his father.)'
b'In Dallas, mom and son live separately near the American Airlines Center as Doncic grows into his independence, but still within walking distance.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis was his dream,\xe2\x80\x9d Poterbin said. \xe2\x80\x9cAt 7 years old he was already talking about N.B.A. I cry a lot of times.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Yet there have been Year 1 challenges and disappointments for Doncic amid the Lukamania \xe2\x80\x94 and beyond the ever-present adjustment to playing for a team with scant postseason prospects.'
b'He watched helplessly as his fellow Spanish-speaking teammate J.J. Barea suffered a season-ending Achilles\xe2\x80\x99 tear in January. He lived through his first big trade, seeing Dallas abruptly abort its planned Doncic/Smith Jr. partnership when the chance arose to acquire his pal Porzingis.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was shocked,\xe2\x80\x9d Doncic said. \xe2\x80\x9cEurope doesn\xe2\x80\x99t work like this.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Doncic has also struggled at times with his free throws, converting just 72.6 percent this season despite proving so adept at getting to the line (6.4 times per game). Instead, the Magic passed the ball around a few times, finding a wide-open Jerian Grant in the corner, 22 feet from a supine Robinson.'
b'In three seconds that defied reasonable expectation, Robinson got to his feet, raced toward the corner and leapt into the air. He fully extended his lanky 7-foot-1 frame and swatted the 3-point attempt out of midair so matter-of-factly that Grant pulled his hands toward his body, looking almost sorry that he had attempted the shot.'
b'The block was Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s eighth of the game, setting a Knicks rookie record (which he stretched to nine blocks by the end of the night). But beyond the block\xe2\x80\x99s impact in the moment, the play illustrated the 20-year-old\xe2\x80\x99s approach to this season. The perception may be that the Knicks are tanking in hopes of drafting Duke\xe2\x80\x99s Zion Williamson, but for Robinson, any shot an opponent takes is a chance for him to get a block \xe2\x80\x94 and he is not going to be cheated out of any of them, even if the shooter is beyond the 3-point line. As a result, a mostly irrelevant team has become must-watch television.'
b'Last time we met the Magic @thegarden, @23savage____ set the Knicks rookie record for blocks \xe2\x9c\x8b Another block party tonight? \xf0\x9f\x91\x80 pic.twitter.com/3RgRQoROec'
b'The Knicks had not forgotten that November block when the Magic came back to Madison Square Garden on Tuesday. The team posted a video of the play on Twitter, wondering if history would repeat. The post proved prophetic, as Robinson led the way in a 108-103 victory for the Knicks with 17 points, 14 rebounds, 6 blocks and 3 steals in 33 minutes off the bench. Four of the blocks came in just 40 seconds in the second quarter.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe kid is making history right now,\xe2\x80\x9d Knicks Coach David Fizdale said of Robinson after the win. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s putting himself in groups with historic names. Every single day he continues to grow and get better.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Knicks\xe2\x80\x99 two-game winning streak ended on Thursday with a disappointing 125-118 loss to the Cleveland Cavaliers. But even in defeat, Robinson managed to add to his highlight reel, this time with a shot an opponent didn\xe2\x80\x99t take. '
b'It was early in the second quarter, and Cavaliers guard Matthew Dellavedova got the ball with a clean look at the basket from 3-point range. As he prepared to shoot, he noticed Robinson a few feet in front of him, with the rookie lowering his shoulder slightly as he prepared to leap. Dellavedova immediately thought better of trying his luck and passed the ball instead. A few seconds later on the same possession, Robinson got his block anyway, swatting away a layup attempt from Marquese Chriss.'
b'A rare prep-to-pro N.B.A. player as a result of his complicated withdrawal from Western Kentucky University, Robinson has been limited to 18.6 minutes a game as he works to refine his game, but he is still third in the N.B.A. at 2.3 blocks a game. When rated by block percentage, which estimates the percentage of an opponents\xe2\x80\x99 shots a player blocks in his time on the floor, Robinson is nothing short of stunning, at 10.4 percent.'
b'Basketball Reference has tracked block percentage back to the 1973-74 season, and the top-four seasons among players with 100 or more blocks belong to Manute Bol, the 7-foot-7 shot-blocking savant. No. 5 on the list belongs to Robinson. '
b'Sample size obviously needs to be considered, but Robinson stands a chance of being the only qualified player beyond Bol and Alonzo Mourning to finish a season with a block percentage higher than 10. Rim protection luminaries such as Serge Ibaka (9.8), Mark Eaton (9.2) and Dikembe Mutombo (8.8) all fell short of that mark in their best seasons. '
b'Robinson, who has quickly become a fan favorite, believes he is just getting started. He was asked recently how many shots he could block a game if the team let him play 30 minutes a night. \xe2\x80\x9cProbably around six,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI feel like I can get like six.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The N.B.A. season record for blocks per game is 5.6, set by Eaton in 1984-85, yet Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s boast does not seem all that far-fetched, largely because of his unusual ability to block shots along the perimeter as well as under the basket.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHis potential is crazy,\xe2\x80\x9d Emmanuel Mudiay, the Knicks guard, told reporters before Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s game. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s probably the best shot-blocker I ever played with in my life. In my opinion, he\xe2\x80\x99s the best shot-blocker in the league.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Fizdale has said that Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s confidence and execution have improved since the team acquired DeAndre Jordan to serve as his mentor. The numbers back that up, as Robinson has averaged 11 points, 8.7 rebounds and 3.2 blocks a game since Jordan\xe2\x80\x99s arrival on Jan. 31, while still averaging only 23.1 minutes a night. He has also continued to pester outside shooters, with eight of his 35 blocks in February coming on 3-point attempts. '
b'Fizdale was asked recently if Robinson compared to any other players he had coached. The coach, who has worked with excellent rim protectors like Marc Gasol, Jermaine O\xe2\x80\x99Neal and Chris Andersen, spoke about his rookie like a proud father.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNo,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a different guy, and he\xe2\x80\x99s got so much more room to grow. I\xe2\x80\x99m going to keep my foot way up his butt to make sure he does.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That could be terrible news for anyone looking to get a shot off against the Knicks in the coming years. They might find there is no place to hide.'
b'Benjamin Hoffman is a senior staff editor and regular contributor to the Keeping Score column in sports. He joined The Times in 2005.  @BenHoffmanNYT \xe2\x80\xa2 Facebook '

b'By Marc Tracy'
b'Duke was given the No. 1 overall seed in the N.C.A.A. Division I men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball tournament Sunday night, starting Coach Mike Krzyzewski and his star freshman Zion Williamson on a path to what they hope will be the Blue Devils\xe2\x80\x99 sixth national title.'
b'Duke (29-5) was one of three Atlantic Coast Conference teams to receive top seeds, joining Virginia (29-3) and North Carolina (27-6). It was the second time members of the same conference were named three of the four No. 1s; the Big East did so in 2009.'
b'The fourth No. 1 seed was Gonzaga (30-3), the small stalwart from Spokane, Wash. While the Bulldogs lost the West Coast Conference title game to St. Mary\xe2\x80\x99s last week, they already have a win over Duke on their r\xc3\xa9sum\xc3\xa9 from a tournament in late November in Hawaii.'
b'[Region previews: East | West | South | Midwest]'
b'Of course, a top seed is no ticket to the Final Four in Minneapolis. Or even to the second round. Last year, for the first time in 136 such games, a No. 16 seed defeated a No. 1 when the University of Maryland-Baltimore County stunned Virginia.'
b'The No. 2 seeds are Michigan State (28-6), Tennessee (29-5), Kentucky (27-6) and Michigan (28-6). The first of these edged the last of these in the Big Ten conference final minutes before the bracket was released. Yet it was the defeated Wolverines who received the privilege of placement in the West alongside Gonzaga, while the Spartans \xe2\x80\x94 who won all three games against their in-state rival this season \xe2\x80\x94 landed in Duke\xe2\x80\x99s dreaded quadrant.'
b'The Blue Devils finished the regular season on a 3-3 skid without Williamson, who sprained his knee when his shoe ripped open during a game on Feb. 20. But Williamson, the prospective No. 1 overall pick in the N.B.A. draft, returned last week, and Duke proceeded to stomp through the A.C.C. tournament. Williamson set the Duke scoring record for that event, with 81 points.'
b'The selection committee effectively ignored the non-Williamson .500 squad and instead considered the team that has won every game except for a 2-point loss to Gonzaga and an overtime loss to Syracuse (20-13). It is Duke\xe2\x80\x99s first No. 1 seed since 2015, which is also the last year it won the tournament.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey earned their right to be there,\xe2\x80\x9d said the selection committee chairman, Bernard Muir, who is Stanford\xe2\x80\x99s athletic director, when he appeared on CBS\xe2\x80\x99s selection show to discuss the bracket.'
b'The most challenging of the four regions appeared to be the South, topped by Virginia. If the Cavaliers get past 16-seeded Gardner-Webb (23-11) on Friday \xe2\x80\x94 a game they surely will not take for granted after last year \xe2\x80\x94 they could face a No. 8-seeded Mississippi (20-12) that has four wins over tournament teams. Then potential round of 16 opponents include Wisconsin (23-10), underseeded at No. 5, or fourth-seeded Kansas State (25-8), which came close to the Final Four last year.'
b'The South final could well feature No. 2-seeded Tennessee (29-5) or No. 3-seeded Purdue (23-9). Both teams are ranked in the top 10 of KenPom.com\xe2\x80\x99s efficiency ratings, a list Virginia sits atop. And either might have home-court advantage at Louisville\xe2\x80\x99s KFC Yum Center.'

b'By The New York Times'
b'The region also features two prominent conference champions: sixth-seeded Villanova (25-9), the current Big East and defending national champion, and seventh-seeded Cincinnati (28-6), which won the American Athletic Conference tournament on Sunday.'
b'In addition to Michigan State, the land mines in the East between Duke and the Final Four could include fourth-seeded Virginia Tech (24-8), which defeated the Williamson-less Blue Devils last month, and third-seeded Louisiana State (26-6), a talented squad that is without Coach Will Wade. He was suspended after a report emerged that he had discussed making an offer to a recruit on a phone call with an aspiring agent convicted of fraud in college recruiting.'
b'The East has other ties to scandal. Seventh-seeded Louisville (20-13) faces 10th-seeded Minnesota (21-13) in the first round, a game that might have been a father-son matchup between Rick and Richard Pitino had the former not been let go as Louisville\xe2\x80\x99s coach in 2017 shortly after corruption allegations became public. And L.S.U.\xe2\x80\x99s first game is against No. 14 Yale (21-7), the Ivy League co-champion, whose women\xe2\x80\x99s soccer program was caught up in the admissions scandal that federal prosecutors revealed last week.'
b'In the national semifinals, the East winner, which will be determined in Washington, will face the West winner. In addition to Gonzaga and Michigan, contenders in that region include third-seeded Texas Tech (26-6), which was considered the best team in the strong Big 12 but was upset in the conference tournament by West Virginia (14-20); and fourth-seeded Florida State (27-7), which looked every bit Duke\xe2\x80\x99s equal in the first half of the A.C.C. title game on Saturday. The West also features two mid-major darlings: No. 6 Buffalo (31-3) and No. 7 Nevada (29-4). The West Regional is in Anaheim, Calif.'
b'North Carolina and Kentucky are fish out of water in the Midwest region, particularly given its setting. In the region semifinals, the Tar Heels could meet fourth-seeded Kansas (25-9), making its record-setting 30th straight N.C.A.A. tournament appearance, while the Wildcats might face sixth-seeded Iowa State (23-11). Those games will take place at Sprint Center in Kansas City, Mo. \xe2\x80\x94 a second home for the Jayhawks and Iowa State, who have combined to win the last seven Big 12 tournaments there.'
b'The Midwest also features fifth-seeded Auburn (25-9), the surprise Southeastern Conference winner Sunday. Tigers Coach Bruce Pearl, hired in 2014, was effectively barred from N.C.A.A. coaching for three years for recruiting violations at Tennessee. Chuck Person, a former Auburn assistant, was charged with bribery and fraud in the recruiting cases, and last Friday, prosecutors said in a court filing that Person was expected to plead guilty on Tuesday.'
b'The Big Ten led all conferences with eight teams in the tournament, while the Pacific-12 had only three. That number was actually larger than expected a week ago: Arizona State was given one of the last four at-large bids, and Oregon (23-13) surprised Washington (26-8) in the tournament final Saturday night to elbow its way into the field.'
b'The Ducks were one of several unlikely receivers of automatic spots who effectively constricted the pool of 36 at-large bids. In another example, St. Louis (23-12) won the Atlantic 10 tournament Sunday, granting the Billikens a slot alongside Virginia Commonwealth (25-7), which effectively took an at-large bid away from a bubble team by failing to win its conference tournament.'
b'This was the first year in decades that the N.C.A.A. did not use the much-maligned Rating Percentage Index, instead favoring the new N.C.A.A. Evaluation Tool. But the tournament field included 11th-seeded Arizona State (22-10) in its \xe2\x80\x9clast four in\xe2\x80\x9d despite the Sun Devils\xe2\x80\x99 poor NET, while North Carolina State (22-11), a good-NET, bad-R.P.I. squad, was not even among the \xe2\x80\x9cfirst four out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But aficionados will be pleased that Belmont (26-5) of the Ohio Valley earned an at-large bid; the Bruins will play Temple in the play-in game on Tuesday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey made the most of the opportunities they had,\xe2\x80\x9d Muir said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe just thought they were a phenomenal basketball team, very high on the offensive front \xe2\x80\x94 great offensive efficiency.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'St. John\xe2\x80\x99s (21-12) was the last team in; the Red Storm will face Arizona State in an opening game on Wednesday.'

b'On Pro Basketball'
b'The rare N.B.A. star willing to lean into his role as a villain, Butler, briefly back in the city he scorned, is ready to absorb fans\xe2\x80\x99 anger.'
b'By Marc Stein'
b'Jimmy Butler knows what\xe2\x80\x99s coming on Saturday night in Minneapolis. He understands, relishes and even encourages the looming prospect of the chilliest welcome any visiting N.B.A. player is bound to receive this season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re going to boo me,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said of the Minnesota fans who watched him force his way out of town via a trade to the Philadelphia 76ers in November \xe2\x80\x94 months after Butler led the woebegone Timberwolves to their first playoff berth in 14 seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI would boo me, too. I\xe2\x80\x99m not going to lie to you.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Now a key member of what is widely regarded as the most potent starting lineup on the N.B.A. map outside of Golden State, Butler will be back at Target Center for the first time since the trade turmoil that captivated the league for the first two months of the season.'
b'Butler insisted he was unfazed by what awaited him, and went on to suggest that a number of his Philadelphia colleagues, as well as some longtime friends who plan to be in attendance, will partake in the inevitable hostilities.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI might actually join in on the boos,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said.'
b'Those who have spent any time around the rugged swingman surely don\xe2\x80\x99t doubt it. At a time when N.B.A. Commissioner Adam Silver openly frets about player happiness \xe2\x80\x94 and when standouts such as Boston\xe2\x80\x99s Kyrie Irving and Golden State\xe2\x80\x99s Kevin Durant routinely rail against the approach of some of the news media \xe2\x80\x94 Butler is the rare star who savors the game\xe2\x80\x99s edgy side and has embraced his portrayal as a villain.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI love it,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said in a phone interview, repeating the phrase three times \xe2\x80\x94 including once with a profanity for emphasis. \xe2\x80\x9cWho wants to be loved all the time?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s O.K. It\xe2\x80\x99s fine. I don\xe2\x80\x99t need everybody to like me. I know who I am. I can\xe2\x80\x99t say that enough. I know what I\xe2\x80\x99m about. I know where my heart is. People will say, \xe2\x80\x98He\xe2\x80\x99s this way, or he\xe2\x80\x99s that way,\xe2\x80\x99 but nobody knows except for the people around me every day. Ask them and they\xe2\x80\x99ll tell you differently.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Elton Brand, the 76ers\xe2\x80\x99 general manager, certainly falls within that category, describing Butler as \xe2\x80\x9ca caring person\xe2\x80\x9d who has quickly endeared himself \xe2\x80\x9cnot only to his teammates but to our whole business operations staff and in the community.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As a first-year general manager, Brand had his own reservations before going through with the first major move of his tenure, having watched chaos engulf the Timberwolves from afar \xe2\x80\x94 with no shortage of the noise coming from Butler himself after news leaked of the mid-September trade request he made in private.'
b'But when Brand did his research, consulting former coaches and executives who had worked with Butler, along with former players he knew well who had firsthand knowledge, such as Nazr Mohammed and Mike Dunleavy Jr., he received little in the way of dissenting feedback.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEven with the story that was reported, that wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a big deal,\xe2\x80\x9d Brand said, referring to an ESPN report in January that asserted Butler \xe2\x80\x9caggressively challenged\xe2\x80\x9d Philadelphia Coach Brett Brown. \xe2\x80\x9cHe didn\xe2\x80\x99t curse. He wasn\xe2\x80\x99t loud. It was his reputation following him.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Butler, 29, admitted in a recent interview with Yahoo Sports\xe2\x80\x99s Chris Haynes that he is a \xe2\x80\x9cconfrontational\xe2\x80\x9d teammate, but that he is also trying to be more selective in showing his blunt nature as he gets older. It should be noted that, as Brand found, Butler has also been a largely popular teammate in his stints with the Chicago Bulls and Team U.S.A. \xe2\x80\x94 and, frankly, with numerous Timberwolves apart from the All-Star center Karl-Anthony Towns.'
b'Butler took a hit in some precincts after informing the since-fired coach with whom he\xe2\x80\x99s so closely associated \xe2\x80\x94 Tom Thibodeau \xe2\x80\x94 that he was no longer interested in trying to nurture Towns and Andrew Wiggins and wanted out of Minnesota. One example of the damage: Butler is one of the top 12 players in the Eastern Conference, but East coaches snubbed him as a reserve for the All-Star Game in February.'
b'Yet Butler plays on, insisting he would \xe2\x80\x9cdo nothing over\xe2\x80\x9d in Minnesota and reveling in the knowledge that for the first time in his career, he\xe2\x80\x99s on a team capable of getting to the N.B.A. finals.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI will tell you that we\xe2\x80\x99ve got a lot of talent,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said.'
b'The Sixers haven\xe2\x80\x99t established the required consistency to earn the label of East favorites, going 11-6 since the All-Star break with middling placement in both offensive (18th) and defensive (12th) efficiency in that span. Butler, though, is doing what he can to make it work, sacrificing in a manner that would seem to invalidate some of the criticism.'
b'Philadelphia followed its trade for Butler on Nov. 12 by acquiring Tobias Harris from the Los Angeles Clippers on Feb. 6, giving Brown two All-Star-caliber players to team with the dynamic duo of Joel Embiid and Ben Simmons and the shooter extraordinaire J.J. Redick. In the first 20 games since, when those five players share the floor, Butler has scaled back more than anyone, taking fewer shots (46) than the other four \xe2\x80\x94 with Embiid by far in the lead (95 shots).'
b'Of course, in fourth quarters, Butler has emerged as the most reliable offensive option of the quintet, shooting 12 for 18 when all five play together, highlighted by last week\xe2\x80\x99s game-winning jumper against Boston after the Celtics had won six of the teams\xe2\x80\x99 seven previous meetings. The natural drop in Butler\xe2\x80\x99s per-game averages this season, playing for such a loaded team, tends to overshadow the fact that he still ranks 16th in the league in a category (Real Plus-Minus) strongly associated with team success.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a special talent at closing and winning games \xe2\x80\x94 and not just offensively,\xe2\x80\x9d Brand said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s just a winner.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'An indication of Butler\xe2\x80\x99s true standing in the game will come July 1, when he becomes an unrestricted free agent for the first time. Brand has said repeatedly that he hopes to keep Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s new core four together, but Butler is expected to attract serious interest from both Los Angeles teams as well as the Nets. The Clippers\xe2\x80\x99 special adviser Jerry West, to name one prominent fan, is said to be a longtime admirer of Butler\xe2\x80\x99s two-way impact.'
b'Not that Butler is prepared to discuss much about the future. He brushed off free-agency talk in our conversation and claimed that he didn\xe2\x80\x99t even know Minnesota was on this week\xe2\x80\x99s calendar until I told him.'
b'He stuck mostly to peripheral subjects. Those include Butler\xe2\x80\x99s devotion to playing dominoes and Uno, his friendship with \xe2\x80\x9cthe best soccer player in the world\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 Paris St.-Germain\xe2\x80\x99s Brazilian star Neymar \xe2\x80\x94 and the trusty American football he travels around with. Butler said he plans to toss the football with other 76ers with greater regularity during the playoffs.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m telling you \xe2\x80\x94 it takes away some of that pressure,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said.'
b'Thibodeau still lives in Minneapolis in the wake of his Jan. 6 firing, but politely declined to comment about Butler\xe2\x80\x99s visit. Butler, for his part, continues to refer to Thibodeau as \xe2\x80\x9cmy guy.\xe2\x80\x9d He said they maintained regular contact.'
b'Although Butler remains unwilling to dig deeply into the reasons he pushed so hard for an exit so soon after the dramatic impact he had in his lone full season with the Wolves, give him this: He is prepared to take whatever pent-up frustration has been stored up for him in the Twin Cities.'
b'Rather than ask for forgiveness from the locals, or even civility, Butler said: \xe2\x80\x9cI did what I did. I\xe2\x80\x99m cool with it. I\xe2\x80\x99m in a good place.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He has only one request for the basketball public: Pick someone else to win the East besides the up-and-down Sixers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t pick us,\xe2\x80\x9d Butler said. \xe2\x80\x9cI hope people say we\xe2\x80\x99re going to lose in the first round. I don\xe2\x80\x99t want anybody to think we\xe2\x80\x99re that good because I think it makes us play a little bit harder.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Marc Stein is a sports reporter specializing in N.B.A. coverage, with occasional forays into soccer and tennis. He spent nearly 15 years at ESPN before coming to The Times.  @TheSteinLine \xe2\x80\xa2 Facebook '

b'By Victor Mather'
b'Jim Boeheim, the longtime men\xe2\x80\x99s basketball coach at Syracuse, struck and killed a pedestrian on Wednesday night, the police said.'
b'A man had been involved in an earlier accident and had left his car on I-690 near Syracuse. Boeheim drove by later, striking the man, the police said.'
b'The victim was Jorge Jimenez, 51, of Syracuse. A police statement said Boeheim had tried to avoid the disabled car in the middle of the road and as a result had \xe2\x80\x9cstruck the victim who was standing on the side of the road.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A police statement said that neither driver was impaired by drugs or alcohol. It said Boeheim\xe2\x80\x99s speed had not been determined. While no tickets had been issued, an investigation was being conducted, it said.'
b'The area was under a weather advisory for snow and ice conditions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI am heartbroken that a member of our community died as the result of last night\xe2\x80\x99s accident,\xe2\x80\x9d Boeheim said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cJuli and I extend our deepest sympathies to the Jimenez family. Out of respect for those involved, I will not be providing further comment at this time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are saddened by the death of a member of our Central New York community,\xe2\x80\x9d said John Wildhack, the Syracuse athletic director. \xe2\x80\x9cCoach Boeheim is in contact with local authorities and cooperating fully.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Boeheim, 74, has been the coach at Syracuse since 1976, winning a national championship in 2003 and logging four other Final Four appearances over the years.'
b'Earlier in the evening, Syracuse (18-8) had beaten No. 18 Louisville, 69-49.'

b'By Marc Stein'
b'[Want to read more from Marc Stein? Sign up for his free, weekly N.B.A. newsletter by clicking here.]'
b'Four of the six best records in the N.B.A. belonged to Eastern Conference teams through Saturday night\xe2\x80\x99s play.'
b'The Golden State Warriors, meanwhile, reached the 41-game midpoint of the schedule on a pedestrian (for them) 54-win pace.'
b'The first half of the regular season, in other words, has defied most preseason prognostications and requires special examination to properly sort out the 1-to-30 landscape. So it is an ideal time to reconvene what is known as the Committee (of One) and share my team-by-team progress report in the form of N.B.A. Power Rankings.'
b'The Committee, as it has since the 2002-03 season, determines the order by weighing what is happening in the present alongside each team\xe2\x80\x99s big-picture outlook \xe2\x80\x94 with sprinkles of subjectivity and whimsy thrown in.'
b'What used to be a weekly endeavor for me is only a once-a-season enterprise every January now. Yet the goal, as always, is to provide a more up-to-date and detailed assessment than the standings do.'
b'(Records and statistics are current heading into Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s games.)'
b'1. Toronto Raptors (32-12)'
b'The Raptors were this season\xe2\x80\x99s first 30-win team, which is impressive when Kawhi Leonard and Kyle Lowry have been in uniform together only three times in Toronto\xe2\x80\x99s last 17 games. The threat of the Los Angeles Clippers signing Leonard away in free agency is all too real for every basketball-loving Canadian, but the Raptors may still assemble the best possible sales pitch: Win the post-LeBron James Eastern Conference to get to the N.B.A. finals and give Leonard ample reason to stay.'
b'2. Milwaukee Bucks (29-12)'
b'Giannis Antetokounmpo supplanting James Harden as the league\xe2\x80\x99s Most Valuable Player? Mike Budenholzer emerging from the usual deep field to win N.B.A. Coach of the Year? Milwaukee clinching the East\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1 seed heading into the playoffs? Any of those would have been fairly wild claims back in September, but suddenly they all seem possible halfway through the regular-season schedule. The challenge now: Milwaukee is just beginning the toughest two months of its schedule.'
b'3. Golden State Warriors (28-14) Maybe the Warriors do not inspire the fear they once did. Maybe their defensive woes (having slipped to 16th in defensive efficiency) are a sign of true vulnerability. Or maybe, with DeMarcus Cousins just days away from making his long-awaited debut, Golden State\xe2\x80\x99s season is about to start for real. I tend to believe it is the latter, in Year 5 of a historic run, having seen firsthand how much this team can struggle with regular-season motivation.'
b'[Read: DeMarcus Cousins Eyes Return as Warriors Prepare for 5-All-Star Lineup]'
b'4. Denver Nuggets (28-13)'
b'The regular season is just under 90 days old. The plucky Nuggets, despite numerous injuries, have held the top spot in the West \xe2\x80\x94 Golden State\xe2\x80\x99s conference \xe2\x80\x94 for 44 of them. Yet you would not know it given the limited attention these guys get, as N.B.A. know-it-alls wrestle with billing Denver as a full-fledged contender \xe2\x80\x94 or dismissing them as a team that can only do pre-April damage. Book this either way: Nikola Jokic is a lock to snag his first All-Star berth.'
b'5. Oklahoma City (26-16)'
b'Remember the Thunder\xe2\x80\x99s 0-4 start? Neither do we. Despite the season-long absence of the ace defender Andre Roberson, Oklahoma City leads the league in defensive rating (allowing just 102.9 points per 100 possessions) and specializes in the physical style that has troubled Golden State in the past. The Thunder have undoubtedly benefited from what ranks as the league\xe2\x80\x99s second-easiest schedule to date, but you would struggle to find a star duo meshing better than Russell Westbrook and Paul George.'
b'6. Houston Rockets (24-17)'
b'Earlier this season, I responded to the Rockets\xe2\x80\x99 disappointing start and Chris Paul\xe2\x80\x99s ongoing hamstring issues by stopping just short of proclaiming the window to contention closed for James Harden and Co. Houston is 7-2 since Dec. 24 \xe2\x80\x94 with Harden averaging a mere 41.0 points (and 16.7 3-point attempts!) per game in that stretch. Write the Rockets off if you wish, but Harden\xe2\x80\x99s brilliance, augmented by a resurgent Clint Capela and the newcomer Austin Rivers, should give you pause.'
b'7. Indiana Pacers (28-14)'
b'Surprise No. 1: Only six teams in the league, according to Basketball-Reference.com\xe2\x80\x99s projections, will finish the season with at least 50 wins. Surprise No. 2: Indiana is on that list, ahead of higher-profile teams like Philadelphia and Oklahoma City, despite the fact that the All-Star guard Victor Oladipo has missed 11 games with a knee problem. Coach Nate McMillan, continuity and a top-two defense have the unfashionable Pacers overachieving \xe2\x80\x94 again.'
b'8. San Antonio Spurs (25-19)'
b'This season\xe2\x80\x99s 11-14 start marked the first time Gregg Popovich has ever sported a sub-.500 record after 25 games and included a four-game stretch in which the Spurs unfathomably suffered three losses in excess of 30 points. The ensuing turnaround, though, has been no less remarkable. San Antonio is 14-5 and ranks No. 1 in offensive efficiency and No. 2 in defensive efficiency in that span, led by the midrange maestros DeMar DeRozan and LaMarcus Aldridge flat-out ignoring the league\xe2\x80\x99s 3-point revolution.'
b'9. Boston Celtics (25-17)'
b'The numbers continue to say that the Celtics are fine. They have a per-game average point differential (+6.4) that ranks second only to Milwaukee\xe2\x80\x99s (+9.1). Boston is also one of just four teams (along with Milwaukee, Toronto and Denver) to rank in the top 10 in both offensive (ninth) and defensive (fourth) efficiency. The problem: Boston just followed up an impressive rout of Indiana with losses in Miami and Orlando that suggested yet again that things are not fine.'
b'10. Philadelphia 76ers (27-16)'
b'For all the creative tension that has bubbled around the Sixers since they acquired Jimmy Butler on Nov. 10, they have the fourth-best overall record in that span (19-10) despite well-chronicled concerns about shooting and depth around Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s star trio as well as the occasional squawking. Butler\xe2\x80\x99s fit alongside Joel Embiid and Ben Simmons has been less than seamless, as predicted, but stockpiling as much talent as possible and then trying to solve the puzzle is the N.B.A. way.'
b'11. Utah Jazz (23-21)'
b'The Jazz have risen to a more familiar No. 5 in defensive efficiency and contend that their road-heavy schedule, with 25 of the first 41 games away, has contributed mightily to keeping them out of the West\xe2\x80\x99s top eight for much of the season. But to resemble the team most experts thought it would be, Utah needs Donovan Mitchell\xe2\x80\x99s January resurgence to last, as well as a return to last season\xe2\x80\x99s standards from Joe Ingles.'
b'12. Portland Trail Blazers (26-17)'
b'One of my faulty predictions from last year asserted that 2018 would be the year that the Trail Blazers finally broke up the Damian Lillard/C.J. McCollum partnership as a means to build a more balanced roster. Portland has instead clung to the hope that Jusuf Nurkic will keep inching closer to becoming the consistent third wheel it has needed for ages. It is a better team than last season\xe2\x80\x99s version but only marginally \xe2\x80\x94 and still vulnerable to athletic opposition.'
b'13. Los Angeles Lakers (23-20)'
b'Winning without LeBron James is hard. Who knew? The Lakers are 3-6 since James suffered a strained groin in a Christmas Day rout of Golden State. As a result, they have slid from a higher-than-expected No. 4 to an uncomfortable No. 8 in the West \xe2\x80\x94 thus resurrecting all the preseason questions about L.A.\xe2\x80\x99s ability to make the playoffs with, shall we say, such an eclectic roster. James appears likely, at 34, to miss more than the 11 games Stephen Curry lost to a similar injury in November.'
b'14. Los Angeles Clippers (24-18)'
b'I fear they are at high risk to slip out of the West\xe2\x80\x99s top eight, but the Clippers would certainly slot in right at the top of the play-hard rankings if there were such an industry. The feisty likes of Montrezl Harrell and Patrick Beverley, flanking a better-than-ever Tobias Harris, continue to make the Clippers more bizarrely competitive than anyone imagined heading into a summer in which they appear well positioned to make the loudest free-agent noise in franchise history.'
b'15. Sacramento Kings (22-21)'
b'A Bogdan Bogdanovic buzzer-beater to topple the Lakers on Dec. 27 hiked the fast-paced Kings\xe2\x80\x99 record to 19-16 and seemed to announce the blossoming tandem of De\xe2\x80\x99Aaron Fox and Buddy Hield as certifiable playoff material after a league-high 12 consecutive seasons of missing out. Sacramento then unraveled, enduring a 1-5 funk which included an embarrassing fall-from-ahead loss at Phoenix when the Suns were without Devin Booker. You cannot afford funks in the West.'
b'16. Miami Heat (21-20)'
b'Little emanating from South Beach makes sense, whether it is Miami\xe2\x80\x99s ability to play .500 basketball despite missing out on Butler via trade and having Goran Dragic healthy for just 14 games \xe2\x80\x94 or the fact this team is 0-3 against Atlanta. It is unclear how long it will take Miami to get back into the trade mix for a player of Butler\xe2\x80\x99s caliber, but the retiring Dwyane Wade should have an opportunity to bid the game farewell from the playoff stage.'
b'17. Brooklyn Nets (21-23)'
b'The drop-off from the East\xe2\x80\x99s top five to teams trying to secure the last three playoff stops is as steep as pessimists feared. Not that the Nets intend to apologize after the barren half-decade they endured in the wake of their disastrous 2014 trade with Boston. While the Knicks tank their way to a shot at Zion Williamson, New Yorkers may get postseason games after all, thanks to success stories like Spencer Dinwiddie, D\xe2\x80\x99Angelo Russell, Joe Harris and Jarrett Allen.'
b'18. New Orleans Pelicans (20-23)'
b'It is a misnomer to say Anthony Davis has no help; Jrue Holiday, Nikola Mirotic and Julius Randle are all accomplished players. The Pelicans\xe2\x80\x99 problems have been health (most notably injuries for Mirotic and the point guard Elfrid Payton) and difficulties in playing Davis, Mirotic and Randle together even when they are all available. New Orleans, as a result, is facing the biggest possible issue: Scenarios that force them to trade The Brow grow more plausible by the day.'
b'19. Washington Wizards (18-25)'
b'Indiana has crashed the East\xe2\x80\x99s upper crust to give the conference its own Fab Five, but we were not exaggerating the drop-off to the chasing pack. Look no further than the nation\xe2\x80\x99s capital for proof, with the Wizards still firmly in the playoff chase despite losing John Wall to season-ending heel surgery. Recent wins over Oklahoma City, Philadelphia and Milwaukee should tell you that the Wiz are not heeding some fans\xe2\x80\x99 calls to tank.'
b'20. Dallas Mavericks (20-22)'
b'Luka Doncic has a real shot to become the first rookie to achieve All-Star status since Blake Griffin in 2011, which already makes this a more successful season in Dallas than many forecast. But the huge disparity between the Mavericks\xe2\x80\x99 play at home (16-4) and on the road (4-18), Dirk Nowitzki\xe2\x80\x99s health woes in what they hoped would be a heartwarming final season and J.J. Barea\xe2\x80\x99s season-ending Achilles tear, have combined to snuff out some of the joy.'
b'[Read: The Mavericks\xe2\x80\x99 Key to Keeping Players Fresh? Blood Samples]'
b'21. Minnesota Timberwolves (21-22) As regular readers know, Glen Taylor\xe2\x80\x99s passive ownership style is a frequent source of consternation for the Committee. But give Taylor this: Firing Tom Thibodeau when he did to replace him with the 32-year-old Ryan Saunders, bizarre as the timing seemed, meant eating an estimated $20 million left on Thibodeau\xe2\x80\x99s contract. If only Taylor was that decisive back in June or July when the Wolves really needed to start dealing with Butler\xe2\x80\x99s discontent.'
b'22. Charlotte Hornets (19-23)'
b'The Michael Jordan-owned Hornets have All-Star Weekend hosting duties in a month to assure the franchise and city a measure of prominence this season. But what they, especially Jordan, really want is a playoff berth that is by no means certain given the limited scoring punch Charlotte can field beyond its do-everything guard Kemba Walker. It also does not help that the Hornets have already racked up a league-high eight costly losses in one-possession games.'
b'23. Detroit Pistons (18-23)'
b'Since it hit my radar during an early season visit to Motown, it has been one of my favorite stats of the season: Blake Griffin leads the league in touches per game at 93.3. Nikola Jokic and Harden are the only others in 90s, but the number doubles as an illustration of the Pistons\xe2\x80\x99 shortcomings as much as it spotlights Griffin\xe2\x80\x99s special ability as a power player to handle the ball like a guard. He is clearly compensating for multiple holes in the roster.'
b'24. Memphis Grizzlies (19-23)'
b'Memphis has nose-dived from a West-leading record of 12-5 on Thanksgiving, losing 18 of 25 games while the former All-Star center Marc Gasol has been submerged in a slump that has shown few signs of relenting. The fade may not only cost the Grizzlies a playoff berth but also threaten to extend Mike Conley\xe2\x80\x99s career-long wait for an All-Star berth, since team success is bound to be factored in to the votes of the media panel and coaches given the glut of worthy guards in the West.'
b'25. Orlando Magic (18-24)'
b'The Magic reeled off seven wins in a nine-game stretch in November under new coach Steve Clifford to spawn hopes that competing for a spot in the inviting lower reaches of the East\xe2\x80\x99s playoff ladder was feasible. Two months later, apart from the career-best season assembled by the veteran big man Nikola Vucevic, Orlando is back on course for a ninth successive trip to the lottery and remains as desperate as Phoenix for an upgrade at point guard.'
b'26. Atlanta Hawks (13-29)'
b'If the Hawks finish where they are as the so-called best of the worst, they will have a 10.5 percent shot at the No. 1 overall pick in June in the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s new lottery system, which flattens out the odds to 14 percent each for teams with the three-worst records. In the interim, Trae Young\xe2\x80\x99s development is the overwhelming focus, which makes it difficult not to partake in obsessing over how Young is shooting from the field (.394) and 3-point range (.291).'
b'27. Phoenix Suns (11-33)'
b'Deandre Ayton\xe2\x80\x99s Rookie of the Year campaign would appear to be the only pleasant diversion for one of the league\xe2\x80\x99s longest-suffering fan bases amid Phoenix\xe2\x80\x99s ninth straight non-playoff season, Booker\xe2\x80\x99s various health woes and the owner Robert Sarver\xe2\x80\x99s struggles to secure public financing for the renovation of the Suns\xe2\x80\x99 downtown arena. Yet I cannot say I love Ayton\xe2\x80\x99s chances after witnessing up close how badly he was outplayed by the R.O.Y. favorite Doncic last week.'
b'28. New York Knicks (10-32)'
b'Will the Knicks really hold Kristaps Porzingis out for the entire season? Will the Knicks trade Enes Kanter? Will the Knicks get lucky in the June draft? Those three questions have dominated Coach David Fizdale\xe2\x80\x99s first season in New York while this franchise waits for its opportunity in July to see if it can really make the long-awaited splash in free agency that many league observers legitimately expect after two mostly hapless decades.'
b'29. Chicago Bulls (10-33)'
b'Jim Boylen is still running some long practices, but things have mellowed (at least somewhat) between the Bulls and their feisty new coach after the initial wave of wind sprints, push-ups and disagreements. While Boylen works to secure a return next season, it is all about development for the rest of this season for the few keepers on the roster \xe2\x80\x94 most notably Lauri Markkanen, Zach LaVine and Wendell Carter Jr. \xe2\x80\x94 and finding new homes for Jabari Parker and Robin Lopez.'
b'30. Cleveland Cavaliers (8-35)'
b'In the four years between James\xe2\x80\x99s two stints with his home-state franchise, Cleveland somehow won the N.B.A. draft lottery three times: 2011 (Kyrie Irving), 2013 (Anthony Bennett) and 2014 (Andrew Wiggins). Dreams of getting lucky again and earning the right to select Zion Williamson may be the only source of comfort for Cavaliers fans to get through what surely must feel like the longest of winters watching such hopeless basketball.'

b'LOS ANGELES \xe2\x80\x94 At the end of a disastrous season in which the Los Angeles Lakers failed to make the playoffs, despite having added LeBron James via free agency, Magic Johnson made the stunning announcement on Tuesday that he was stepping down as the team\xe2\x80\x99s president of basketball operations.'
b'Johnson delivered the news at an impromptu news conference before the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 regular-season finale, against the Portland Trail Blazers, and he said he had not yet informed Jeanie Buss, the team\xe2\x80\x99s controlling owner. In fact, he had told nearly no one before he addressed a mass of hastily assembled reporters.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI couldn\xe2\x80\x99t face her to tell her,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, referring to Buss. He later added that he would find her at Staples Center to address her in person.'
b'Earvin, I loved working side by side with you. You\xe2\x80\x99ve brought us a long way. We will continue the journey. We love you \xf0\x9f\x92\x9c\xf0\x9f\x92\x9b https://t.co/ofmQl6BtBz'
b'Later, the team released a statement, calling Johnson \xe2\x80\x9cnot only a Lakers icon, but our family.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'[Magic Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s biggest moments running the Lakers.]'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is no greater Los Angeles Laker than Earvin Johnson,\xe2\x80\x9d the statement read, using Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s formal name. \xe2\x80\x9cWe are deeply grateful to Magic for all that he has done for our franchise \xe2\x80\x94 as a player, an ambassador and an executive.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The statement continued, \xe2\x80\x9cAs we begin the process of moving forward, we will work in a measured and methodical fashion to make the right moves for the future of our organization.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMeasured\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cmethodical\xe2\x80\x9d would be an about-face from the way Johnson stepped down. It was a surreal scene as he fielded questions for nearly 45 minutes after he made his announcement, appearing to hold back tears at times, and repeatedly said that he loved Buss like a sister. He then posed for pictures with team employees, former teammates and a local news anchor.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI want to go back to having fun,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson, 59, said. \xe2\x80\x9cI want to go back to being who I was before taking on this job, and we\xe2\x80\x99re halfway there with LeBron coming. I think this summer, with that other star coming in \xe2\x80\x94 whoever\xe2\x80\x99s going to come in \xe2\x80\x94 I think this team is going to be in position to really contend for a championship with the growth of the other young players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson was named to the post in February 2017 and said at the time that it was \xe2\x80\x9ca dream come true.\xe2\x80\x9d But on Tuesday he said that he wanted to get back to being a mentor and a businessman, and that he had felt limited in his ability to do those things in his current role.'
b'For example, he said he was upset that he could not attend Dwyane Wade\xe2\x80\x99s final game for the Miami Heat on Tuesday night \xe2\x80\x94 or congratulate Russell Westbrook of the Oklahoma City Thunder on Twitter for finishing the regular season averaging another triple-double. (Johnson said the league would have considered it \xe2\x80\x9ctampering.\xe2\x80\x9d)'
b'Johnson also said that he had received a phone call last week from the tennis star Serena Williams, asking if he would be an adviser to her.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen Serena called me, wow, that\xe2\x80\x99s who I am,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said. \xe2\x80\x9cI love helping people.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added: \xe2\x80\x9cI like to be free. And then I got a great life outside of this. What am I doing? I got a beautiful life, so I\xe2\x80\x99m going to go back to that beautiful life, and I\xe2\x80\x99m looking forward to it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But there is palace intrigue at play, too \xe2\x80\x94 these are the Lakers, after all \xe2\x80\x94 and Johnson strongly indicated that he had been leaning toward firing Coach Luke Walton. Buss, though, is known to think highly of Walton, a former Laker who has been the team\xe2\x80\x99s coach for three seasons, and Johnson suggested that he did not want to go through with it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI would have to affect someone\xe2\x80\x99s livelihood and their life,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said, \xe2\x80\x9cand I thought about that. That\xe2\x80\x99s not fun for me. That\xe2\x80\x99s not who I am, and then I don\xe2\x80\x99t want to put her in the middle of us, even though she said, \xe2\x80\x98Hey, do what you want to do.\xe2\x80\x99 I know she has great love for him.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Lakers, who have been downtrodden in recent years, are still one of the most glamorous franchises in the league, and Johnson, who helped the Lakers win five championships as a Hall of Fame point guard, remains one of the organization\xe2\x80\x99s most popular figures.'
b'Johnson was hired to replace Jim Buss, the brother of Jeanie Buss. (Johnson said that he had not told Pelinka of his decision to step down, either.)'
b'While Johnson had some memorable moments at the helm of the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 operation, the roster that he and Pelinka built around James was widely considered inadequate. b'James\xe2\x80\x99s first season with the Lakers has been disappointing, but passing his idol in career scoring goes beyond winning and losing.'
b'By Benjamin Hoffman'
b'There was no Instagram post celebrating the achievement in advance this time. There was relatively little buildup from the news media. It was an event that might have dominated the news cycle in years\xe2\x80\x99 past, but when LeBron James passed Michael Jordan on the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s career scoring list on Wednesday night, it was a triumph that somehow had been reduced to a footnote.'
b'James came into the Los Angeles Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 game against the Denver Nuggets needing 13 points to surpass Jordan for fourth place on the career list. With 5 minutes 38 seconds remaining in the second quarter, he managed to force his way to the basket for a layup, giving him 14 points for the game and 32,294 for his career. For good measure, he was fouled on the play. '
b'After a short stoppage to acknowledge the moment, play resumed as the Lakers, clinging to the last shreds of their playoff hopes, tried their best to overcome a huge early deficit at home against a heavily favored opponent.'
b'LeBron passes Michael Jordan on all-time scoring list pic.twitter.com/G2tAovqMrz'
b'The Lakers, led by an unlikely group of bench players, did make a run at Denver, reducing a 17-point deficit at halftime to 2 points with 8:37 left in the fourth quarter. But the Nuggets regained their footing and ran away with a 115-99 victory, spoiling a night in which James contributed 31 points, 7 rebounds and 7 assists, looking far more energized on both ends of the court than he had in recent weeks, and finishing the night with his career point total up to 32,311. '
b'James, who has taken the brunt of the criticism for the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 failings in a difficult first year in Los Angeles, had acknowledged the pending accomplishment in a tweet shortly before the game, but was measured when discussing it with reporters earlier in the day.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI take all accomplishments as they come,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cAny time I\xe2\x80\x99m in the breath with any other greats \xe2\x80\x94 and obviously M.J. being the guy that I looked up to my whole life, the guy I admired as a kid \xe2\x80\x94 I think it\xe2\x80\x99s going to be pretty cool.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Jordan, who owns the Charlotte Hornets, issued a brief statement on Thursday, saying, \xe2\x80\x9cI want to congratulate LeBron on achieving another great milestone during his amazing career.\xe2\x80\x9d The statement was notable mostly for being far more succinct than the one he issued when Kobe Bryant passed him on the career scoring list in 2014.'
b'One would hardly have guessed from either man\xe2\x80\x99s words that the greatest current basketball player had just surpassed his idol in their sport\xe2\x80\x99s signature statistic. The inability for James to truly celebrate the moment was yet another indignity in a season full of them.'
b'It was a little more than a year ago when James had seemingly settled into a groove. He scored his 30,000th point \xe2\x80\x94 a feat he congratulated himself about on Instagram hours before he actually accomplished it. With that hurdle cleared, and with recent championship runs in Miami and Cleveland under his belt, his march toward challenging Jordan, then Bryant, then Karl Malone and maybe even Kareem Abdul-Jabbar, the N.B.A.\xe2\x80\x99s career scoring leader, seemed as if it would come without the criticism that had followed him earlier in his career.'
b'A decision \xe2\x80\x94 a loaded word when it comes to James \xe2\x80\x94 to move to an ill-prepared Lakers team in the off-season has changed the calculus altogether. The team was predicted by most to struggle to make the playoffs in the West thanks to its collection of too-young players and veterans who do not complement James. Nevertheless, many have labeled the year a disappointment by virtue of the team\xe2\x80\x99s struggles despite having James, a player whose presence has seemingly guaranteed a finals appearance for close to a decade.'
b'As a result, James and the people around him have not been able to take much joy in his accomplishments. Just last week he passed Andre Miller to move into 10th place in career assists, thus making him the only player currently in the top 10 in both career points and assists. That feat \xe2\x80\x94 it had been temporarily attained by only a handful of other players going back to the days of Bob Cousy \xe2\x80\x94 was met with a collective shrug.'
b'It is a reality of James\xe2\x80\x99s life that he acknowledged on Wednesday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t really appreciated anything I\xe2\x80\x99ve been able to accomplish because I\xe2\x80\x99m so engulfed in what\xe2\x80\x99s next,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHow I can continue to get better; how I can help this franchise get back to where it needs to be.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'An occasional season of missing the playoffs is not unusual for most players \xe2\x80\x94 even the great ones \xe2\x80\x94 but to capture how truly rare it would be for a James-led team, consider that he has played double-digit playoff games in each of the last 13 years. He has appeared in nine N.B.A. finals \xe2\x80\x94 winning three \xe2\x80\x94 and as a result his career rankings among playoff performers come off as outrageous, even for someone as accomplished as James. '
b'Those rankings almost certainly will not improve this year. But among the more interesting aspects of James\xe2\x80\x99s current predicament is the opinion among many Lakers fans that the team\xe2\x80\x99s struggles have resulted in James\xe2\x80\x99s failing to live up to Bryant\xe2\x80\x99s legacy. Those criticisms ignore the fact that the Lakers\xe2\x80\x99 current six-year run of missing the playoffs included three seasons in which Bryant was still with the team. '
b'In fact, when Bryant passed Jordan on the career scoring list in 2014 \xe2\x80\x94 a feat considered a big enough deal at the time that a road game in Minnesota was stopped for several minutes so the crowd could give him a standing ovation and the Timberwolves\xe2\x80\x99 owner could present him with the game ball \xe2\x80\x94 the Lakers were only 8-16 and, partially a result of a season-ending injury to Bryant later in the year, were on their way to a 21-61 record.'
b'But in one of the endless parallels between the careers of Jordan and James, players who will be debated long after both are gone, Jordan, who passed Wilt Chamberlain for No. 3 on the career scoring list in 2003, also found little joy in what should have been a huge accomplishment, largely because his Washington Wizards were a .500 team at the time. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe thing about stats is they define you when you\xe2\x80\x99re 10 or 20 years past the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Jordan said when asked to sum up his feelings on the accomplishment. \xe2\x80\x9cWhile you\xe2\x80\x99re playing, what matters is wins.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'James, who wears No. 23 because of Jordan, put a wristband on his forearm because of Jordan, learned to shoot fadeaways because of Jordan and pitches sneakers for Nike just like Jordan does, may want to heed that advice from Jordan in terms of coming back on his accomplishments later, even if they have to be put aside for now. '
b'The Lakers could never win another game and James, a player who still refuses to label himself a scorer, will always have more points than Jordan, the player who served as his inspiration on a path to greatness. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI gotta carry it on to the next kid,\xe2\x80\x9d James said after the game, finally letting his emotion truly show. \xe2\x80\x9cHopefully I can inspire the next kid like myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'No Chris Paul. No Eric Gordon. No Clint Capela. No problem. The Houston Rockets still have James Harden.'
b'In a mind-boggling performance, Harden and his supporting cast \xe2\x80\x94 if you can call it that \xe2\x80\x94 managed to beat the Memphis Grizzlies by 112-94 at Houston\xe2\x80\x99s Toyota Center, with Harden scoring 57 points in 34 minutes.'
b'It was the 17th game in a row in which Harden scored at least 30 points \xe2\x80\x94 a feat previously accomplished in a single season by only Wilt Chamberlain \xe2\x80\x94 and it was Harden\xe2\x80\x99s third game of 50 or more points this season. No other player has more than one.'
